Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Ta'diyyah in Qiyas: Linguistic vs. Indication-Based Extension
Explains ta'diyyah concept and its application to pickpocket and grave robber

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ta'diyyah via wording (ibarah) and via indication (dalalah) and apply this distinction to evaluate whether a ruling extends to a new case in Hanafi qiyas.

Core Idea
Ta'diyyah by wording is stronger than by indication; the pickpocket is included by wording, the grave robber is not.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut delves into the Hanafi usul concept of ta'diyyah—the extension of a ruling from an original case to a branch via qiyas. The author critiques a common misunderstanding: that ta'diyyah always operates through textual indication (dalalah). He clarifies that when the meaning is fully present, the extension occurs through the very wording of the text (ibarah). This distinction has a direct impact on whether the hadd penalty applies to the pickpocket (tarrar) and the grave robber (nabbash).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of ta'diyyah
The text distinguishes between ta'diyyah via wording (ibarah) and via indication (dalalah). Understand that ta'diyyah via wording is direct and stronger, while via indication is weaker and depends on completeness of the effective cause (manat).
The phrase 'فلا وجه للدلالة' indicates that when wording suffices, indication is not needed.
2
Understand why the pickpocket is covered by wording
The pickpocket (tarrar) possesses the complete meaning of theft (taking secretly) and therefore falls under the Quranic term 'sariq' directly. The text says: 'أثبت هذا الإمام وجود مفهوم السرقة على الكمال وهذا يوجب تناول الصيغة عبارة'.
The term 'صيغة' refers to the Quranic verse on cutting the hand of the thief.
3
Understand why the grave robber is not covered by wording
The grave robber (nabbash) lacks the complete meaning of theft because the grave is not a secure place (hirz) and the shroud may not be of significant value. Hence, the name 'sariq' does not apply linguistically. The text says: 'لما لم يوجد فيه المعنى على الكمال قيوداته من الحرز وكون بجميع المأخوذ ذا خطر لم يتناوله اسم السارق'.
Even ta'diyyah via indication is weak due to missing manat.
4
Grasp the distinction between specific specialization and generic specialization
The text addresses an objection: pickpocket and grave robber are like species of a genus, so why treat them differently? The answer: 'الاختصاص الذي فيهما' is such that each is used in contrast to 'sariq', unlike species of a genus which are not opposed to the genus. This subtlety resolves the doubt.
This is a key logical distinction in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the principle to the nabbash ruling
Since the grave robber is not called 'sariq' linguistically, the hadd penalty does not apply. This is the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad), supported by companion consensus.
The ruling is stated at the end: 'عدم وجوب الحد على النباش عند الإمام أبي حنيفة و الإمام محمد'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول الكتاب ما هو المتبادر، وهو اطراد حكم الأصل في الفرع بالقياس، بل أراد بالتعدية اطراد الحكم بالدلالة، فإن ثبوت الحكم في الطرار بالدلالة ولا تستقيم هذه الدلالة في النباش لضعف المناط، وتبعه صاحب «التحرير»، وليس الأمر كما ظنه هذا الحبر، فإنه قد أثبت هذا الإمام وجود مفهوم السرقة في الطرار على الكمال وهذا يوجب تناول الصيغة عبارة، فلا وجه للدلالة، مع أن ضعف المناط أيضاً لا يوجب انتفاء الدلالة في النباش، بل الحق أن مراد هذا الإمام بالتعدية المعنى اللغوي، وهو اطراد الحكم ومقصوده أنه لما وجد الأخذ خفية في الطرار على الكمال اطرد حكم السارق وتعدى إليه وثبت فيه عبارة وهذا في غاية الحسن والاستقامة، وأما النباش فلما لم يوجد فيه المعنى على الكمال قيوداته من الحرز وكون بجميع المأخوذ ذا خطر لم يتناوله اسم السارق، فالتعدية أي سراية الحكم إليه في غاية الضعف، بعدم دلالة العبارة ; وهل هذا إلا كما تعدى حكم الإنسان في الفرس لوجود الحيوانية، فافهم والجواب عن الأول : أنه فرق بين الاختصاص الذي فيهما واختصاص أنواع جنس واحد، فإن الاختصاص فيهما بحيث يطلق كل منهما في مقابلة السارق حتى يقال : هذا طرار وهذا سارق أو نباش، فعلم بالتأمل أن معنى المثال المضروب أنه ليس سارقاً ضعيفاً، بل قوياً، وأنه من أفراده، بخلاف أنواع الجنس، فإنه لا يطلق في مقابلة الجنس أصلاً، والمورث للشبهة هو الاختصاص الأول دون هذا هذا غاية الكلام في هذا المقام احفظه فإنه دقيق (هذا) أي عدم وجوب الحد على النباش (عند الإمام أبي حنيفة و الإمام محمد، خلافاً لأبي يوسف والأئمة (الثلاثة مالك والشافعي وأحمد رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وهم ظنوا أن النباش داخل في عموم السارق، واعتبروا القبر حرزاً وقول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله قول ابن عباس) وفي «فتح القدير روى ابن أبي شيبة عن الزهري قال : أخذ نباش في زمن معاوية، وكان مروان على المدينة، فسأل من بحضرته من الصحابة والفقهاء، فاجتمع رأيهم على أن يضرب ويطاف به، وعلم من هذا أن غير ابن عباس أيضاً من الصحابة الكثيرين مذهبهم كمذهبنا (والثوري والأوزاعي ومكحول والزهري كلهم من التابعين وقولهم (مذهب أمير المؤمنين (عمر) رضوان الله تعالى عليه (و) عبد الله بن مسعود و أم المؤمنين (عائشة) رضوان الله تعالى عليهم (والحسن) من التابعين وأبي ثور) من تبع التابعين كذا) في التيسير
The first principle: the book: what is the apparent meaning? It is the extension of the ruling of the original to the branch by analogy, but he intended by 'ta'diyyah' the extension of the ruling by indication (dalalah). For the establishment of the ruling in the pickpocket is by indication, and this indication is not sound in the grave robber due to the weakness of the effective cause. The author of al-Tahrir followed him, but the matter is not as this scholar thought. For this imam has established the existence of the concept of theft in the pickpocket completely, and this necessitates that the expression includes it by wording, so there is no need for indication. Moreover, weakness of the effective cause does not necessitate the negation of indication in the grave robber. Rather, the truth is that this imam intended by 'ta'diyyah' the linguistic meaning, which is the extension of the ruling. His purpose is that when taking secretly was found completely in the pickpocket, the ruling of the thief extended and transferred to him and was established by wording. This is most excellent and straightforward. As for the grave robber, since the meaning was not found completely due to its restrictions of the secure place and that the taken thing is of significant value, the name of thief does not include him. So the ta'diyyah, i.e., the transmission of the ruling to him, is extremely weak due to the lack of textual indication. Is this not like the extension of the ruling of man to the horse due to the existence of animality? Understand. The answer to the first objection: that there is a difference between the specialization (ikhtisas) that exists in them and the specialization of types of a single genus. The specialization in them is such that each is used in contrast to the thief, so it is said: 'this is a pickpocket and this is a thief or a grave robber.' So it is understood by reflection that the meaning of the given example is that he is not a weak thief, but rather a strong one, and that he is from among his individuals, unlike the types of a genus, for they are not used in contrast to the genus at all. What causes doubt is the first specialization, not this. This is the end of the discussion on this point; memorize it, for it is precise. (This) i.e., the non-obligation of the hadd penalty on the grave robber (according to Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf and the three imams Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, may Allah be pleased with them. They thought that the grave robber is included in the general meaning of thief, and they considered the grave a secure place. The saying of Abu Hanifah is the saying of Ibn Abbas. In Fath al-Qadir: Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from al-Zuhri who said: 'A grave robber was caught in the time of Mu'awiyah, and Marwan was the governor of Madinah. He asked the companions and jurists present, and they agreed that he should be beaten and paraded.' From this it is known that other than Ibn Abbas from the many companions also held our school of thought. (Al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Makhul, al-Zuhri — all from the Tabi'in — and their saying is the school of the Commander of the Faithful Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and the Mother of the Believers Aishah, may Allah be pleased with them, and of al-Hasan from the Tabi'in, and of Abu Thawr from the followers of the Tabi'in. Thus in al-Taysir.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the application of the hadd penalty for theft to the grave robber (nabbash). The author begins by discussing the concept of ta'diyyah (transitivity) in qiyas. The point at issue is whether the ruling of the thief (sariq) extends to the pickpocket (tarrar) and the grave robber. The imam (likely Abu Hanifah) holds that the pickpocket fully meets the definition of theft (taking secretly) and is therefore included by the wording of the verse, not just by analogy. The grave robber, however, fails to meet the conditions of the theft definition (e.g., the taking is from a grave, which is not a secure place (hirz), and the grave clothes may not be of significant value). Hence, the ruling does not extend to him via wording, and qiyas is weak due to the missing effective cause. The author defends this view against critics, explaining that the difference between pickpocket/grave robber and species of a genus is significant. Then the passage states the ruling: the hadd is not obligatory on the grave robber according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf and the other three imams disagree. The passage provides evidence from the companions and tabi'in supporting the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
التعدية (al-ta'diyyah): The extension of a ruling from the original to the branch in qiyas; here interpreted as the linguistic meaning of transitivity.
النباش (al-nabbash): One who digs up graves to steal the burial shroud or items.
المناط (al-manat): The effective cause or ratio legis in qiyas; here, the set of attributes that trigger the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the pickpocket (tarrar) come under the Quranic ruling on theft via wording, while the grave robber (nabbash) does not?
A) Because the pickpocket is mentioned explicitly in the Quran
B) Because the pickpocket possesses the complete meaning of theft, while the grave robber lacks conditions like hirz and significant value
C) Because the grave robber is not a true thief by nature
D) Because the companions disagreed on the grave robber

Key Takeaway
Ta'diyyah in qiyas operates either by wording (when the complete meaning is present) or by indication (when the meaning is partial); the former is stronger and directly includes the branch.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Hadd Penalty for the Grave Robber (Nabbash): Hanafi Position and Ikhtilaf
States the Hanafi ruling on grave robber's hadd and presents evidence from companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the hadd penalty for grave robbery (nabbash), identify the opposing schools, and evaluate the evidence from companions.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school (except Abu Yusuf) does not apply the hadd penalty to the grave robber because the grave is not a secure place.

This passage presents the ikhtilaf (scholarly dispute) regarding whether the grave robber (nabbash) is subject to the hadd penalty of theft. The Hanafi position, held by Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, is that the hadd does not apply due to missing conditions. The opposing view includes Abu Yusuf, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad. The passage provides evidence from the practice of the companions and tabi'in supporting the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the nabbash
The text explicitly states: 'عدم وجوب الحد على النباش عند الإمام أبي حنيفة و الإمام محمد'. No hadd penalty is required for the grave robber.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their reasoning
The passage lists Abu Yusuf, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad as opponents. They considered the grave a secure place (hirz) and included the grave robber under the general term 'thief'.
Note: Abu Yusuf, though Hanafi, disagreed with the founding imams on this issue.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence from companions
The text quotes a report from Fath al-Qadir: When a grave robber was caught in the time of Mu'awiyah, the companions and jurists agreed on beating and parading, not cutting off the hand. This indicates that they did not consider the grave robber a thief for hadd.
Other companions like Ibn Abbas, Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, and Aishah are also cited.
4
Understand the key conditions for theft (sariq) in Hanafi fiqh
To be a sariq, the taking must be from a secure place (hirz) and the taken item must be of significant value (nisab). The grave is not hirz, and the shroud may not reach nisab.
This explains why the complete meaning of theft is absent.
5
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is whether the grave robber receives the hadd (amputation) or a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The Hanafi school (except Abu Yusuf) applies ta'zir only.
This is a clear example of how usul principles affect fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the application of the hadd penalty for theft to the grave robber (nabbash). The author begins by discussing the concept of ta'diyyah (transitivity) in qiyas. The point at issue is whether the ruling of the thief (sariq) extends to the pickpocket (tarrar) and the grave robber. The imam (likely Abu Hanifah) holds that the pickpocket fully meets the definition of theft (taking secretly) and is therefore included by the wording of the verse, not just by analogy. The grave robber, however, fails to meet the conditions of the theft definition (e.g., the taking is from a grave, which is not a secure place (hirz), and the grave clothes may not be of significant value). Hence, the ruling does not extend to him via wording, and qiyas is weak due to the missing effective cause. The author defends this view against critics, explaining that the difference between pickpocket/grave robber and species of a genus is significant. Then the passage states the ruling: the hadd is not obligatory on the grave robber according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf and the other three imams disagree. The passage provides evidence from the companions and tabi'in supporting the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
النباش (al-nabbash): One who digs up graves to steal the burial shroud or items.
الحرز (al-hirz): A secure place that protects property from theft; e.g., a locked house or shop.
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed penalty prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes, such as theft (amputation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the unanimous decision of the companions when a grave robber was captured in the time of Mu'awiyah?
A) They ordered the hand to be cut off
B) They ordered beating and parading
C) They referred the case to the caliph
D) They released him due to lack of evidence

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not apply the hadd of theft to the grave robber because the conditions of hirz and significant value are not met, and this is supported by companion practice.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Feeding One Poor for Sixty Days: A Hanafi Qiyas in Kaffarah
Defense of qiyas for feeding one poor for sixty days in kaffarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas method to derive the ruling that feeding one poor for sixty days suffices for kaffarah, and evaluate the objections raised against it.

Core Idea
The objective of kaffarah is to provide a specific quantity of food, not to feed a specific number of poor.

The verse on kaffarah for zihar (Quran 58:4) commands feeding sixty poor. The Hanafi school permits feeding one poor person for sixty days instead of sixty in one day. This lesson examines the qiyas (analogical deduction) used to justify this position, the objections from other schools, and the Hanafi responses. You will learn how the concept of manat (basis) and illah (effective cause) operate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Original Ruling (Asl) and Its Illah
The original ruling is feeding sixty poor in one day. The Hanafi identify the illah as providing the specific amount of food that suffices sixty poor for one day.
The illah is derived from the purpose of financial kaffarah: repelling need.
2
Identify the New Case (Far') and Shared Illah
The new case is feeding one poor for sixty days. The shared illah is the same total quantity of food.
The total food is identical: sixty days' worth for one person equates to one day's worth for sixty.
3
Assess Objections: Changing the Text and Virtue of Group
Opponents argue that the text literally specifies 'sixty poor' (siyyina miskinan) and that feeding a group has additional virtue (barakat al-jama'ah).
These objections claim the illah is not the quantum but the number of recipients or the blessing of congregation.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
Hanafis respond that this is qiyas, not tawil (interpretive redefinition) of the text. The mention of sixty poor is to indicate the measure (miqdar) of food required. The virtue of the group does not negate the primary illah of need fulfillment.
The author states that priority in the original does not prevent transference to the branch.
5
Determine the Applicability of Qiyas
The qiyas is valid because the manat (basis) is the quantum of food, and changing the text by ta'lil (reasoning) is permissible when the text itself indicates a measure.
The passage concludes that counting this as tawil is out of context.

ومنها قولهم في قوله تعالى في كفارة الظهار : ﴿فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِيِّينَ مِسْكِيناً ﴾ [المجادلة: ٤] (إطعام طعام ستين) مقولة للقول (إذ حاجة واحد في ستين) يوماً (كحاجة ستين مسكيناً والمقصود في الكفارة المالية دفع حاجة هذا المبلغ كما في سائر العبادات المالية فيجزىء إطعام مسكين واحد في ستين يوماً، كما يجزىء إطعام ستين مسكيناً في يوم، فالمقصود من الآية إطعام هذا القدر من الطعام ووجه البعد أن هذا صرف عن الظاهر من غير ملج، فإن ما ذكر لا يصلح مغيراً للنص (مع إمكان قصد إطعام الستين لفضل الجماعة وبركتهم وتضافر قلوبهم) يعني : مع أن هذا القياس غير صحيح في نفسه لوجود الفارق أو لمنع العلة مستنداً بأن بركة الجماعة ونشاط قلوبهم علة لكفارة الذنب أو شرط فيها، فلا يلزم كفاية الواحد في ستين يوماً (والحق) أن هذا ليس من التأويل، لأن لفظ ستين مسكيناً على معناه، بل أنه قياس للواحد في الستين من الأيام على الستين من المساكين (لظهور أن المناط دفع هذا المبلغ في الحاجات كما قررنا وما قالوا إن في الأصل فضل الجماعة فجوابه : أن غاية ما لزم منه كون المناط في الأصل أقوى ووجود الأولوية بوجه ما في الأصل لا يمنع التعدي) للحكم إلى الفرع كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى فذكر ستين مسكيناً لكون دفع حاجتهم معياراً للواجب وهو القدر الصالح لهذا كما الشاة، فعدّ هذا مر في التأويلات خروج عن المقام، ثم بقي ههنا إيرادان : الأول : أن فضل الجماعة عندهم مناط للحكم وعلة ،له وليس دفع الحاجات علة عندهم كما قررنا فلا يتوجه الجواب بعدم منع الأولوية القياس : والثاني : أن ظاهر الآية وجوب إطعام ستين مسكيناً، وهذا التعليل مغير له ، وسيجيء في بحث القياس أن تغيير النص لا سيما نص الأصل مما لا يجوز بالتعليل، وإن قيل بالتأويل بإرادة ستين مسكيناً حقيقة أو حكماً، فهو إذن من المقام لأنه من غير دليل فتأمل (ومنها حمل قوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم أيما امرأة نكحت نفسها من غير إذن وليها

So the purpose of the verse is to feed this amount of food. (The truth) is that this is not tawil, because the wording of sixty poor is upon its meaning; rather it is a qiyas of one for sixty days upon sixty poor (because it is apparent that the manat is to fulfill this amount of needs as we explained, and what they said that there is virtue of the group in the original is answered: the utmost that follows from it is that the manat in the original is stronger and the existence of preference in some way in the original does not prevent the transference) of the ruling to the branch, as will come by Allah's will. So the mention of sixty poor is because fulfilling their need is a measure for the obligatory, which is the suitable amount for this, like the sheep. So counting this among tawilat is leaving the context. Then there remain two objections here: First: that the virtue of the group for them is the manat of the ruling and the 'illa for it, not fulfilling needs as we established, so the answer that the priority does not prevent qiyas does not address it. Second: that the apparent meaning of the verse is the obligation of feeding sixty poor, and this ta'lil changes it, and it will come in the discussion of qiyas that changing the text, especially the text of the original, is not permissible by ta'lil. And if it is said by tawil intending sixty poor actually or virtually, then it is from the context because it is without evidence. Ponder it. (And among them is interpretation of the Prophet's saying: Any woman who marries herself without her guardian...

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi interpretation of the kaffarah for zihar (Quran 58:4). The issue is whether feeding one poor person for sixty days is equivalent to feeding sixty poor persons in one day. The Hanafi position, presented here, holds that the objective of kaffarah is to provide a specific amount of food (the sustenance of sixty poor for one day). Therefore, feeding one poor for sixty days suffices, as the total food quantity is the same. Opponents argue that this violates the apparent meaning of the text which specifies sixty poor (siyyina miskinan). They also argue that there is a virtue in feeding a group (barakat al-jama'ah). The author defends the Hanafi view by stating that this is not a tawil (interpretation) that changes the wording, but rather a qiyas that extends the ruling from feeding sixty in one day to feeding one over sixty days, based on the common illa of fulfilling a specific quantum of need. The author then notes two objections: first, that the opponents consider the virtue of the group as the illa, not the need fulfillment; and second, that the apparent text indicates feeding sixty poor, and the ta'lil changes it, which is impermissible. The author counters that the manat (basis) is the quantum of food, and that priority in the original does not prevent qiyas. The passage ends with a mention of another issue about a woman marrying without a guardian, but it is cut off.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyās): Analogical deduction extending the ruling from feeding sixty poor in one day to feeding one poor for sixty days based on the common illah of providing a specific amount of food.
مناط (manāṭ): The basis or criterion for the ruling; here it is the amount of food that fulfills need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the Hanafis allow feeding one poor for sixty days in kaffarah?
A) The verse is abrogated by a later hadith.
B) The word 'sixty poor' is interpreted as a measure of food quantity.
C) Feeding one poor for sixty days is easier for the wealthy.
D) The kaffarah rules were relaxed for later generations.

Key Takeaway
Feeding one poor for sixty days suffices for kaffarah because the illah is the quantum of food, not the number of recipients.

The Sheep in Zakat: Literal Animal or Monetary Value?
Analyzing the hadith of zakat sheep and the role of ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles to analyse whether the obligation in a zakat hadith is literal or value-based, and explain the role of ta'lil in extending the ruling.

Core Idea
The sheep in zakat is a measure: the obligation is the value that fulfills the need, not the animal itself.

In this lesson, we examine a key usul debate: does the hadith obligating a sheep in zakat mean a literal animal or its monetary value? The Hanafi school, using the principle of ta'lil (causation), holds that the sheep is a measure for the value needed to meet the poor's need. This analysis shows how usul al-fiqh extends rulings via illah. We will follow the author's reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possibilities for 'shah'
Recognize the three interpretations: (1) sheep is a metaphor for value, (2) literal sheep, (3) literal sheep but substitution allowed. Understand the implications for ta'lil and abrogation.
The author discusses these options at the outset.
2
Examine the argument against abrogation (naskh)
The author argues that if the sheep were metaphorical, the hadith would be abrogated by other evidence. But since scholars have used this hadith, abrogation is rejected. This preserves the hadith's authority for ta'lil.
Abrogation would prevent ta'lil on the basis that a mansukh text cannot have an illah.
3
Understand the author's preferred view
The author concludes that the sheep is literal (haqiqah), but substitution (istibdal) is permissible based on other proofs. The illah is 'daf' al-hajah' (fulfilling the need). Thus the wajib is the value that suffices the need, and the sheep is mentioned as a standard measure.
This aligns with Hanafi: the obligation is the monetary value, not the animal.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule of ta'lil
The benefit of ta'lil is twofold: (a) to extend the ruling to similar cases (e.g., other livestock) based on the illah of monetary value, and (b) to specify the wajib. Note that the explicit illah (al-illah al-mansusah) does not require extension, but it still serves to define the wajib.
The author cites the hadith of Mu'adh to reinforce the illah.
5
Contrast with opposing views and reflect
Consider why some might insist on a literal sheep. The author responds that substitution is proven by other evidence, and ta'lil is still valid. This demonstrates how Hanafi usul balances textual command with reasoned extension.
The passage also hints at istihsan as a basis for substitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الأول الكتاب القياس وفصله مطلع الأسرار الإلهية أن المراد في الحديث إما إيجاب الشاة بصورتها أو ماليتها، فإما أن تكون الشاة مجازاً عن المالية أو على الحقيقة، ويكون ذكرها التقدير الواجب وعلى الأول يلزم انتساخ هذا الحديث بهذه الإشارة أو بأثر معاذ أو بما روي في كتاب الخليفة الحق الصديق الأكبر رضي الله تعالى عنه، فلا تعليله كما سيجيء أن تعليل المنسوخ لا يجوز، وأيضاً إن يصح العلماء سلفاً وخلفاً استدلوا بهذا الحديث فلا نسخ، وعلى الأخيرين فلا فائدة في التعليل بل لا يصح، والذي يظهر لهذا العبد في التفصي عنه أن الشاة على الحقيقة، وقد علم جواز الاستبدال بهذه الإشارة بالحجج السابقة، فعلم أن الحكم معلل بدفع الحاجة ليظهر أن الواجب ما يكفي لدفع الحاجة، وهو مالية الشاة، مثلاً، وذكرها لتكون معيار المعرفة الواجب، ففائدة التعليل تعدية الحكم إلى نظائرها في المالية ولتعيين الواجب لا جواز الاستبدال فقط الذي يفيده هذه الإشارة وغيرها من الحجج، ولو تنزلنا قلنا : قد علم من حديث معاذ أن المقصود دفع الحاجة، فإنه قال : ذلك خير لأصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم والعلة المنصوصة لا يجب فيها التعدية فافهم
The first principle of the book is qiyas, and its section: the beginning of divine secrets: that the intended meaning in the hadith is either the obligation of the sheep by its form or by its monetary value. So either the sheep is a metaphor for monetary value or it is literal, and its mention is the estimation of the obligatory. On the first possibility, it would necessitate the abrogation of this hadith by this indication or by the narration of Mu'adh or by what was reported in the book of the truthful caliph, the great al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him). So its ta'lil is not permissible, as it will come that ta'lil of the abrogated is not allowed. Also, scholars past and present have used this hadith as evidence, so there is no abrogation. On the latter two possibilities, there is no benefit in ta'lil; rather it is invalid. What appears to this servant in response is that the sheep is literal, and the permissibility of substitution by this indication is known from previous proofs. Thus it is known that the ruling is ta'lil with fulfilling the need, to show that the obligatory is what suffices for the need, which is the monetary value of the sheep, for example, and its mention is to be a measure for knowing the obligatory. So the benefit of ta'lil is to extend the ruling to its counterparts in monetary value and to specify the obligatory, not just the permissibility of substitution, which is indicated by this indication and other proofs. And if we concede, we say: it is known from the hadith of Mu'adh that the purpose is fulfilling the need, for he said: 'That is better for the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family).' And the explicit cause does not require extension, so understand.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith concerning zakat on sheep. The author, commenting on the first principle of qiyas, examines a key usul issue: whether the obligation of a sheep in zakat is literal (an animal) or rather its monetary value. He considers three possibilities: (1) the sheep is a metaphor for value, (2) it is literal, or (3) the sheep is literal but substitution is permitted. He argues that the ruling is grounded in the cause (illah) of fulfilling the need (daf' al-hajah), so the obligatory is whatever suffices that need—namely, the monetary value. Thus the mention of a sheep serves as a standard measure. This analysis is Hanafi: the obligation is not tied to the specific animal but to its value, allowing substitution by cash or equivalent. The author also refutes claims of abrogation (naskh) by noting that scholars have consistently used this hadith. The passage illustrates how Hanafi usul uses ta'lil to extend rulings to similar cases.

Key Terms
الشاة (al-shah): The sheep mentioned in the zakat hadith, discussed as either literal animal or as a standard for monetary value.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): The process of identifying the cause (illah) for a ruling, here the need (hajah).
المنسوخ (al-mansukh): An abrogated legal ruling; a mansukh text cannot be used as basis for ta'lil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude is the obligatory in zakat according to the hadith?
A) The literal sheep itself
B) The monetary value of the sheep
C) Either a sheep or its value at the giver's choice
D) Nothing, as the hadith is abrogated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the obligation in zakat on sheep is the monetary value sufficient for the needy, and the mention of sheep is a measure, not the object itself.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas vs. Nass: Feeding Sixty Poor in Kaffarah
Critique of qiyas in kaffarah al-zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a proposed qiyas against a sacred text by applying the Hanafi principle that explicit nass cannot be overridden by analogy.

Core Idea
Qiyas cannot override the explicit nass of the Quran, even if the underlying need is the same.

Some scholars argued that feeding one poor for sixty days fulfills the requirement of feeding sixty poor in kaffarah al-zihar, based on the idea that the goal is to meet need. This lesson examines why the Hanafi school rejects this qiyas, emphasizing the binding nature of the literal text and the principle that qiyas cannot change an explicit nass.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Proposed Qiyas
Recognize the analogy: feeding one poor for sixty days is equated to feeding sixty poor in one day, based on the illah of fulfilling need.
The illah is the same total amount of food and the goal of satisfying hunger.
2
State the Hanafi Objection
The Hanafi position is that the qiyas is invalid because it deviates from the apparent meaning of the verse without a compelling reason.
The verse explicitly says 'sixty poor people', not 'sixty meals'.
3
Understand the Principle: Qiyas Cannot Override Nass
In Hanafi usul, an explicit text (nass) is qat'i (certain) in its dalalah; qiyas, being zanni, cannot change it.
This is a foundational rule: al-amm yufidu al-wujub and qiyas cannot specify or restrict it.
4
Recognize the Differentiating Factor
The text mentions 'sixty poor' not just for the amount but also for the virtue of group feeding (barakah, collective worship). This additional element prevents the qiyas from being valid.
The illah in the original includes a social/spiritual dimension, not just physical need.
5
Apply the Principle to Similar Cases
Consider other financial expiations or zakat where the explicit text specifies recipients; analogy based solely on need is insufficient if the text includes additional conditions.
Always check if the nass has a broader purpose that cannot be captured by a simplified illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها قولهم في قوله تعالى في كفارة الظهار : ﴿فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِيِّينَ مِسْكِيناً ﴾ [المجادلة: ٤] (إطعام طعام ستين) مقولة للقول (إذ حاجة واحد في ستين) يوماً (كحاجة ستين مسكيناً والمقصود في الكفارة المالية دفع حاجة هذا المبلغ كما في سائر العبادات المالية فيجزىء إطعام مسكين واحد في ستين يوماً، كما يجزىء إطعام ستين مسكيناً في يوم، فالمقصود من الآية إطعام هذا القدر من الطعام ووجه البعد أن هذا صرف عن الظاهر من غير ملج، فإن ما ذكر لا يصلح مغيراً للنص (مع إمكان قصد إطعام الستين لفضل الجماعة وبركتهم وتضافر قلوبهم) يعني : مع أن هذا القياس غير صحيح في نفسه لوجود الفارق أو لمنع العلة مستنداً بأن بركة الجماعة ونشاط قلوبهم علة لكفارة الذنب أو شرط فيها، فلا يلزم كفاية الواحد في ستين يوماً (والحق) أن هذا ليس من التأويل، لأن لفظ ستين مسكيناً على معناه، بل أنه قياس للواحد في الستين من الأيام على الستين من المساكين (لظهور أن المناط دفع هذا المبلغ في الحاجات كما قررنا وما قالوا إن في الأصل فضل الجماعة فجوابه : أن غاية ما لزم منه كون المناط في الأصل أقوى ووجود الأولوية بوجه ما في الأصل لا يمنع التعدي) للحكم إلى الفرع كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى فذكر ستين مسكيناً لكون دفع حاجتهم معياراً للواجب وهو القدر الصالح لهذا كما الشاة، فعدّ هذا مر في التأويلات خروج عن المقام، ثم بقي ههنا إيرادان : الأول : أن فضل الجماعة عندهم مناط للحكم وعلة له وليس دفع الحاجات علة عندهم كما قررنا فلا يتوجه الجواب بعدم منع الأولوية القياس : : والثاني : أن ظاهر الآية وجوب إطعام ستين مسكيناً، وهذا التعليل مغير له، وسيجيء في بحث القياس أن تغيير النص لا سيما نص الأصل مما لا يجوز بالتعليل، وإن قيل بالتأويل بإرادة ستين مسكيناً حقيقة أو حكماً، فهو إذن من المقام لأنه من غير دليل فتأمل
And among them is their saying regarding the word of Allah in the expiation of zihar: {And if he cannot, then feeding of sixty poor people} [Q. 58:4]. (Feeding food of sixty) is attributed to the saying (since the need of one person in sixty days is like the need of sixty poor people). And the purpose in financial expiation is to fulfill the need of this amount, as in other financial acts of worship. So it suffices to feed one poor for sixty days, just as it suffices to feed sixty poor in one day. So the purpose of the verse is to feed this amount of food. The aspect of distance is that this is a diversion from the apparent meaning without compulsion, for what is mentioned does not serve as a changer of the text (with the possibility of intending to feed the sixty for the virtue of the group and their blessing and the uniting of their hearts). That is, although this analogy is itself invalid due to the existence of a difference or because the cause is prevented, based on the fact that the blessing of the group and the activity of their hearts is a cause for the expiation of the sin or a condition in it. So it does not necessitate the sufficiency of one person for sixty days. (The truth) is that this is not from ta'wil, because the word 'sixty poor' is upon its meaning, rather it is a qiyas of one person in sixty days to sixty poor (because it is evident that the point of attachment is the payment of this amount for needs, as we have established. And what they said that in the original there is the virtue of the group, the response is: the utmost that follows from it is that the point of attachment in the original is stronger, and the existence of a kind of superiority in the original does not prevent the extension) of the ruling to the branch, as will come, Allah willing. So the mention of sixty poor is for the fact that meeting their need is a standard for the obligatory, which is the quantity suitable for this, like the sheep. Therefore, counting this among the far-fetched ta'wils is a departure from the topic. Then there remain two objections here: First, that the virtue of the group is, according to them, the point of attachment for the ruling and its cause, and not the meeting of needs as we have established, so the response of not preventing the superiority does not address the analogy. Second, that the apparent meaning of the verse is the obligation of feeding sixty poor, and this ta'lil changes it. It will come in the discussion of qiyas that changing the text, especially the text of the original, is not permissible through ta'lil. And if it is said that ta'wil intends sixty poor real or legally, then it is from the topic because it is without evidence. So reflect.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents a qiyas (analogy) proposed by some scholars regarding the kaffarah of zihar (the verse requiring feeding sixty poor). The analogy argues that feeding one poor person for sixty days is equivalent to feeding sixty poor in one day, based on the concept that the goal is to satisfy hunger. The author critiques this qiyas on multiple grounds: (1) it is a departure from the apparent meaning without a compelling reason; (2) the virtue of the group (blessing of feeding sixty together) may be a condition or cause for expiation; (3) even if the need is the cause, the existence of a stronger cause (group blessing) in the original prevents the analogy from extending to the branch. The author aligns with the Hanafi position that the literal text (sixty poor individuals) must be followed, and the qiyas is invalid because it changes the explicit text (nas) of the Quran, which is not permissible. This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that qiyas cannot override an explicit nass.

Key Terms
كفارة الظهار (kaffarat al-zihar): The expiation for zihar (a pre-Islamic divorce-like declaration), which includes feeding sixty poor.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning, here applied to compare feeding one poor for sixty days to feeding sixty poor in one day.
النص (al-nass): An explicit text (Quran or sunnah) with clear meaning; in Hanafi usul, nass is qat'i (certain) in its dalalah.
الظاهر (al-zahir): The apparent meaning of a text; it is binding unless there is evidence to depart from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the qiyas of feeding one poor for sixty days in kaffarah al-zihar?
A) Because the hadith explicitly forbid it.
B) Because feeding one person for sixty days is more expensive.
C) Because the qiyas changes the explicit text (nass) of the Quran without evidence.
D) Because the verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The explicit wording of the Quran specifying 'sixty poor' requires feeding sixty distinct individuals; any analogy that replaces this with one person over time is invalid because qiyas cannot override nass.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

6 min
Qiyas Cannot Abrogate Nor Be Abrogated
Statement of a usul rule with reasoning and critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that qiyas is neither a nasikh nor mansukh, explain the majority's reasoning, and evaluate the critique of that reasoning.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a divine proof, but only Allah abrogates; qiyas merely reveals the ruling.

In this usul lesson, we examine a foundational rule: analogical deduction (qiyas) does not have the power to abrogate any textual proof, nor can it itself be abrogated. This is the position of the majority (jumhur), including the Hanafi school. We will unpack the reasoning behind this rule and critically analyze the argument presented, preparing you to apply this principle when deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule's two aspects
The passage states that qiyas is neither a nasikh (abrogator) nor a mansukh (abrogated). Separate these two claims and note that the text only fully covers the first (non-nasikh).
The second aspect is mentioned but not elaborated; you may infer reasons logically.
2
Understand the majority's reasoning for non-nasikh
The text argues: the ummah has no authority to invalidate Allah's rulings, and abrogation is a legislative act of Allah. Qiyas is a method of discovering the ruling, not a source of legislation, so it cannot abrogate.
The key premise: no wilayah (authority) for the ummah over divine rulings.
3
Analyze the critique of this reasoning
The commentator raises a counterpoint: if qiyas is a proof from Allah, then its operation in 'raising' a ruling is actually Allah's action via that proof, not the ummah's. The critique questions whether the first reasoning is fully sound.
The text says 'Fihi nazar zahir' (there is apparent scrutiny). This is a critical assessment.
4
Synthesize the rule and its implications
Conclude that qiyas does not independently abrogate; any apparent conflict between a qiyas-based ruling and a textual ruling is resolved by preferring the text, as qiyas is subordinate.
This reinforces the hierarchy: nass > qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: القياس لا يكون ناسخاً لشيء من الأدلة ولا منسوخاً بها عند الجمهور خلافاً للبعض الغير المعتد بهم (أما الأول) وهو عدم ناسخيته (فلأنه لا ولاية للأمة على إبطال حكم من أحكام الله تعالى ولا مجال للرأي في إدراك مدد الأحكام (ولهذا) أي لأجل أن لا ولاية للأمة (لا يعلل النسخ حتى يتعدى في المسكوت لجامع، وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإنه سلمنا أن لا ولاية للأمة، لكن القياس حجة من حجج الله تعالى فرفعه لحكم ليس من باب ولاية الأمة، بل هو رفع من الله تعالى بإقامة دليل عليه ولا يلزم منه المجال للعقل في معرفة مدة الحكم، بل ظهورها بدلالة دليل شرعي غايته أن العقل عرفه ولا شناعة فيه فتأمل (وأما الثاني)
Issue: Qiyas does not abrogate any of the proofs nor is it abrogated by them according to the majority, contrary to some whose opinion is not considered. (As for the first), i.e., its not abrogating [is] because the ummah has no authority to invalidate any of Allah's rulings, and there is no scope for opinion in perceiving the durations of rulings. (For this reason), i.e., because the ummah has no authority, abrogation is not based on an illah such that it could extend to the unmentioned [cases] through a commonality [in the illah]. But there is apparent scrutiny: we concede that the ummah has no authority, but qiyas is a proof among Allah's proofs, so its raising of a ruling is not from the ummah's authority; rather it is a raising by Allah through establishing a proof for it, and it does not entail scope for the intellect in knowing the duration of the ruling; rather its manifestation is through the indication of a legal proof, the utmost of which is that the intellect recognizes it, and there is no impropriety in that. So ponder. (As for the second...)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a usul rule: qiyas (analogical deduction) cannot be a nasikh (abrogator) of any textual proof, nor can it be mansukh (abrogated) by them. This is the position of the majority of scholars, with only a few dissenting opinions. The reasoning given is that the ummah (the community) has no authority to invalidate a divine ruling; abrogation is solely the prerogative of the Lawgiver (Allah). Since qiyas is a method of deriving rulings—a proof (hujjah) from Allah—when it yields a ruling that seems to 'raise' (i.e., overturn) a previous ruling, it is not the ummah acting on its own, but rather the discovery of a proof that indicates the abrogation. However, the text contains a critique: if qiyas is a divine proof, then its operation in apparently abrogating a ruling is actually a manifestation of a proof, not an act of the ummah. But the rule remains that qiyas is not an independent source of abrogation; it is merely a tool for deriving rulings, and abrogation is tied to explicit texts (nusus) from Quran and sunnah. The passage ends incomplete, but it likely continues to discuss the second aspect: that qiyas cannot be abrogated, because abrogation applies to direct textual rulings, not to a method of inference.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a common effective cause ('illah).
الناسخ (al-nāsikh): The abrogating proof that removes a previous ruling.
المنسوخ (al-mansūkh): The earlier ruling that is abrogated.
الجمهور (al-jumhūr): The majority of scholars (of usul al-fiqh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is qiyas not considered a nasikh?
A) Because qiyas is not a proof (hujjah)
B) Because the ummah has no authority to abrogate divine rulings
C) Because qiyas is only used in muamalat (transactions)
D) Because qiyas can only be used by mujtahids

Key Takeaway
Qiyas neither abrogates nor is abrogated; it is a subordinate proof that discovers rulings, never overrides explicit divine texts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Qiyas Cannot Be Nasikh or Mansukh According to the Majority
Stating and proving the rule that qiyas cannot abrogate or be abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that qiyas cannot be nasikh or mansukh and explain the two main proofs (ummah's lack of authority and loss of preponderance) that support it.

Core Idea
Qiyas is too weak to abrogate a text; its own validity requires preponderance, which vanishes when a stronger proof appears.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul principle: whether analogical reasoning (qiyas) can abrogate or be abrogated. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that it cannot. The author, in his commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, presents the reasoning behind this position and addresses counterarguments. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly prioritizing proofs in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states the rule: qiyas cannot be a nasikh (abrogating) nor mansukh (abrogated) according to the majority.
2
Examine the first argument (no abrogation by qiyas)
The first reason: the ummah has no authority to invalidate Allah's rulings, and naskh is not based on opinion. The passage also critiques this argument, noting that qiyas is a divine proof, but the author insists it cannot initiate naskh.
The author acknowledges a 'clear consideration' but defends the rule.
3
Examine the second argument (qiyas cannot be abrogated)
The second reason: the condition for acting on qiyas is its preponderance; when a stronger proof appears, that preponderance is lost, so qiyas is no longer valid. It is not 'abrogated' in the technical sense.
This also implies qiyas cannot abrogate, as the condition for naskh (genuine conflict) is absent.
4
Analyze the counterarguments
The passage addresses objections: e.g., that qiyas is a proof like any other, and that qiyas could abrogate another qiyas. The author refutes these by clarifying that two qiyas do not truly conflict; rather, one is preferred (tarjih).
The father of the commentator adds that qiyas with inferred 'illa is too weak to cause any change.
5
Apply the distinction: inferred 'illa vs. textual 'illa
The passage ends by discussing qiyas with a textual 'illa (like mafhum al-muwafaqah). Ibn al-Hajib's view is cited: during the Prophet's ﷺ lifetime, such qiyas could abrogate, but after him it cannot. The author finds this distinction arbitrary.
The overall conclusion: qiyas does not have the strength to abrogate or be abrogated in the standard sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: القياس لا يكون ناسخاً) لشيء من الأدلة (ولا) منسوخاً) بها (عند الجمهور) خلافاً للبعض الغير المعتد بهم (أما الأول) وهو عدم ناسخيته (فلأنه لا ولاية للأمة) على إبطال حكم من أحكام الله تعالى (ولا مجال للرأي) في إدراك مدد الأحكام (ولهذا) أي لأجل أن لا ولاية للأمة (لا يعلل النسخ حتى يتعدى في المسكوت لجامع، وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإنه سلمنا أن لا ولاية للأمة، لكن القياس حجة من حجج الله تعالى فرفعه لحكم ليس من باب ولاية الأمة، بل هو رفع من الله تعالى بإقامة دليل عليه ولا يلزم منه المجال للعقل في معرفة مدة الحكم، بل ظهورها بدلالة دليل شرعي غايته أن العقل عرفه ولا شناعة فيه فتأمل (وأما الثاني) أن القياس لا يكون منسوخاً فلأن شرط العمل به ،رجحانه وقد زال بوجود المعارض) وهو الذي يتوهم ناسخاً، وإذا انتفى شرط العمل فلا حجية فيه فلا رفع به) وهذا لو تم لدل على المطلب الأول أيضاً وحاصله أنه لا بد للنسخ أن يكون الدليلان بحيث لو فرض اتحاد زمانهما كانا متعارضين والقياس يضمحل عند معارضة الدليل، فلا يصح منسوخاً من دليل ولا يرد أن كل نسخ لا بد فيه من معارضة وشرط العمل عدمها، فلا يصح نسخ أصلاً. وكذا لا یرد يجوز أن يكون القياس مرفوعاً بدليل معارض أو رافعاً له، فلا ينتفي شرط العمل لعدم بقاء المعارضة، ثم إنه بقي ههنا بحيث هو أنه لا نسلم اضمحلال القياس عند معارضة الدليل، بل القياس حجة شرعية كالدليل الآخر، فإذا لم يضمحل ويتقدم على الدليل الآخر يكون مرفوعاً منه وإن تأخر يكون رافعاً له على أنه يجوز أن يكون قياس متقدم الأصل منسوخاً بقياس متأخرة والقياس لا يضمحل في مقابلة القياس الآخر. قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره الأشبه أن القياس المستنبط العلة ظن العلة فيه ضعيف لكونها بالرأي ثم الحكم الثابت في الفرع بوجودها فيه أشد ضعفاً، فلا يبقى عند مقابلة نص دال على خلافه، فلا تتحقق المعارضة لو فرض اتحاد الزمان فلا ناسخية ولا منسوخية، أما عدم منسوخيته من قياس مثله وعدم ناسخيته له فلأن القياسين لا يتعارضان كما بين في بحث التعارض، بل يجب الترجيح وإن لم يتفق فللمجتهد أن يعمل بأيهما شاء، والنسخ فرع التعارض، وأما منصوص العلة فمثله مثل مفهوم الموافقة . انتهى كلماته الشريفة وهذا بناء على أن القياس المستنبط مرجوح عن النص، ولا يعتد به عند المقابلة، وهو في حيّز الخفاء، فإن العام المخصوص يجوز تخصيصه به عندنا وتخصيص العام مطلقاً عند الشافعية ومن الفطريات أن المرجوح لا يغيّر الراجح، وإذ قد صلح مغير النص فليصلح رافعاً لما ثبت به ويكون مرتفعاً مثله في الدلالة ولا محذور فيه أصلاً، وأما القياس عند مقابلة آخر مثله فهما أيضاً متعارضان لكون كل منهما منتجاً خلاف ما ينتجه الآخر وهو التعارض، وإنما لا يهدران لأنه ليس دليل دونهما حتى يصار إليه بل يصار إلى الترجيح وإن لم يوجد يحكم القلب لئلا يلزم العمل من غير دليل وأما إذا كان أحدهما متأخر الأصل فله ترجيح فيكون رافعاً لمقدم العلة وأما المنصوص العلة، فقد قال ابن الحاجب إنه يجوز نسخ القياس المقطوع للمقطوع في حياته صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وبعده صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله وأصحابه لا يجوز لأنه لا مجال للرأي. وأورد أن القياس لا يكون مقطوعاً وإن كانت العلة مقطوعة لجواز أن يكون الفرع مانعاً أو الأصل شرطاً. ولو فرض مقطوعاً لكان كالنص فينسخ وينسخ ولعله أراد به مقطوع العلة فلا ورود لما ذكر نعم يرد عليه أن الفرق تحكم فإن القياس في زمانه الشريف وبعده سواسيان في الحجية وإفادة الحكم فإذا علم الآن قياس على أصل ثم علم قياس آخر على أصل آخر متأخر عنه، ويكون هذا القياس معارضاً إياه يحكم بانتساخ الأول من الثاني لوجود دليلين مفيدين للحكمين، فيرفع المتأخر المقدم وليس هذا مجالاً للرأي المحض في نصب الأحكام، بل إنما هو نصب من الشارع دليلاً من عنده موجباً لانتهاء عمر الحكم، فإن العلة بنص
Issue: Qiyas cannot be a nasikh for any evidence nor mansukh by it according to the majority, contrary to some not considered reliable. As for the first (that it cannot be nasikh), it is because the ummah has no authority to invalidate a ruling from Allah's rulings, and there is no room for opinion in perceiving the durations of rulings. And for this reason (i.e., because the ummah has no authority), naskh is not attributed to a cause so that it extends to the unspoken due to a commonality. There is a clear consideration in this, for we grant that the ummah has no authority, but qiyas is a proof from Allah's proofs, so its raising of a ruling is not from the category of the ummah's authority, but rather it is a raising by Allah through establishing a proof for it, and it does not necessitate room for reason in knowing the duration of the ruling, but rather its appearance by the indication of a legal proof, the utmost of which is that reason knows it, and there is no disgrace in it. So reflect. As for the second (that qiyas cannot be mansukh), it is because the condition for acting upon it is its preponderance, and it has disappeared due to the existence of the opposing proof (which is imagined to be the nasikh). And if the condition for acting is absent, then there is no authority in it, so no raising occurs. If this were complete, it would also indicate the first point. The summary is that for naskh, the two proofs must be such that if their time were assumed to be the same, they would be in conflict, and qiyas collapses when opposed by a proof. So it cannot be mansukh by a proof. And it cannot be objected that every naskh necessarily involves opposition and the condition for acting is its absence, so no naskh would be valid at all. Similarly, it cannot be objected that it is permissible for qiyas to be raised by a conflicting proof or be a raiser of it, so the condition for acting is not negated because the opposition does not remain. Then there remains here a consideration: we do not concede the collapse of qiyas when opposed by a proof. Rather, qiyas is a legal proof like any other proof. If it does not collapse and precedes the other proof, then it is raised by it; if it comes later, it is a raiser of it. Moreover, it is permissible for an earlier qiyas to be abrogated by a later qiyas, and qiyas does not collapse in the face of another qiyas. The opener of divine secrets, my father (may his secret be sanctified) said: The more likely view is that qiyas based on inferred 'illa has a weak presumption of 'illa because it is by opinion, and then the ruling established in the branch by its existence is even weaker. So it does not remain when confronted by a text indicating otherwise; thus opposition would not be realized if their time were assumed to be the same, so there is no naskh or being abrogated. As for not being abrogated by a similar qiyas and not abrogating it, it is because two qiyas do not conflict, as established in the discussion of conflict. Rather, tarjih is necessary, and if agreement is not reached, the mujtahid may act by whichever he wishes. Naskh is a branch of conflict. As for qiyas with a textual 'illa, it is like the concept of verbal correspondence (mafhum al-muwafaqah). End of his noble words. This is based on the view that qiyas based on inferred 'illa is inferior to the text and is not considered when confronted. This is somewhat obscure, because a general text that has been specified may be further specified by it according to us, and specification of a general text is absolutely allowed by the Shafi'is. It is axiomatic that the inferior does not change the superior. But if it is capable of changing the text, then let it be capable of raising what is established by it, and it would be raised like it in indication, and there is no harm in it at all. As for qiyas when confronted by another like it, they are also conflicting because each produces a different result from the other, which is conflict. They are not discarded only because there is no proof below them to resort to; rather, resort is to tarjih. If tarjih is not found, the heart judges to avoid acting without evidence. But if one of them is later in origin, it has a weighting, so it raises the earlier one. As for qiyas with a textual 'illa, Ibn al-Hajib said: It is permissible for determined qiyas to abrogate determined qiyas during his lifetime (peace be upon him) but after him it is not allowed because there is no room for opinion. It was objected that qiyas cannot be determined even if the 'illa is determined because it is possible that the branch has a preventing factor or the original has a condition. If it were assumed determined, it would be like a text, so it would abrogate and be abrogated. Perhaps he meant determined in 'illa, so the objection does not apply. However, it can be objected that the distinction is arbitrary, because qiyas during his noble time and after it are equal in authority and in providing rulings. So if a qiyas based on an original is now known, then another qiyas based on another original later is known, and this qiyas conflicts with it, one judges the abrogation of the first by the second due to the existence of two proofs providing two rulings. The later raises the earlier, and this is not mere opinion in establishing rulings; rather it is the establishment by the Lawgiver of a proof from Him causing the expiry of the ruling's time. For the 'illa is by text.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul principle that analogical deduction (qiyas) cannot serve as an abrogating proof (nasikh) nor can it be abrogated (mansukh) according to the majority. The author explains the reasons: first, the ummah has no authority to repeal Allah's laws, and qiyas is based on opinion, not revelation. Second, for naskh to occur, two proofs must be in conflict if contemporaneous, but qiyas is weaker than nass and collapses when opposed by a text. The author also addresses the view of his father, who held that qiyas based on inferred 'illa is too weak to cause naskh. However, the author disagrees, noting that even weak proofs can specify general texts, so they might affect rulings. The discussion includes the views of Ibn al-Hajib on qiyas with a known 'illa. The overall conclusion is that qiyas does not have the strength to abrogate or be abrogated, though it may be overridden by a stronger proof.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction applying a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared 'illa.
ناسخ (nasikh): An abrogating proof that removes a previous ruling.
منسوخ (mansukh): A ruling that is abrogated by a later proof.
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the majority hold that qiyas cannot be a nasikh?
A) Because the ummah has no authority to nullify Allah's laws.
B) Because qiyas is not a valid proof.
C) Because qiyas is always weaker than nass.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas, being a weaker proof, cannot abrogate a stronger text, nor can it be abrogated because its preponderance is lost when opposed.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced

Does Abrogation of the Original Ruling Abrogate the Qiyas Ruling?
Dispute on whether far' ruling remains if asl ruling is abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether abrogation of the asl nullifies the far' in qiyas, and evaluate the arguments for and against.

Core Idea
Abrogation of the original ruling nullifies the 'illa, so the qiyas-derived branch ruling falls.

In usul al-fiqh, a key question arises: if the ruling of the original case (asl) used in qiyas is abrogated, does the ruling of the branch case (far') remain valid? This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the Hanafi stance that it does not, and critically examines opposing views. Understanding this helps clarify the dependence of qiyas on the continued validity of its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
Restate the mas'ala: Does abrogation of the asl ruling remove the far' ruling derived by qiyas on that asl?
The issue is whether the far' ruling survives the removal of its source.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Reasoning
The Hanafi school holds that the far' ruling falls because abrogation nullifies the 'illa. The 'illa is the basis of qiyas; without it, the far' has no evidence.
Hanafi proof: abrogation of asl = cancellation of 'illa, so far' ruling is invalid.
3
Analyze the Opposing Argument
Some claim the far' ruling remains because the indication (dalala) of the asl on the far' persists, or because the 'illa might be stronger in the far'.
The opposing view attributes to Hanafis but is unsubstantiated.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi rebuttal: if the 'illa is stronger in the far', it becomes a direct dalala, not qiyas. The dependence on 'illa means removal of asl removes the far'.
The passage also discusses whether abrogation might be due to a mafsada specific to asl, leaving the 'illa intact. The author considers this but leans toward removal.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: if far' ruling survived, it would be a ruling without valid basis, which is unacceptable in usul.
The dispute may be partly verbal; the Hanafi position is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : إذا نسخ حكم الأصل للقياس (لا يبقى حكم الفرع الثابت بالقياس على هذا الأصل (وهذا ليس نسخاً عند الجمهور وقيل نسخ قالوا لأن انتفاء الحكم لانتفاء العلة ليس من النسخ فإنه رفع من الشارع ولم يوجد وأيضاً هذا انتهاء جلي، فإنه يعرف عند ملاحظة حكم الأصل، وعلته أنه يزول بزوالها فهو موجب موقت وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن الأول إعادة عين الدعوى، والحكم قد كان ثابتاً من الشارع، وإنما أزال بإزالته وإلغاء علته، فهو رفع من الشارع وهذا هو النسخ، وزوال العلة قد يكون خفياً أيضاً، بحيث لا يعلم إلا عند إبانة الشرع انتفاء الحكم المعلل بها عند وجودها، كما فيما نحن فيه. والأشبه أن النزاع لفظي (وقيل: يبقى) حكم الفرع عند انتساخ حكم الأصل ونسب) هذا إلى الحنفية) أشار إلى هذه النسبة لم تثبت وكيف لا وقد صرحوا أن النص المنسوخ لا يصح عليه القياس وسيجيء في شروط القياس أن من شروطه أن لا يكون حكم الأصل منسوخاً لنا: أن نسخ الأصل إلغاء للعلة عن العلية وهو ظاهر فيرتفع الفرع) أي حكمه (وإلا) أي وإن لم يرتفع حكم الفرع (لكان) ثبوته (عن غير دليل ولو بقاء إذ غير القياس مفروض الانتفاء، والقياس قد تقاعد لعدم اعتبار الشارع ،علته وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن العلة ربما كانت في الفرع أقوى، ومن ارتفاع الأصل لا يلزم إلا عدم اعتبار قدر العلة الموجودة فيه، ولا يلزم منه عدم اعتبارها مطلقاً، فيجوز أن يبقى القدر الموجود في الفرع معتبراً، فبقى الحكم المنوط بها فيه، إلا أن يقال المناط إذا كان أقوى في الفرع يكون دلالة لا قياساً، والقياس إنما يكون فيما إذا كان الفرع مساوياً للأصل في العلة ،وأضعف وحينئذ يلزم البتة من عدم اعتبار القدر الموجود في الأصل عدم اعتبار الموجود في الفرع، لكن هذا اصطلاح محض لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، فإن مناط الفرق والقياس على كون المناط مفهوماً لغة وعدمه، فإذا لم يكن المناط مفهوماً لغة بل رأياً يعود الإشكال ،قهقرى ثم ههنا بحث آخر هو أن انتساخ الأصل لا يوجب عدم اعتبار العلة، بل يجوز أن تبقى العلة معتبرة، وإنما رفع حكم العلة بطريان مفسدة مختصة بالأصل لأجلها ارتفع، ويبقى القدر الموجود في الفرع من العلة معتبراً، سواء كان مساوياً لما في الأصل أو أضعف، ويبقى الحكم لوجود العلة وانتفاء المفسدة من الحكم ومما يؤيد ما قلنا إن نسخ الحكم عن بعض أفراد العام مع بقائه في البعض جائز من غير ريبة كما صح عن ابن مسعود، فقد انتفى اعتبار العلة في البعض إما بإلغاء القدر الموجود فيه وإما لغلبة مفسدة مختصة به مع أنه لم ينتف اعتبار العلة في البعض الآخر، حتى بقي الحكم فليكن فيما نحن فيه كذلك فتأمل فيه. قائلو بقاء حكم الفرع مع انتفاء حكم الأصل (قالوا : أولاً : الفرع تابع للدلالة للأصل على الحكم (وهي باقية لا لحكم الأصل وهو المنتفى فقط، والدلالة باقية كما كانت فيبقى تابعها (قلنا) حكم الفرع إنما تبع لدلالة الأصل بوساطة العلة المعتبرة شرعاً، وإذا نسخ الأصل لزم من انتفاء الأصل انتفاء الحكمة المعتبرة شرعاً) فانتفى التابع وأيضاً تعلق حكم الفرع بذمة الدلالة
Issue: If the ruling of the origin for qiyas is abrogated, the ruling of the branch established by qiyas on this origin does not remain. This is not considered abrogation according to the majority, and it is said it is abrogation. They said: Because the disappearance of the ruling due to the disappearance of the 'illa is not abrogation, for it is a lifting by the Lawgiver that did not occur. Also, this is an obvious ending, for it is known when considering the ruling of the origin and its 'illa that it ceases with its cessation, so it is a temporary obligation. There is an apparent problem in this: the first is a repetition of the very claim; the ruling was established by the Lawgiver, and He removed it by removing its 'illa, so it is a lifting by the Lawgiver and that is abrogation. The removal of the 'illa may also be hidden, such that it is not known except when the Lawgiver clarifies the disappearance of the ruling that is conditioned by it when it exists, as in our case. The more likely is that the dispute is verbal. And it is said: the ruling of the branch remains when the ruling of the origin is abrogated, and this is attributed to the Hanafis. He indicated that this attribution is not established. How not, when they have stated that an abrogated text does not allow qiyas upon it, and it will come in the conditions of qiyas that among its conditions is that the ruling of the origin is not abrogated. For us: the abrogation of the origin is the nullification of the 'illa from being an 'illa, and that is apparent, so the branch (its ruling) is removed. Otherwise, if the branch ruling is not removed, its establishment would be without evidence, even if by way of remainder, since the other than qiyas is assumed absent, and qiyas has fallen short due to the Lawgiver's non-consideration of its 'illa. There is an apparent problem in this: for the 'illa might be stronger in the branch, and from the removal of the origin only follows the non-consideration of the amount of 'illa existing in it, and from it does not follow its absolute non-consideration. So it is possible that the amount existing in the branch remains considered, and the ruling dependent on it in it remains. Unless it is said: if the manat is stronger in the branch, it is a dalala, not qiyas, and qiyas is only when the branch is equal to the origin in the 'illa or weaker. Then indeed from the non-consideration of the amount in the origin follows the non-consideration of the amount in the branch. But this is pure terminology that does not suffice for truth at all, for the criterion of difference and qiyas is on whether the manat is understood linguistically or not. If the manat is not understood linguistically but by opinion, the problem returns backwards. Then here is another discussion: the abrogation of the origin does not necessitate non-consideration of the 'illa; rather, it is possible that the 'illa remains considered, and the ruling of the 'illa was lifted only due to an arising mafsada specific to the origin, due to which it was lifted. And the amount of 'illa existing in the branch remains considered, whether equal to that in the origin or weaker, and the ruling remains due to the existence of the 'illa and the absence of the mafsada from the ruling. Supporting what we said: that the abrogation of the ruling from some individuals of a general ruling while it remains in others is permissible without doubt, as established from Ibn Mas'ud. The consideration of the 'illa has been negated in some individuals, either by nullifying the amount existing in them or by the prevalence of a specific mafsada, while the consideration of the 'illa in other individuals was not negated, to the point that the ruling remained. So let it be likewise in our case, so reflect on it. Those who say the ruling of the branch remains while the ruling of the origin is abrogated (said): First, the branch is a follower of the indication of the origin upon the ruling, and it (the indication) remains, not the ruling of the origin which is only removed. The indication remains as it was, so its follower remains. (We said): The ruling of the branch is only a follower of the indication of the origin through the medium of the 'illa considered by the Shariah. When the origin is abrogated, the removal of the origin necessitates the removal of the wisdom considered by the Shariah, so the follower is removed. Also, the ruling of the branch is attached to the responsibility of the indication.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific mas'ala in usul al-fiqh: if the ruling of the original case (asl) is abrogated, does the ruling of the branch (far') established by qiyas on that asl continue to be valid? The Hanafi position is that it does not remain; the abrogation of the asl nullifies the 'illa, so the far' ruling falls. This is considered not naskh by the majority (جمهور) but some call it naskh. The author then presents the argument that since the ruling disappears due to the disappearance of its cause, it is not naskh because the Lawgiver did not directly lift it. However, the author finds this problematic: the ruling was established by the Lawgiver, and its removal by removing its cause is still a lifting by the Lawgiver, hence naskh. The dispute may be verbal. He then mentions an attribution to the Hanafis that the far' ruling remains, but he dismisses this as unsubstantiated because Hanafis explicitly state that an abrogated text cannot be used for qiyas. The author then provides the Hanafi proof: abrogation of asl cancels the 'illa, so the far' ruling rises. If it remained, it would be without evidence. An objection is raised: the 'illa may be stronger in the far', so the removal of the asl does not necessitate removing the 'illa entirely. The author responds that if the manat (the basis of the ruling) is stronger in the far', it becomes a direct dalala rather than qiyas; qiyas requires equality or weakness. But this is a terminological issue. He then introduces another angle: the abrogation of the asl might be due to a specific mafsada in the asl, leaving the 'illa still considered in the far'. This is supported by the permissibility of abrogating a ruling from some individuals of a general category while it remains in others, as reported from Ibn Mas'ud. The passage ends with the argument of those who support the survival of the far' ruling: the indication (dalala) of the asl on the far' remains even if the asl ruling is abrogated. The Hanafi response is that the far' ruling depends on the 'illa, and the 'illa is invalidated by the abrogation of the asl. The debate is nuanced, with the author leaning toward the position that the far' ruling does not remain, but he presents both sides for reflection.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that is the basis for qiyas; its presence gives the ruling, its absence removes it.
الفرع (al-far'): The secondary case whose ruling is derived from the original case (asl) through qiyas.
الأصل (al-asl): The original case whose ruling is used as a basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when the ruling of the asl is abrogated, what happens to the far' ruling established by qiyas?
A) It remains because the indication of the asl remains.
B) It falls because the 'illa is nullified.
C) It remains only if the far' has a stronger 'illa.
D) It is considered abrogated separately from the asl.

Key Takeaway
If the asl ruling is abrogated, the far' ruling in qiyas does not remain because the 'illa is nullified.

The Principle of Ziyada: Is Purity a Condition for Tawaf?
تطبيق قاعدة الزيادة على شرط الطهارة للطواف

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle regarding ziyada (addition) by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) to an absolute text (mutlaq), and derive the ruling for tawaf without purity.

Core Idea
Adding a condition to an absolute Quranic text requires definitive evidence; a solitary hadith cannot impose a condition but can establish obligation.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, we examine how the Hanafi school applies the usul principle of ziyada (addition) to the issue of purity (tahara) for tawaf. The central question: does the hadith 'tawaf is like prayer' make purity a condition (shart) for tawaf, or merely an obligation (wajib)? The Hanafi response distinguishes between adding a condition (ziyada) and clarifying an ambiguous text (bayan)—a subtle but crucial distinction in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing texts
Locate the Quranic verse (22:29) and the hadith from Ibn Abbas in the passage. Note that the verse is an absolute command to perform tawaf, while the hadith states 'tawaf is like prayer.'
The verse is from al-Hajj, the hadith is narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i.
2
Classify the Quranic text as mutlaq or mujmal
The Hanafi school holds that the verse is mutlaq (absolute) – it commands tawaf without specifying conditions. The Shafi'i school and al-Haddad argue it is mujmal (ambiguous) because the true nature of tawaf is determined by the Lawgiver, so the hadith serves as bayan (clarification).
This classification is the crux of the dispute.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule: ziyada on mutlaq by khabar al-wahid is not allowed
Under Hanafi usul, an absolute text from the Quran (qat'i al-thubut) cannot be restricted or have conditions added by a solitary report (zanni al-thubut). Doing so would amount to naskh (abrogation) which requires definitive evidence. Therefore, the hadith cannot make purity a condition (shart).
However, the hadith is still acted upon to impose obligation (wajib) due to its content.
4
Determine the practical Hanafi ruling
Since purity is not a condition, tawaf performed without purity is valid and the obligation (fard) is discharged. But because purity is wajib based on the hadith, a compensatory sacrifice (dam jabir) is required. The Shafi'i ruling: tawaf is invalid without purity.
Thamarah al-khilaf: validity vs invalidity.
5
Evaluate the counter-objection by al-Haddad
Al-Haddad argues that the verse is not mutlaq but mujmal, so the hadith is bayan (clarification), not ziyada/naskh. The Hanafi response: the analogy in the hadith is about reward or speech, not imposing prayer-like conditions.
This refines the understanding of tashbih (likening).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالطهارة للطواف فإنا لا نجعلها شرطاً حتى يجزىء الطواف من غير طهارة، ولا تجب الإعادة خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله تمسك أصحابه بما روى الترمذي والنسائي عن ابن عباس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلاة إلا أنكم تتكلمون فيه، فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم إلا بخير وأجاب مشايخنا كما أشار إليه المصنف بأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطَوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ [الحج : 29] مطلق، فزيادة الطهارة عليه وتقييد إطلاقها لا يجوز بهذا الخبر المظنون بل يبقى الطواف المفروض مطلقاً، لكن قلنا بوجوب الطهارة عملاً بهذا الخبر، فيجب الدم الجابر إن طاف محدثاً، لكن سقط الفرض كذا قالوا واعترض عليه الشيخ الهداد بأنا لا نسلم أن الطواف مطلق، كيف ولو كان مطلقاً لكفى شوط واحد فإنه أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم الطواف لغة، بل المراد الطواف الشرعي المعتبر عند الشارع، وهو مجمل في الأركان والشروط، فيقع هذا الخبر بياناً لشرطه، فلا نسخ أصلاً، فلا يلزم عليه محذور فحينئذ لا يصلح تفرع هذه الفريعة على هذا الأصل، بل الحق في الجواب أن تمثيل شيء بشيء لا يوجب في المماثلة للصلاة في اشتراط الطهارة، بل يجوز أن يكون المعنى يوجب الطواف، مثل الصلاة في الثواب في الآخرة، فلا تكلموا إلا بخير، لكن على هذا لا بد لوجوب الطهارة من غير اشتراط من دليل آخر، ولعله هنا الاحتياط في أمر العبادة فافهم
Like purity (tahara) for tawaf: we do not make it a condition such that tawaf without purity is invalid, nor is repetition obligatory, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may God have mercy on him). His followers hold to what al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks should only speak good.' And our teachers answered, as the author pointed out, that God's statement: {And let them circumambulate the Ancient House} (al-Hajj 22:29) is absolute, so adding purity to it and restricting its absoluteness is not permissible by this probable report; rather, the obligatory tawaf remains absolute. However, we say that purity is obligatory by acting on this report, so a compensatory blood sacrifice (dam jabir) is obligatory if one performs tawaf in a state of impurity, but the obligation is discharged. So they said. And al-Shaykh al-Haddad objected: we do not concede that tawaf is absolute; how can it be? If it were absolute, a single circuit would suffice, for it is the minimum to which the name tawaf is applied linguistically. Rather, what is meant is the legally prescribed tawaf as considered by the Lawgiver, and it is mujmal (ambiguous) regarding its pillars and conditions. So this report serves as a clarification of its condition, so there is no abrogation at all. Thus no difficulty arises. Then this branch cannot be derived from this principle. Rather, the correct answer is that likening one thing to another does not necessitate similarity to prayer in requiring purity; it may mean that tawaf is like prayer in reward in the Hereafter, so speak only good. But on this, there must be another evidence for the obligation of purity without it being a condition. Perhaps here it is out of caution in matters of worship. So understand.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage applies the principle of ziyada to the case of tawaf and tahara. The Hanafi position: tawaf without purity is valid (the obligation is discharged) but a sacrifice (dam) is required because purity is obligatory but not a condition. This is based on the absolute verse of tawaf (Quran 22:29). The Shafi'i position, citing the hadith 'Tawaf is like prayer,' considers purity a condition (tahara), so tawaf without it is invalid. The Hanafi response: the verse is absolute, so making purity a condition would be an addition (ziyada) to a definitive text by a solitary report, which is not allowed. However, the hadith is acted upon to establish obligation (wujub) but not conditionality (shartiyya). The commentator al-Haddad objects that the verse is not absolute but mujmal, so the hadith is a bayan (clarification), not an addition. The author counters that the analogy to prayer is not about conditions but about reward.

Key Terms
دم جابر (dam jabir): دم يجب لجبر نقص في النسك وليس لفوات ركن
مطلق (mutlaq): لفظ دال على فرد شائع غير مقيد بقيد
مجمل (mujmal): لفظ لم يتضح معناه المراد بدون بيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما حكم الطواف بدون طهارة عند الحنفية؟
A) الطواف باطل ويجب الإعادة
B) الطواف صحيح ولا شيء عليه
C) الطواف صحيح ويجب دم جابر
D) الطواف صحيح وتلزمه الإعادة

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: an absolute text (mutlaq) from the Quran can only be restricted by a definitive proof; a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) cannot add a condition but can establish an obligation (wajib).
