The Principle of Ziyada: Applying Usul to Wudu Elements
Application of ziyada principle to wudu branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a solitary report cannot abrogate a definitive text (ziyada 'ala al-qat'i) to determine the legal status of disputed wudu elements and distinguish between fard and wajib.

Core Idea
The Quranic command for wudu is definitive; additional elements can only be wajib, not fard, because a solitary report cannot abrogate a definitive text.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school uses the usul principle of ziyada (addition) to resolve disputes about the obligation of intention, sequence, continuity, basmala, and interdigitation in wudu. The Quranic verse (5:6) is considered qat'i (definitive) in its meaning, so any addition from a hadith can only establish wujub (obligation) if the hadith is strong enough, but cannot make the element a rukn (pillar). We will trace the reasoning for each element, focusing on the interplay between textual evidence and usul maxims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitive text
Start with the Quranic verse of wudu (5:6). Note that it commands washing the three limbs and wiping the head without mentioning intention, sequence, etc. As a qat'i text, its ruling is binding.
In Hanafi usul, the Quran (mutawatir) is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala unless specified as mujmal.
2
Classify the additional proofs
For each disputed element, identify the proof: hadith, practice, or consensus. Classify each proof's reliability (thubut) and clarity (dalala). Determine if it is zanni (probable) or qat'i.
Most proofs here are khabar wahid (solitary reports) or fi'l (action) which are zanni.
3
Apply the ziyada rule
The Hanafi rule: a solitary report (khabar wahid) cannot add to (ziyada) or abrogate (naskh) a definitive text. Therefore, these elements cannot be made fard (pillar) because that would add to the Quranic command.
Exception: a mashhur hadith (like 'Actions by intentions') may be considered for ziyada but its meaning must be carefully interpreted.
4
Distinguish fard from wajib
Even if an element cannot be fard, it may be wajib (obligatory but not a pillar) if supported by strong enough evidence. Action does not indicate obligation; only explicit command does.
For example, tasmiya: Ibn al-Humam argued the hadith is hasan, so it establishes wujub but not rukniyya because that would be ziyada.
5
Synthesize the rulings
For each element, state the final Hanafi ruling: intention is sunnah (not fard or wajib), sequence and continuity are sunnah (action does not indicate obligation), interdigitation is sunnah (lack of transmission), basmala is wajib (based on hasan hadith) but not a pillar.
Note the nuance: the basmala ruling is a minority view within the Hanafi school; the majority holds it is sunnah. The author questions Ibn al-Humam's conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكثير أي ككثير من الفروع منها عدم وجوب النية والترتيب في الوضوء، لقوله عليه وآله الصلاة والسلام: «الأعمال بالنيات» رواه الشيخان وغيرهما والمواظبة على الترتيب من غير ترك قال في سفر السعادة لم يترك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الترتيب مرة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله بوجوبهما لذلك، وكذا عدم وجوب الموالاة بالمواظبة المذكورة كما عليه مالك رضي الله عنه، وكذا عدم وجوب التسمية لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «لا وضوء لمن لم يسم» رواه الدارقطني كما قال به أحمد رحمه الله وكذا عدم وجوب التخليل، لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : خللوا أصابعكم كيلا تتخللها نار جهنم وذلك لأن آية الوضوء إنما تدل على أجزاء غسل الأعضاء الثلاثة الرأس مطلقاً مع مسح عن النية وغيرها مما ذكر، فلو زيد أحد هذه الأشياء لزم انتساخ القاطع بخبر الواحد، كذا قالوا: وهذا العذر صحيح فيما وراء النية، أما هي فحديث : الأعمال بالنيات مشهور به تصح الزيادة على الكتاب، بل الحق فيه أن الحديث لا يدل على اشتراط النية أصلاً في الوضوء وغيره من الوسائل. ثم إن هذا العذر إنما يكفي لعدم افتراض هذه الأمور، لكنه يجوز أن تكون واجبة، فالنية قد عرفت حالها، وأما الترتيب والموالاة فلأن الفعل لا يدل على الوجوب كما سيجيء، وليس قول يدل عليه، وأما التخليل فلثبوت الترك، وعدم نقل من نقل وضوء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم من الصحابة المعتبرين، وأما التسمية فلأن الحديث ضعيف كما بين في موضعه، لكن الشيخ ابن الهمام قال في فتح القدير: إنّ هذا الحديث لتكثر طرقه وكون الخلل الذي في راويه غير الفسق صار في درجة الحسن، فهو وإن لم يوجب الركنية لئلا يلزم الزيادة على الكتاب لكن ينبغي أن يثبت الوجوب، فتأمل فيه فإنه موضع تأمل
And many, i.e., many of the branches, include: non-obligation of intention (niyya) and sequence (tartib) in wudu, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Actions are by intentions' (agreed upon), and the constancy upon sequence without omission. It is said in Safar al-Sa'ada: The Messenger of God never once left sequence. And al-Shafi'i said they are obligatory because of that. Likewise, non-obligation of continuity (muwalah) by the mentioned constancy, as Malik holds. Likewise, non-obligation of naming (tasmiya) because of his saying: 'No wudu for one who does not mention God's name' (al-Daraqutni) as Ahmad said. Likewise, non-obligation of interdigitation (tahlil) because of his saying: 'Interdigitate your fingers lest the fire of Hell interdigitate them.' And that is because the verse of wudu only indicates the parts: washing the three limbs and wiping the head absolutely, without intention and other things mentioned. So if any of these things were added, it would necessitate abrogating the definitive by a solitary report. So they said. And this excuse is correct except for intention, because the hadith 'Actions by intentions' is well-known (mashhur), so it is permissible to add to the Book by it. Rather, the truth is that the hadith does not indicate the conditionality of intention at all in wudu and other means. Then this excuse suffices for not making these things obligatory (fard), but they could be obligatory (wajib). The status of intention is known. As for sequence and continuity, action does not indicate obligation, as will come, and there is no saying indicating it. As for interdigitation, because omission is established, and it is not transmitted from the reliable companions who transmitted the wudu of the Messenger. As for naming (tasmiya), because the hadith is weak, as explained in its place. However, Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: this hadith, due to the multiplicity of its chains and the flaw in its narrator not being sinful, becomes hasan. So although it does not necessitate being a pillar (rukn) to avoid addition to the Book, it should establish obligation. So ponder, for it is a place of reflection.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage discusses several rulings related to wudu: intention (niyya), sequence (tartib), continuity (muwalah), basmala (tasmiya), and interdigitation (tahlil). The Hanafi position is that these are not obligatory (fard) because the verse of wudu (Quran 5:6) is absolute and any addition would be a ziyada on a qat'i text. However, some of these may be wajib (obligatory but not pillars) based on other evidence. The author addresses objections: intention is not indicated by the hadith 'Actions by intentions' in the context of wudu; sequence and continuity are not proven obligatory by the Prophet's consistent practice because action does not imply obligation; interdigitation is not obligatory because it was not transmitted from the companions; tasmiya is based on a weak hadith, though Ibn al-Humam considers it hasan and suggests wujub but not rukniyya. This demonstrates the nuance: the principle of ziyada prevents making these things pillars (fard) but allows them to be wajib.

Key Terms
نية (niyya): قصد الفعل في العبادة
ترتيب (tartib): غسل الأعضاء بالترتيب المذكور في الآية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما حكم التسمية في الوضوء عند الحنفية بناءً على حديث 'لا وضوء لمن لم يسم'؟
A) فرض (ركن)
B) واجب (غير ركن)
C) سنة
D) مكروه

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of ziyada prevents making additional wudu elements into pillars (fard) but allows them to be wajib if supported by strong evidence.

The Ziyada Principle: Why Fatiha and Ta'dil Are Not Pillars
Applying the ziyada principle to prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a definitive (qat'i) text cannot be abrogated or specified by a solitary report (khabar wahid) to derive the ruling that reciting al-Fatiha, ta'dil al-arkan, and qawma are not pillars of prayer.

Core Idea
A definitive Quranic text cannot be superseded by a solitary hadith — the Hanafi foundation for why Fatiha is not a pillar.

In this passage, the author applies the Hanafi usul principle of 'ziyada' (addition) to the prayer. The Quran establishes the obligation of recitation, bowing, and prostration in absolute terms. The Hanafi school argues that making recitation of the specific chapter al-Fatiha, or adding standing after bowing (qawma) and proper adjustment (ta'dil), as mandatory pillars would constitute an addition to the definitive text by a solitary report, which is impermissible. You will walk through the derivation and see how the Hanafis rebut the counter-argument that these hadiths serve as clarifications (bayan) rather than additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitive text (qat'i) for recitation
Locate the Quranic verse that establishes the obligation of recitation in prayer. The passage cites {So recite what is easy from the Quran} (al-Muzzammil 73:20). This is absolute (mutlaq) and definitive in transmission (qat'i al-thubut).
Quran 73:20 is the basis for the Hanafi position.
2
Identify the solitary report (khabar wahid) in question
The hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book' is a khabar wahid (zanni al-thubut). It is recorded by Bukhari and Muslim but not transmitted to the level of tawatur.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the opposing school.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle: qat'i cannot be abrogated or specified by zanni
Since the Quranic verse is qat'i, the hadith, being zanni, cannot abrogate or specify it. Therefore, the obligation remains general: any recitation suffices, not only al-Fatiha.
This is the core of the Hanafi argument.
4
Analyze the counter-argument: prayer is mujmal and the hadith is bayan
The opposition argues that the prayer is ambiguous (mujmal) and the hadith clarifies (bayan) what is obligatory. The Hanafi rebuttal: the Quranic verse is not mujmal; it clearly establishes the pillar of recitation as absolute. Moreover, the hadith itself has textual instability (idhtirab), as some versions include the word 'khidaj' (deficient), indicating the prayer exists with deficiency.
The author also notes that the hadith cannot be bayan because the Quranic text is not ambiguous.
5
Extend the same reasoning to ta'dil al-arkan and qawma
The same principle applies: the verses {Bow and prostrate} (al-Hajj 22:77) are qat'i in establishing ruku' and sujud. Adding ta'dil and qawma as pillars would be a ziyada on a qat'i text via a solitary report (hadith of the Bedouin), which is not permissible according to Hanafi usul. Note that Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees on ta'dil, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that they are not pillars.
The passage contrasts with the three Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : عدم ركنية الفاتحة في الصلاة، كما قال الأئمة الثلاثة، لقول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب رواه الشيخان لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزمل: 20] يقتضي افتراض مطلق القراءة لما تيسر أي قدر كان من أي سورة كانت، فجعل الفاتحة ركناً نسخ لهذا القاطع بخبر الواحد فلا يجوز، وكذا تعديل الأركان ليس ركناً، وكذا القومة بعد الركوع ، لحديث الأعرابي المخرّج في الصحيحين». و«موطأ الإمام محمد» خلافاً للأئمة الثلاثة والإمام أبي يوسف، وإلا لزم الزيادة على قوله تعالى: ﴿أَرْكَعُواْ وَاسْجُدُوا ﴾ [الحج : 77] بخبر الواحد وأورد عليه أيضاً بمثل ما أن الصلاة مجملة، فيلتحق مر خبر الفاتحة وحديث الأعرابي بياناً، فلا نسخ ويمكن أن يجاب أن ركن القراءة والركوع والسجود قد ثبت بالقاطع، فلا يلحق هذان الخبران بياناً، وإنما يصيران زيادة على هذا القاطع، ثم ألحق في خبر الفاتحة ما ذكر، فإن القراءة قد فرضت مطلقة بالقاطع ولا إجمال فيه أصلاً حتى يلحق خبر الفاتحة بياناً مع أن متنه مضطرب أيضاً، فإنه قد يروي الصلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب خداج والخداج الناقص، فهذا يقتضي تحقق الصلاة مع النقصان بدونها، وأما حديث الأعرابي فإنما سيق لبيان حقيقة الصلاة، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قال له : صلِّ فإنك لم تصل حين ترك التعديل، ثم بين له الأركان الصلاتية المعدلة
And among them: the non-pillarity of al-Fatiha in prayer, as the three Imams say, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book' (agreed upon). Because God's statement: {So recite what is easy from the Quran} (al-Muzzammil 73:20) necessitates the obligation of absolute recitation of whatever is easy, i.e., whatever it may be from any surah. So making al-Fatiha a pillar would abrogate this definitive text by a solitary report, so it is not permissible. Likewise, adjusting the pillars (ta'dil al-arkan) is not a pillar, and likewise standing up after bowing (qawma) is not a pillar, according to the hadith of the Bedouin recorded in the Sahihs and the Muwatta of Imam Muhammad, contrary to the three Imams and Imam Abu Yusuf. Otherwise, it would necessitate addition to God's statement: {Bow and prostrate} (al-Hajj 22:77) by a solitary report. And an objection was raised against this as well, that prayer is mujmal (ambiguous), so the hadith of Fatiha and the hadith of the Bedouin attach as clarifications (bayan), so there is no abrogation. And it can be answered that the pillar of recitation, bowing, and prostration are established by definitive texts, so these two hadiths do not attach as clarifications; rather, they become additions to this definitive text. Then in the hadith of Fatiha, there is what was mentioned: recitation was made obligatory absolutely by a definitive text, and there is no ambiguity at all for the hadith of Fatiha to attach as a clarification, especially since its text is also inconsistent. For it is narrated: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book' but with the word 'khidaj' (deficient), indicating the prayer exists with deficiency without it. As for the hadith of the Bedouin, it was only narrated to clarify the reality of prayer. The Messenger (peace be upon him) said to him: 'Pray, for you have not prayed' when he left adjustment, then he explained to him the adjusted pillars of prayer.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage applies the ziyada principle to prayer. The Hanafi position: reciting al-Fatiha is not a pillar (rukn) of prayer, nor is standing after ruku' (qawma) or adjusting the pillars (ta'dil). The proof: the Quranic verse {So recite what is easy from the Quran} is absolute, so specifying al-Fatiha as mandatory would be a ziyada on a qat'i text by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid), hence invalid. The hadith 'No prayer without the Fatiha' is thus interpreted to mean no perfect prayer, or it is abrogated, or the word 'khidaj' indicates deficiency but not invalidity. Similarly, the verse {Bow and prostrate} establishes the pillars of ruku' and sujud absolutely; adding qawma and ta'dil would be a ziyada. The objection that prayer is mujmal (ambiguous) and these hadiths serve as bayan is rebutted: the definitive texts clearly establish the pillars, so the hadiths cannot be bayan but are ziyada. The author notes that the text of the Fatiha hadith is also unstable (mudtarib), supporting the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): ما تبطل الصلاة بتركه عمداً أو سهواً
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): الطمأنينة والاستقامة في الأركان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that ta'dil al-arkan is not a pillar of prayer?
A) Because the hadith of the Bedouin is weak.
B) Because the Quranic verse {Bow and prostrate} is qat'i, and adding ta'dil would be a ziyada on a qat'i text by a solitary report.
C) Because Imam Abu Yusuf disagreed, so the school does not accept it.
D) Because the school does not consider any hadith for the pillars of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes definitive (qat'i) texts over solitary (zanni) reports, preventing the addition of pillars to prayer beyond what the Quran explicitly establishes.

The Five Skeptical Doubts Against Tawatur
Listing five skeptical arguments against tawatur and the Hanafi response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five skeptical objections to tawatur and explain why each is considered invalid by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tawatur yields certain knowledge; skeptics' doubts are sophistry that challenge self-evident truths.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents five arguments raised by the Samaniyya, a group of Indian skeptics, against the epistemological value of mutawatir reports. While at first glance these objections may appear plausible, the Hanafi response is that they are mere sophistry akin to questioning necessary knowledge. Understanding these objections and their rebuttal strengthens your grasp of tawatur as a source of qat'i knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the skeptics and their challenge
Recognize that the Samaniyya are a group from India who deny prophethood; they are rejecting all mutawatir reports, including those about distant lands and past nations, as a denial of necessary knowledge.
2
Analyze the meal analogy (doubt 1)
The skeptics argue that tawatur is like a crowd agreeing to share one meal, which is customarily impossible. Understand the fallacy: tawatur does not require the reporters to agree on a lie; they independently transmit the same report.
The analogy is a false comparison.
3
Analyze the possibility of individual lies (doubt 2)
They argue that since each reporter could lie, the whole could also lie. Note the flaw: customary impossibility of mass lying overrides the individual possibility, as it is customarily impossible for a large group to independently lie about the same event.
4
Analyze contradictory reports (doubt 3)
They argue that two groups reporting opposites would lead to contradiction if both were taken as certain. Recognize that in practice, contradictory tawatur reports do not occur simultaneously; one report is false and not truly mutawatir.
5
Analyze the remaining doubts and the Hanafi response
For doubt 4 (Jewish/Christian fabrications) the flaw is that those reports are not actually mutawatir. For doubt 5 (difference in certainty), the Hanafi response is that tawatur yields necessary knowledge, though the degree of obviousness may vary. The overall response: these are sophistries against necessary knowledge.
The author dismisses them as 'mukabarah' (stubborn denial).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسمنية قوم من الهند منكرو النبوة (وهو) أي قولهم ( مكابرة) صريحة على العقل (ضرورة العلم بالبلاد النائية) كمكة والمدينة شرفهما الله تعالى ( والأمم الخالية) كالأنبياء السابقين، وكأوس وكي قالوا :أولاً : إنه أي الأخبار تواتراً (كاجتماع الجمع على طعام واحد، وهو ممتنع عادة) فيستحيل الأخبار تواتراً، فلا يفيد العلم، إذ هو فرع التحقق، وهذه الشبهة تدل على أنهم أنكروا وجود التواتر أيضاً (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : يجوز الكذب على كل من المخبرين بتعمد أو نسيان أو ذهول (فكذا) يجوز الكذب على الكل إجماعاً (لأنه) أي لأن الكل (هو) أي كل واحد (مجتمعاً) فحكمه حكمهم، وإذا جاز الكذب فلا علم (و) قالوا (ثالثاً) لو أفاد التواتر العلم يؤدي إلى التناقض إذا أخبر جمعان غفيران (بنقيضين) كما إذا أخبر جمع بوجود اسكندر وآخر بعدمه، فلو كانا معلومين لكان موجوداً ومعدوماً في الواقع (و) قالوا (رابعاً) لو أفاد المتواتر علماً (يلزم تصديق اليهود أو النصارى فيما نقلوه) افتراء (عن موسى عليهما وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) أنه قال: لا نبي بعدي والثاني باطل قطعاً، فإن هذا النقل كذب وافتراء بلا مرية (و) قالوا (خامساً) لو أفاد المتواتر العلم لما كان بينه وبين العلوم الأخر تفاوت و نجد التفاوت بينه وبين قولنا الواحد نصف الاثنين، وهو دليل احتمال النقيضين في المتواتر، فلا يفيد العلم و(الجواب عن شبهاتهم كلها (إجمالاً أنه تشكيك في الضروري) فإن كل أحد يعلم إفادة المتواتر العلم كشبه السوفسطائية) فإنها تشكيكات في الأمور الضرورية، فالشبهات جلها باطلة لا يلتفت إليها فافهم
And the Samaniyya are a people from India who deny prophethood. (And it) i.e. their statement (is a clear stubbornness) against reason (due to necessary knowledge of distant lands) like Mecca and Medina, may Allah honor them, (and past nations) like the previous prophets, and like Aws and Kay? They said: First: That is, the report being mutawatir (like the gathering of a crowd for one meal, and that is customarily impossible) so a report cannot be mutawatir, thus it does not yield knowledge, since it is a branch of verification. And this doubt indicates that they also denied the existence of tawatur. (And) they said: (Second: Lying is possible for each of the reporters intentionally or by forgetfulness or heedlessness, (so likewise) lying is possible for all of them unanimously (because) i.e. because the whole (is) i.e. each one (collectively), so its ruling is their ruling. If lying is possible then no knowledge. (And) they said (Third: If tawatur produced knowledge, it would lead to contradiction when two large groups report (two opposites), as when a group reports the existence of Alexander and another reports his non-existence. If both were known, he would exist and not exist in reality. (And) they said (Fourth: If mutawatir led to knowledge, (it would necessitate believing the Jews or Christians in what they fabricated) (about Moses, peace be upon him, and upon our Prophet and his family and companions) that he said: no prophet after me, and the second is definitely false, for this report is a lie and fabrication without doubt. (And) they said (Fifth: If mutawatir yielded knowledge, there would be no difference between it and other sciences, yet we find a difference between it and our saying 'one is half of two', which indicates the possibility of opposites in mutawatir, so it does not yield knowledge. And (the answer to all their doubts) (in summary is that it is a questioning of the necessary) for everyone knows that mutawatir yields knowledge, like the sophistical doubts, for they are questionings of necessary matters, so the doubts are mostly invalid and not to be heeded. So understand.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents five arguments raised by the Samaniyya skeptics against the epistemological value of mutawatir reports. The author first identifies them as a group from India who deny prophethood, then lists their five doubts: (1) an analogy to the impossibility of a crowd agreeing to eat one meal; (2) the possibility of each reporter lying individually, so the whole may also lie; (3) contradictory reports would lead to impossible simultaneous existence and non-existence; (4) accepting tawatur would force us to believe Jewish/Christian fabrications about Moses; (5) the difference in certainty between tawatur and self-evident truths like 'half of two' shows it is not certain. The author's summary response is that these are mere sophistries akin to questioning necessary knowledge, thus not worth detailed rebuttal at this stage.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Successive transmission of a report by a group that cannot be lying by custom, yielding certain knowledge.
ضروري (ḍarūrī): Necessary knowledge that is self-evident and not dependent on reasoning.
مكابرة (mukābarah): Stubborn denial of the obvious, a form of sophistry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The possibility of lying by reporters
B) The impossibility of a crowd agreeing on one meal as an analogy
C) The contradiction from two reports opposing each other
D) The need to believe Jewish fabrications

Key Takeaway
Tawatur yields certain knowledge; skeptics' doubts are sophistical challenges that do not undermine its epistemological value.

Refutation of Doubt 1: Analogy with Difference
Refutation of the first doubt by qiyas ma'a al-fariq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific difference between the skeptics' analogy (qiyas) and the actual case of tawatur, and state why the analogy fails.

Core Idea
Tawatur rebutted: motive to report is present; crowd appetite for same meal is rare.

The first doubt against tawatur is an analogy: just as a crowd cannot all desire the same meal, so too can a crowd not all agree on a report. In this lesson, we examine the detailed Hanafi response, which exposes a critical difference (fariq) between the root case (the meal) and the branch (tawatur), invalidating the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the skeptics' analogy
Pinpoint the two cases being compared: the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal (asl) and the claim that tawatur (collective transmission) is impossible (far').
The skeptics use qiyas to argue that if a crowd cannot share a meal, then it cannot share a report.
2
Analyze the motive factor
Recognize that the Hanafi response highlights a fariq: in tawatur, reporters have a natural motive (dā'ī) to report what they know (habitual truth-telling), whereas in the meal example, the motive (appetite) is rarely shared by a crowd.
The key difference is the presence/absence of a universal motive.
3
Determine the logical consequence
Conclude that the analogy is flawed (qiyās ma'a al-fāriq), so the doubt does not stand. The presence of motive in reporting makes collective agreement possible, unlike the rare shared appetite.
This is a classic Hanafi critique of analogies that ignore contextual differences.
4
Apply to modern contexts
Consider how this refutation applies to any argument that dismisses widespread consensus based on a false analogy. The motive to report truth is a key presumption in tawatur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المجموع) (حكم كل) أي كل واحد واحد (فللاجتماع أثر في الحكم فلا يوجد عند عدمه، وإذا كان حكماهما متخالفين فلا يلزم من جواز كذب كل جواز كذب الجميع، ثم مثل لافتراق الحكمين بقوله ألا ترى أن كلاً النقيضين مقدور) لإمكانه (بخلاف الكل فإنه مستحيل غير مقدور فإن قلت : لو كان كل النقيضين غير ممكن لوجب نقيضه وهو رفعهما، أنه بالذات، قلت: رفع الكل أعم مع ممتنع من رفعهما معاً، بل هو قد يكون برفع واحد لا بعينه ولا يلزم من وجوب الأعم وجوب الأخص، نعم يلزم وجوب أحدهما لامتناع الارتفاع وإن كان كل ممكناً، ولا يلزم من أفراد شيء إمكان مطلقه فافهم وعن الدليل الثالث وهو لزوم اجتماع النقيضين عند إمكان جميع أخبار محال، ولو فرض ههنا لزم المحال وهو التناقض، فحصول العلم بالتواتر محال لأنه ما لزم المحال إلا منه قلت لا نسلم إمكانه بالذات، بل هو محال بالذات والعادة تفيد العلم باستحالته فتأمل. وأيضاً : الممكن بالذات لا يلزم منه محال بالنظر إلى ذاته، وأما بحسب الواقع فقد يستلزم محالاً بالذات، فهذا الإخبار وإن كان في نفسه ممكناً غير مستلزم للمحال لعدم وجوب العلم منه بالذات لكنه مستحيل في الواقع بالعادة، فيستلزم في الواقع المحال لإيجاب العادة العلم به فافهم وعن) الدليل (الرابع) وهو لزوم صدق إخبار اليهود والنصارى الكاذبة بيقين بأن تواترها ممنوع و(أن ابتداءه ليس كوسطه) بل لم يوجد في الابتداء مخبرون بعدد التواتر إنما هم بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا أمثال هذه الأقاويل وأخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين وهم أخبروا ظناً، بل علماً بالكذب شياطينهم الآخرين، فقد وجد في الوسط مبلغ التواتر، ثم إن كلهم ظانون غير مستيقنين، فلم يوجد التواتر، ومثل هذا إخبار الشيعة بالنص الجلي على إمامة أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأشجعين علي بن أبي طالب كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام، فإن بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا وكذبوا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، ثم أخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين حتى صار منقولاً فيهم، ثم إن الشبهة إنما ترد على من لا يشترط العدالة في التواتر وأما على الشارط فلا تتجه أصلاً فتدبر (وعن) الدليل (الخامس) وهو وجدان التفاوت بينه وبين البديهي الآخر الموجب لاحتمال النقيض أن غاية ما لزم من شبههم التفاوت في الجملة و لا نسلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت) فإنه قد يكون البعض خفياً عن بعض لعدم ملاحظة الأطراف حقها، أو لمصاحبة بعض الوسط دون بعض نعم إنها لا تتفاوت بمعنى احتمال أحدها النقيض دون الاخر ولزومه ههنا ممنوع، بل المتواتر والواحد نصف الاثنين لا يحتمل كل منهما النقيض ( ولو سلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت جلاء وخفاء أصلاً ( فالتفاوت) ههنا (للإنس وعدمه لا لكون أحدهما جلياً والآخر خفياً فتدبر
And as for the detailed answer to their doubts: concerning the first proof, which is their analogy to the impossibility of the whole gathering on one meal, (it is an analogy with a difference between the branch and the root regarding the existence of motive in the reports of the whole — and that is custom here, for the custom of a person is to report what he knows — and its absence there, i.e., in the thing being analogized to, for the motive to eat is appetite, and it is rare customarily that a crowd desires one meal. And concerning the second proof, which is the possibility of lying: the ruling of the whole (i.e., the group) may differ from the ruling of each individual, for the collective has an effect on the ruling, so it does not exist in its absence. Since their rulings differ, the possibility of each individual lying does not entail the possibility of all lying together. Then he gave an example of the difference of rulings: 'Do you not see that each of the two opposites is possible (due to its capability), unlike the whole which is impossible, not capable? If you say: if each of the opposites were not possible, then its opposite would be necessary, which is the negation of both, in itself; I say: the negation of the whole is more general and is not possible with the negation of both together; rather it may be by negating one without specifying, and the necessity of the general does not require the necessity of the specific. Yes, the necessity of one of them is required due to the impossibility of both being negated, even if each is possible, and the possibility of the parts does not imply the possibility of the whole. So understand. And concerning the third proof, which is the necessitation of the conjunction of opposites when two reports are contradictory: tawatur of opposites is customarily impossible, so no contradiction in reality results; rather, if it were contrary to reality, there is no impossibility. If you say: reporting opposites, though against custom, is intrinsically possible, and assuming it here would lead to the impossible, i.e., contradiction, so obtaining knowledge from tawatur is impossible because the impossible would only result from it; I say: We do not concede its intrinsic possibility; rather it is intrinsically impossible, and custom yields knowledge of its impossibility. So reflect. Also: the intrinsically possible does not necessarily entail impossibility in itself, but in reality it may entail impossibility. So this report, though in itself possible and not entailing impossibility due to knowledge not being necessary from it in itself, is in reality impossible by custom, so in reality it entails the impossible because custom necessitates knowledge from it. So understand. And concerning the fourth proof, which is the necessitation of believing the false reports of Jews and Christians: that their tawatur is denied, and its beginning is not like its middle. Rather, at the beginning there were not reporters reaching the number of tawatur; only some of their devils invented such sayings and informed their other devils, and they informed others by conjecture, nay with knowledge of the lie, until those at the middle reached the number of tawatur, yet all of them were conjecturing, not certain, so tawatur did not exist. An example is the Shi'a report of the explicit text on the Imamate of the Commander of the Faithful and the Imam of the brave, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family); some of their devils invented and lied against the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), then informed other devils until it became transmitted among them. Moreover, this doubt only arises against those who do not stipulate integrity ('adala) in tawatur; as for those who stipulate it, it is not applicable at all. So ponder. And concerning the fifth proof, which is the perceived difference between it and other self-evident truths leading to the possibility of the opposite: the utmost that follows from their doubt is difference in some respect, and we do not concede that sciences do not differ. For some may be hidden from some people due to not properly observing all aspects, or due to accompanying some intermediaries but not others. Indeed, they do not differ in the sense that one might admit the opposite while another does not; that it admits the opposite here is denied. Rather, both the mutawatir and 'one is half of two' do not admit the opposite. Even if one concedes that sciences do not differ at all in clarity and obscurity, the difference here is due to familiarity or unfamiliarity, not because one is clear and the other obscure. So ponder.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed refutation of each of the five doubts against tawatur. The author systematically responds: (1) The analogy to the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal is flawed because the motive for reporting (informing of known facts) is present in tawatur but lacking in the example (appetite for food is rarely shared). (2) The possibility of each individual lying does not extend to the whole when considered collectively, as the whole has a distinct ruling; he illustrates with the logical point that each of two opposites is possible individually but together they are impossible. (3) The possibility of contradictory reports is intrinsically impossible by custom, and even if possible in theory, custom establishes knowledge that the contradiction does not occur in reality. (4) The Jewish/Christian fabrications did not originate from tawatur; the initial transmitters were few and knowingly lying, and the later transmitters only conjectured, not knowing the truth; thus no genuine tawatur occurred. This also applies to similar fabrications like Shi'a reports. Moreover, if one stipulates 'adala, the doubt is irrelevant. (5) The difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths is not due to probability of the opposite but due to familiarity; for those acquainted with the report, tawatur is equally certain.

Key Terms
قياس مع الفارق (qiyās ma'a al-fāriq): An analogy where the branch (far') differs from the root (asl) in a relevant aspect, invalidating the comparison.
داعي (dā'ī): Motive or incentive that drives action or reporting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core difference (fariq) identified in the refutation of the first doubt?
A) The number of people involved
B) The presence of motive (dā'ī) in reporting but its absence in the meal example
C) The possibility of lying is greater in a crowd
D) The meal example is about eating, not speaking

Key Takeaway
The key insight: qiyas fails when the effective cause differs between the original and analogized cases; here, motive distinguishes tawatur from a shared meal.

Refutation of Doubt 2: The Whole vs. Its Parts
Refutation of the second doubt using whole-part distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ruling of the whole (kull) and the ruling of each part (kull wāḥid), and explain why the possibility of each individual lying does not entail the possibility of the whole lying.

Core Idea
The whole has its own ruling: collective lying is impossible even if each could lie.

The second doubt argues that since each individual can lie, the whole group could also lie. The Hanafi response exposes a logical fallacy: the collective has an effect that changes the ruling. We will explore the distinction between the possibility of each part and the impossibility of the whole, illustrated by the example of the impossibility of both opposites coexisting.

Guided Path
1
State the skeptics' claim
The skeptics argue: since each individual can lie, therefore the whole group can lie. This is an inference from part to whole.
This is a fallacy of composition.
2
Introduce the Hanafi counter-principle
The author states: the ruling of the whole (ḥukm al-kull) differs from the ruling of each individual (ḥukm kull wāḥid). The collective has an effect (athar) that is absent in the individual.
Example: each of two opposites is possible, but both together are impossible.
3
Analyze the logical illustration
The author gives the example of two opposites: each is individually possible, but it is impossible for both to be true together. Similarly, each reporter can lie, but it is impossible for all reports to be lies collectively (because truth would still emerge from some).
The key: the possibility of each part does not imply the possibility of the whole.
4
Apply to tawatur
Conclude: from the possibility of each individual lying, it does not follow that the whole group's report is a lie. The collective effect (tawatur) requires a different analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed refutation of each of the five doubts against tawatur. The author systematically responds: (1) The analogy to the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal is flawed because the motive for reporting (informing of known facts) is present in tawatur but lacking in the example (appetite for food is rarely shared). (2) The possibility of each individual lying does not extend to the whole when considered collectively, as the whole has a distinct ruling; he illustrates with the logical point that each of two opposites is possible individually but together they are impossible. (3) The possibility of contradictory reports is intrinsically impossible by custom, and even if possible in theory, custom establishes knowledge that the contradiction does not occur in reality. (4) The Jewish/Christian fabrications did not originate from tawatur; the initial transmitters were few and knowingly lying, and the later transmitters only conjectured, not knowing the truth; thus no genuine tawatur occurred. This also applies to similar fabrications like Shi'a reports. Moreover, if one stipulates 'adala, the doubt is irrelevant. (5) The difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths is not due to probability of the opposite but due to familiarity; for those acquainted with the report, tawatur is equally certain.

Key Terms
حكم الكل (ḥukm al-kull): The ruling of the whole, which may differ from the ruling of individual parts due to collective effect.
نقيضان (naqīḍān): Two logical opposites that cannot both be true simultaneously.

What does the Hanafi refutation say about the ruling of the whole compared to the parts?

Key Takeaway
The logical insight: possibility of parts does not entail possibility of the whole when the whole involves collective effects.

Refutation of Doubt 3: Contradictory Reports and Impossibility of Opposites
Refutation of the third doubt using custom and intrinsic impossibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the possibility of contradictory reports does not undermine tawatur, and evaluate the Hanafi argument that such contradiction is impossible by custom and intrinsically impossible.

Core Idea
Contradictory tawatur is impossible by custom and reason; custom yields knowledge.

The third doubt posits that if tawatur could be received for two contradictory reports, then both would be true, leading to a contradiction. The Hanafi response argues that tawatur of opposites is impossible both by custom (istihāla ʿādiyya) and in reality, and custom itself provides knowledge of this impossibility. We will analyze the nuanced interplay of intrinsic possibility, custom, and the production of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
State the skeptics' argument
The skeptics argue: if tawatur is accepted, then it is possible to have two contradictory reports both reaching tawatur, leading to contradictory certainties (impossible).
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Hanafi response: custom makes this impossible
The author asserts that tawatur of opposites is impossible by custom (ʿāda). It is not a real possibility because the conditions for tawatur (independence, motives, etc.) cannot be met for two directly contradictory statements.
Custom (ʿāda) here is a source of epistemological certainty.
3
Address the objection about intrinsic possibility
The hypothetical objector says: reporting opposites is intrinsically possible (mumkin bi al-dhāt), even if rare. The author responds that it is not intrinsically possible; it is intrinsically impossible because the nature of truth-telling custom makes it impossible for both sides to have independent mass transmission.
The argument relies on the idea that custom generates knowledge (ʿāda tufīd al-ʿilm).
4
Final refinement
Even if one insists on intrinsic possibility, the author adds that in reality (bi al-wāqiʿ), such a situation would entail impossibility because custom would force knowledge of the contradiction, nullifying the tawatur.
The distinction between possibility in the abstract and in reality is key.

Source Text

ولا يلزم من وجوب الأعم وجوب الأخص، نعم يلزم وجوب أحدهما لامتناع الارتفاع وإن كان كل ممكناً، ولا يلزم من أفراد شيء إمكان مطلقه فافهم وعن الدليل الثالث وهو لزوم اجتماع النقيضين عند إمكان جميع أخبار الجماعة بخبرين متناقضين إن تواتر النقيضين محال عادة فلا يلزم التناقض في الواقع، بل على تقدير خلاف الواقع فلا استحالة. فإن قلت : الأخبار بالمتناقضين وإن كان خلاف العادة لكنه ممكن بالذات لا يلزم من فرضه محال، ولو فرض ههنا لزم المحال وهو التناقض، فحصول العلم بالتواتر محال لأنه ما لزم المحال إلا منه قلت لا نسلم إمكانه بالذات، بل هو محال بالذات والعادة تفيد العلم باستحالته فتأمل. وأيضاً : الممكن بالذات لا يلزم منه محال بالنظر إلى ذاته، وأما بحسب الواقع فقد يستلزم محالاً بالذات، فهذا الإخبار وإن كان في نفسه ممكناً غير مستلزم للمحال لعدم وجوب العلم منه بالذات لكنه مستحيل في الواقع بالعادة، فيستلزم في الواقع المحال لإيجاب العادة العلم به فافهم وعن) الدليل (الرابع) وهو لزوم صدق إخبار اليهود والنصارى الكاذبة بيقين بأن تواترها ممنوع و(أن ابتداءه ليس كوسطه) بل لم يوجد في الابتداء مخبرون بعدد التواتر إنما هم بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا أمثال هذه الأقاويل وأخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين وهم أخبروا ظناً، بل علماً بالكذب شياطينهم الآخرين، فقد وجد في الوسط مبلغ التواتر، ثم إن كلهم ظانون غير مستيقنين، فلم يوجد التواتر، ومثل هذا إخبار الشيعة بالنص الجلي على إمامة أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأشجعين علي بن أبي طالب كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام، فإن بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا وكذبوا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، ثم أخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين حتى صار منقولاً فيهم، ثم إن الشبهة إنما ترد على من لا يشترط العدالة في التواتر وأما على الشارط فلا تتجه أصلاً فتدبر (وعن) الدليل (الخامس) وهو وجدان التفاوت بينه وبين البديهي الآخر الموجب لاحتمال النقيض أن غاية ما لزم من شبههم التفاوت في الجملة و لا نسلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت) فإنه قد يكون البعض خفياً عن بعض لعدم ملاحظة الأطراف حقها، أو لمصاحبة بعض الوسط دون بعض نعم إنها لا تتفاوت بمعنى احتمال أحدها النقيض دون الاخر ولزومه ههنا ممنوع، بل المتواتر والواحد نصف الاثنين لا يحتمل كل منهما النقيض ( ولو سلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت جلاء وخفاء أصلاً ( فالتفاوت) ههنا (للإنس وعدمه لا لكون أحدهما جلياً والآخر خفياً فتدبر
And as for the detailed answer to their doubts: concerning the first proof, which is their analogy to the impossibility of the whole gathering on one meal, (it is an analogy with a difference between the branch and the root regarding the existence of motive in the reports of the whole — and that is custom here, for the custom of a person is to report what he knows — and its absence there, i.e., in the thing being analogized to, for the motive to eat is appetite, and it is rare customarily that a crowd desires one meal. And concerning the second proof, which is the possibility of lying: the ruling of the whole (i.e., the group) may differ from the ruling of each individual, for the collective has an effect on the ruling, so it does not exist in its absence. Since their rulings differ, the possibility of each individual lying does not entail the possibility of all lying together. Then he gave an example of the difference of rulings: 'Do you not see that each of the two opposites is possible (due to its capability), unlike the whole which is impossible, not capable? If you say: if each of the opposites were not possible, then its opposite would be necessary, which is the negation of both, in itself; I say: the negation of the whole is more general and is not possible with the negation of both together; rather it may be by negating one without specifying, and the necessity of the general does not require the necessity of the specific. Yes, the necessity of one of them is required due to the impossibility of both being negated, even if each is possible, and the possibility of the parts does not imply the possibility of the whole. So understand. And concerning the third proof, which is the necessitation of the conjunction of opposites when two reports are contradictory: tawatur of opposites is customarily impossible, so no contradiction in reality results; rather, if it were contrary to reality, there is no impossibility. If you say: reporting opposites, though against custom, is intrinsically possible, and assuming it here would lead to the impossible, i.e., contradiction, so obtaining knowledge from tawatur is impossible because the impossible would only result from it; I say: We do not concede its intrinsic possibility; rather it is intrinsically impossible, and custom yields knowledge of its impossibility. So reflect. Also: the intrinsically possible does not necessarily entail impossibility in itself, but in reality it may entail impossibility. So this report, though in itself possible and not entailing impossibility due to knowledge not being necessary from it in itself, is in reality impossible by custom, so in reality it entails the impossible because custom necessitates knowledge from it. So understand. And concerning the fourth proof, which is the necessitation of believing the false reports of Jews and Christians: that their tawatur is denied, and its beginning is not like its middle. Rather, at the beginning there were not reporters reaching the number of tawatur; only some of their devils invented such sayings and informed their other devils, and they informed others by conjecture, nay with knowledge of the lie, until those at the middle reached the number of tawatur, yet all of them were conjecturing, not certain, so tawatur did not exist. An example is the Shi'a report of the explicit text on the Imamate of the Commander of the Faithful and the Imam of the brave, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family); some of their devils invented and lied against the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), then informed other devils until it became transmitted among them. Moreover, this doubt only arises against those who do not stipulate integrity ('adala) in tawatur; as for those who stipulate it, it is not applicable at all. So ponder. And concerning the fifth proof, which is the perceived difference between it and other self-evident truths leading to the possibility of the opposite: the utmost that follows from their doubt is difference in some respect, and we do not concede that sciences do not differ. For some may be hidden from some people due to not properly observing all aspects, or due to accompanying some intermediaries but not others. Indeed, they do not differ in the sense that one might admit the opposite while another does not; that it admits the opposite here is denied. Rather, both the mutawatir and 'one is half of two' do not admit the opposite. Even if one concedes that sciences do not differ at all in clarity and obscurity, the difference here is due to familiarity or unfamiliarity, not because one is clear and the other obscure. So ponder.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed refutation of each of the five doubts against tawatur. The author systematically responds: (1) The analogy to the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal is flawed because the motive for reporting (informing of known facts) is present in tawatur but lacking in the example (appetite for food is rarely shared). (2) The possibility of each individual lying does not extend to the whole when considered collectively, as the whole has a distinct ruling; he illustrates with the logical point that each of two opposites is possible individually but together they are impossible. (3) The possibility of contradictory reports is intrinsically impossible by custom, and even if possible in theory, custom establishes knowledge that the contradiction does not occur in reality. (4) The Jewish/Christian fabrications did not originate from tawatur; the initial transmitters were few and knowingly lying, and the later transmitters only conjectured, not knowing the truth; thus no genuine tawatur occurred. This also applies to similar fabrications like Shi'a reports. Moreover, if one stipulates 'adala, the doubt is irrelevant. (5) The difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths is not due to probability of the opposite but due to familiarity; for those acquainted with the report, tawatur is equally certain.

Key Terms
محال عادة (muḥāl ʿādatan): Impossible by custom; something that custom (ʿāda) shows never occurs, thus not a real possibility.
ممكن بالذات (mumkin bi al-dhāt): Intrinsically possible; something that abstractly could exist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi response address the objection that reporting opposites is intrinsically possible?
A) It denies intrinsic possibility and asserts it is intrinsically impossible
B) It accepts intrinsic possibility but says custom overrides it in reality
C) It argues that intrinsic possibility is irrelevant to tawatur
D) It says both A and B are used in the passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi refutation uses custom (ʿāda) as an epistemic source to establish impossibility, both intrinsically and in reality, against the reductio of contradictory tawatur.

Refutation of Doubt 4: Fabricated Reports (Jews, Christians, and Shi'a)
Refutation of the fourth doubt using origin analysis and ʿadāla condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze why fabricated mass reports like those from Jews, Christians, and Shi'a do not count as tawatur, and explain the role of the initial transmitters and the condition of ʿadāla in tawatur.

Core Idea
Tawatur requires an origin free from fabrication; 'adala condition excludes false reports.

The fourth doubt points to reports from Jews, Christians, and Shi'a that are widely transmitted but false. Could tawatur then be unreliable? The Hanafi response examines the genesis of these reports: they did not originate from a large independent group but from a few fabricators who then spread them. The later transmitters were merely speculating, not certain. Additionally, if one stipulates ʿadāla (integrity) as a condition for tawatur, such reports are automatically excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the skeptics' example
The skeptics cite false mass reports like Jewish/Christian fabrications or Shi'a claims of explicit text for Ali's imamate. These are widely transmitted but false.
The goal is to argue that tawatur can be false.
2
Analyze the beginning vs. middle
The Hanafi response distinguishes the beginning of transmission (al-ibtidā') from the middle (al-wasaṭ). At the start, only a few devils (shayāṭīn) invented the report; later, it spread, but the later transmitters were not sure of the truth—they merely passed on what they heard by conjecture (ẓann), not certainty.
True tawatur requires certainty in each level.
3
Apply the ʿadāla condition
The author notes that this doubt only applies to those who do not require ʿadāla (moral integrity) in the transmitters of tawatur. Those who require it (like some Hanafis) reject the report because the initial fabricators are not ʿādil.
The condition of ʿadāla is debated among scholars; here it provides an additional refutation.
4
Conclude: no tawatur occurred
Thus, the reported examples do not constitute genuine tawatur because either the origin lacks mass independent transmission, or the transmitters lack certainty, or they lack ʿadāla. So the doubt does not undermine true tawatur.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed refutation of each of the five doubts against tawatur. The author systematically responds: (1) The analogy to the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal is flawed because the motive for reporting (informing of known facts) is present in tawatur but lacking in the example (appetite for food is rarely shared). (2) The possibility of each individual lying does not extend to the whole when considered collectively, as the whole has a distinct ruling; he illustrates with the logical point that each of two opposites is possible individually but together they are impossible. (4) The Jewish/Christian fabrications did not originate from tawatur; the initial transmitters were few and knowingly lying, and the later transmitters only conjectured, not knowing the truth; thus no genuine tawatur occurred. This also applies to similar fabrications like Shi'a reports. Moreover, if one stipulates 'adala, the doubt is irrelevant. (5) The difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths is not due to probability of the opposite but due to familiarity; for those acquainted with the report, tawatur is equally certain.

Key Terms
ابتداء (ibtidā’): The beginning of transmission; the origin of the report.
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The middle of the transmission chain; the later transmitters who passed on the report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Shi'a reports of explicit text for Ali's imamate not constitute tawatur?
A) They are contradicted by Sunni reports
B) They were invented by a few and then spread by conjecture
C) The number of transmitters is too small
D) They are not about legal rulings

Key Takeaway
Genuine tawatur requires a mass, truthful, and certain transmission at every stage; fabricated mass reports fail at the origin or in certitude.

Refutation of Doubt 5: Difference in Clarity Between Tawatur and Basic Self-Evident Truths
Refutation of the fifth doubt by distinguishing clarity from certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the apparent difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths (like 'one is half of two') does not undermine the epistemic validity of tawatur, and identify the role of familiarity (uns) in this difference.

Core Idea
Tawatur gives certainty equal to basic truths; difference is due to familiarity, not probability.

The fifth doubt points out that tawatur does not produce the same immediate clarity as basic self-evident truths like 'one is half of two'. This perceived difference might suggest that tawatur allows for the possibility of the opposite. The Hanafi response argues that sciences (ʿulūm) can differ in clarity for individuals due to familiarity (uns) or lack of complete observation, but they do not differ in the sense that one admits the opposite while the other does not. Tawatur, like basic truths, does not admit the opposite.

Guided Path
1
State the skeptics' claim
The skeptics observe that tawatur feels less certain than basic self-evident truths like 'one is half of two'. This difference in clarity might imply that tawatur is not fully certain.
This is an objection from subjective perception.
2
Hanafi response: difference exists, but not in probability of opposite
The author concedes that sciences (ʿulūm) can differ in clarity (jalāʾ) and obscurity (khafāʾ) between individuals. Some may find tawatur less clear due to not examining all aspects or due to lack of familiarity with the intermediaries.
But this does not mean tawatur admits the opposite; it is as certain as basic truths to those who are familiar.
3
Agreement on core: no opposite possibility
The author emphasizes that both tawatur and basic truths do not admit the opposite (lā yaḥtamil al-naqīḍ). The difference is not in the type of certainty but in the ease of perception.
Example: a mathematician finds '1+1=2' self-evident; a layperson might need explanation. Yet both are equally certain.
4
Final: differences due to familiarity (uns)
If one insists that sciences do not differ at all in clarity, then the difference here is due to familiarity with the report (uns) or lack thereof, not because one is more probable than the other.
Thus, the doubt is based on a misunderstanding of the nature of certainty.

Source Text

أن يخبر بما يعلم (وعدمه) أي عدم الداعي (ثمة) أي في المقيس عليه، فإن الداعي إلى الأكل الاشتهاء، وقلما يكون اشتهاء الجماعة طعاماً واحداً عادة (وعن) الدليل (الثاني) وهو جواز الكذب قد يخالف حكم (الكل) أي المجموع) (حكم كل) أي كل واحد واحد (فللاجتماع أثر في الحكم فلا يوجد عند عدمه، وإذا كان حكماهما متخالفين فلا يلزم من جواز كذب كل جواز كذب الجميع، ثم مثل لافتراق الحكمين بقوله ألا ترى أن كلاً النقيضين مقدور) لإمكانه (بخلاف الكل فإنه مستحيل غير مقدور فإن قلت : لو كان كل النقيضين غير ممكن لوجب نقيضه وهو رفعهما، أنه بالذات، قلت: رفع الكل أعم مع ممتنع من رفعهما معاً، بل هو قد يكون برفع واحد لا بعينه ولا يلزم من وجوب الأعم وجوب الأخص، نعم يلزم وجوب أحدهما لامتناع الارتفاع وإن كان كل ممكناً، ولا يلزم من أفراد شيء إمكان مطلقه فافهم وعن الدليل الثالث وهو لزوم اجتماع النقيضين عند إمكان جميع أخبار الجماعة بخبرين متناقضين إن تواتر النقيضين محال عادة فلا يلزم التناقض في الواقع، بل على تقدير خلاف الواقع فلا استحالة. فإن قلت : الأخبار بالمتناقضين وإن كان خلاف العادة لكنه ممكن بالذات لا يلزم من فرضه محال، ولو فرض ههنا لزم المحال وهو التناقض، فحصول العلم بالتواتر محال لأنه ما لزم المحال إلا منه قلت لا نسلم إمكانه بالذات، بل هو محال بالذات والعادة تفيد العلم باستحالته فتأمل. وأيضاً : الممكن بالذات لا يلزم منه محال بالنظر إلى ذاته، وأما بحسب الواقع فقد يستلزم محالاً بالذات، فهذا الإخبار وإن كان في نفسه ممكناً غير مستلزم للمحال لعدم وجوب العلم منه بالذات لكنه مستحيل في الواقع بالعادة، فيستلزم في الواقع المحال لإيجاب العادة العلم به فافهم وعن) الدليل (الرابع) وهو لزوم صدق إخبار اليهود والنصارى الكاذبة بيقين بأن تواترها ممنوع و(أن ابتداءه ليس كوسطه) بل لم يوجد في الابتداء مخبرون بعدد التواتر إنما هم بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا أمثال هذه الأقاويل وأخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين وهم أخبروا ظناً، بل علماً بالكذب شياطينهم الآخرين، فقد وجد في الوسط مبلغ التواتر، ثم إن كلهم ظانون غير مستيقنين، فلم يوجد التواتر، ومثل هذا إخبار الشيعة بالنص الجلي على إمامة أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأشجعين علي بن أبي طالب كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام، فإن بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا وكذبوا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، ثم أخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين حتى صار منقولاً فيهم، ثم إن الشبهة إنما ترد على من لا يشترط العدالة في التواتر وأما على الشارط فلا تتجه أصلاً فتدبر (وعن) الدليل (الخامس) وهو وجدان التفاوت بينه وبين البديهي الآخر الموجب لاحتمال النقيض أن غاية ما لزم من شبههم التفاوت في الجملة و لا نسلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت) فإنه قد يكون البعض خفياً عن بعض لعدم ملاحظة الأطراف حقها، أو لمصاحبة بعض الوسط دون بعض نعم إنها لا تتفاوت بمعنى احتمال أحدها النقيض دون الاخر ولزومه ههنا ممنوع، بل المتواتر والواحد نصف الاثنين لا يحتمل كل منهما النقيض ( ولو سلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت جلاء وخفاء أصلاً ( فالتفاوت) ههنا (للإنس وعدمه لا لكون أحدهما جلياً والآخر خفياً فتدبر
And as for the detailed answer to their doubts: concerning the first proof, which is their analogy to the impossibility of the whole gathering on one meal, (it is an analogy with a difference between the branch and the root regarding the existence of motive in the reports of the whole — and that is custom here, for the custom of a person is to report what he knows — and its absence there, i.e., in the thing being analogized to, for the motive to eat is appetite, and it is rare customarily that a crowd desires one meal. And concerning the second proof, which is the possibility of lying: the ruling of the whole (i.e., the group) may differ from the ruling of each individual, for the collective has an effect on the ruling, so it does not exist in its absence. Since their rulings differ, the possibility of each individual lying does not entail the possibility of all lying together. Then he gave an example of the difference of rulings: 'Do you not see that each of the two opposites is possible (due to its capability), unlike the whole which is impossible, not capable? If you say: if each of the opposites were not possible, then its opposite would be necessary, which is the negation of both, in itself; I say: the negation of the whole is more general and is not possible with the negation of both together; rather it may be by negating one without specifying, and the necessity of the general does not require the necessity of the specific. Yes, the necessity of one of them is required due to the impossibility of both being negated, even if each is possible, and the possibility of the parts does not imply the possibility of the whole. So understand. And concerning the third proof, which is the necessitation of the conjunction of opposites when two reports are contradictory: tawatur of opposites is customarily impossible, so no contradiction in reality results; rather, if it were contrary to reality, there is no impossibility. If you say: reporting opposites, though against custom, is intrinsically possible, and assuming it here would lead to the impossible, i.e., contradiction, so obtaining knowledge from tawatur is impossible because the impossible would only result from it; I say: We do not concede its intrinsic possibility; rather it is intrinsically impossible, and custom yields knowledge of its impossibility. So reflect. Also: the intrinsically possible does not necessarily entail impossibility in itself, but in reality it may entail impossibility. So this report, though in itself possible and not entailing impossibility due to knowledge not being necessary from it in itself, is in reality impossible by custom, so in reality it entails the impossible because custom necessitates knowledge from it. So understand. And concerning the fourth proof, which is the necessitation of believing the false reports of Jews and Christians: that their tawatur is denied, and its beginning is not like its middle. Rather, at the beginning there were not reporters reaching the number of tawatur; only some of their devils invented such sayings and informed their other devils, and they informed others by conjecture, nay with knowledge of the lie, until those at the middle reached the number of tawatur, yet all of them were conjecturing, not certain, so tawatur did not exist. An example is the Shi'a report of the explicit text on the Imamate of the Commander of the Faithful and the Imam of the brave, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family); some of their devils invented and lied against the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), then informed other devils until it became transmitted among them. Moreover, this doubt only arises against those who do not stipulate integrity ('adala) in tawatur; as for those who stipulate it, it is not applicable at all. So ponder. And concerning the fifth proof, which is the perceived difference between it and other self-evident truths leading to the possibility of the opposite: the utmost that follows from their doubt is difference in some respect, and we do not concede that sciences do not differ. For some may be hidden from some people due to not properly observing all aspects, or due to accompanying some intermediaries but not others. Indeed, they do not differ in the sense that one might admit the opposite while another does not; that it admits the opposite here is denied. Rather, both the mutawatir and 'one is half of two' do not admit the opposite. Even if one concedes that sciences do not differ at all in clarity and obscurity, the difference here is due to familiarity or unfamiliarity, not because one is clear and the other obscure. So ponder.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed refutation of each of the five doubts against tawatur. The author systematically responds: (1) The analogy to the impossibility of a crowd sharing one meal is flawed because the motive for reporting (informing of known facts) is present in tawatur but lacking in the example (appetite for food is rarely shared). (2) The possibility of each individual lying does not extend to the whole when considered collectively, as the whole has a distinct ruling; he illustrates with the logical point that each of two opposites is possible individually but together they are impossible. (3) The possibility of contradictory reports is intrinsically impossible by custom, and even if possible in theory, custom establishes knowledge that the contradiction does not occur in reality. (4) The Jewish/Christian fabrications did not originate from tawatur; the initial transmitters were few and knowingly lying, and the later transmitters only conjectured, not knowing the truth; thus no genuine tawatur occurred. This also applies to similar fabrications like Shi'a reports. Moreover, if one stipulates 'adala, the doubt is irrelevant. (5) The difference in certainty between tawatur and basic self-evident truths is not due to probability of the opposite but due to familiarity; for those acquainted with the report, tawatur is equally certain.

Key Terms
بديهي (badīhī): Self-evident truth that requires no proof.
أنس (uns): Familiarity; the state of being accustomed to something, which affects clarity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why might some people find tawatur less clear than basic self-evident truths?
A) Tawatur is inherently less certain
B) They lack familiarity with the evidence or have not examined all aspects
C) The skeptics are correct
D) The truth of tawatur is different

Key Takeaway
Subjective clarity varies, but epistemic certainty of tawatur is on par with basic self-evident truths; neither admits the opposite.

The Minimum Number for Tawatur: A Usul Dispute on Qiyas and Custom
Discusses three opinions on the minimum number for tawatur using qiyas and rebuts a Mu'tazili principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on the minimum number for tawatur, apply the Hanafi critique of the qiyas arguments, and evaluate the role of custom versus analogy in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The minimum number for tawatur is not fixed by analogy; it is determined by custom and the ritual nature of tazkiyah.

This passage dives into a classic usul al-fiqh dispute: what is the minimum number of narrators needed for a report to be mutawatir (mass-transmitted, yielding certainty)? Three positions are debated: four, by analogy to zina witnesses; five, by analogy to li'an; and a rejection of any fixed number by al-Qadi al-Baqillani, who argues that if four sufficed, tazkiyah would be unnecessary. The Hanafi response reveals a deeper methodological principle: tazkiyah is a ritual requirement (ta'abbudi), not a rational one, and the effect of a number varies with context. This lesson unpacks the arguments, the qiyas, and the Hanafi turn to custom (ʿādah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the three views on the minimum number for tawatur as presented: four (qiyas to zina), five (qiyas to li'an), and Baqillani's denial of four.
Note that the Hanafi position is not explicitly given but is implied by the critique.
2
Analyze the qiyas arguments
For each view, identify the asl (original case), far' (new case), and illah (effective cause). For four: asl = zina witnesses, illah = removing doubt in a grave matter. For five: asl = li'an testimonies, illah = repeated testimony yields certainty.
The author does not accept these qiyas as valid.
3
Examine Baqillani's objection and Hanafi response
Baqillani: if four give certainty, then zina witnesses would not need tazkiyah. Hanafi response: tazkiyah is a ritual requirement, not for certainty; even 70,000 witnesses need tazkiyah. The Prophet's hadith about the woman who confessed supports this.
The Hanafi response shows that tazkiyah is ta'abbudi, not connected to certainty.
4
Synthesize the Hanafi position on custom
The Hanafi school holds that the number for tawatur is not fixed by qiyas but by custom (ʿādah) — the number that prevents collusion under normal circumstances. This rejects the Mu'tazili principle that the same number always yields knowledge.
Custom varies; hence no fixed number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف في أقل العدد المشروط في التواتر (فقيل : أربعة قياساً على شهود الزنا) فإنه أمر عظيم وقد أمرنا بالدرء بالشبهات ولا شك أن غير المتواتر مما فيه شبهة، فعلم أن الأربعة مفيدة للقطع (وقيل) ذلك العدد (خمسة قياساً على اللعان) فإنه خمس شهادات، وإذا قبل إخبار رجل خمس مرات وأفاد اليقين فإخبار خمسة رجال بالطريق الأولى (وقطع القاضي) الباقلاني بنفي الأربعة، إذ لو (أفاد خبر الأربعة اليقين لم تحتج شهود الزنا إلى التزكية) لأن العدالة غير معتبرة في التواتر وفيه تأمل ويرد عليه وروداً ظاهراً أن التزكية في الشهادة أمر تعبدي لا لتحصيل اليقين، ألا ترى أن سبعين ألفاً لو شهدوا بالزنا لوجب التزكية أيضاً، لذا لو حصل اليقين لا عن شهود لم يجب الحد ولذا لم يحدّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم تلك المرأة وقال: «لو رجمت من غير شهود لرجمت هذه» رواه البخاري فإن قلت غاية ما لزم من دليله عدم إفادة الأربعة في الزنا، ولا يلزم منه عدم الإفادة في صورة أخرى قال : (وذلك) أي دليل القاضي بناء على ما قاله هو ووافقه أبو الحسين) من المعتزلة أن كل عدد أفاد علماً بواقعة لشخص فمثله أي مثل هذا العدد يفيد العلم) (بغير تلك الواقعة لشخص آخر) فلو كان الأربعة مفيداً للعلم في الواقعة لأفاد في الزنا، فلا يحتاج إلى التزكية (وفيه وما فيه) فإنه باطل بالضرورة، كيف والإفادة تختلف باختلاف المخبر عنه والمخبرين وغير ذلك، وربما يؤوّل بأن كل عدد أفاد علماً بواقعة فمثل هذا العدد في الأحوال العارضة
Then there is disagreement on the minimum number required for tawatur. It was said: four, by analogy to the witnesses for zina, for it is a grave matter and we have been commanded to repel [punishments] by doubts, and there is no doubt that non-mutawatir involves doubt; so it is known that four produce certainty. And it was said: that number is five, by analogy to li'an, for it is five testimonies, and if the report of a man five times is accepted and produces certainty, then the report of five men is all the more apt. And al-Qadi al-Baqillani decisively denied four, for if the report of four produces certainty, then the witnesses for zina would not need tazkiyah (credibility assessment), because justice is not considered in tawatur. In it there is reflection, and it is refuted obviously: tazkiyah in testimony is a ritual requirement, not for obtaining certainty. Do you not see that even if seventy thousand testified to zina, tazkiyah would be required? Therefore, if certainty is attained without witnesses, the hadd punishment is not obligatory. For this reason the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) did not stone that woman and said: 'If I were to stone without witnesses, I would have stoned this one' – narrated by al-Bukhari. If you say: The utmost that follows from his proof is that four do not suffice in zina, and it does not follow that they do not suffice in another situation. He said: That is, the proof of al-Qadi is based on what he and Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili said: that any number that gives knowledge of an event for a person, the same number gives knowledge of a different event for another person. So if four give knowledge in one event, they would give knowledge in zina, thus tazkiyah would not be needed. But there is much in it, for it is false necessarily – how can it be? The effect differs according to the difference of the reported matter, the reporters, and other factors. Perhaps it is interpreted as: any number that gives knowledge of an event, the same number under similar accidental conditions [gives knowledge].
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents the classical debate on the minimum number of narrators required for a report to be mutawatir. Three positions are discussed: (1) Four, by analogy to the four witnesses required for zina (adultery) – since zina is a serious matter and we are commanded to avoid punishment through doubts, and non-mutawatir reports involve doubt, therefore a number that removes doubt (four) is deemed sufficient for certainty. (2) Five, by analogy to li'an (mutual imprecation) which involves five testimonies (the husband swears five times). If a single man's repeated testimony (five times) yields certainty, then five men testifying is even stronger. (3) Al-Qadi al-Baqillani argued that four cannot be the minimum because if four were sufficient for certainty, then the four witnesses in zina would not need tazkiyah (character screening) – since tawatur does not require justice of narrators. The author refutes this by pointing out that tazkiyah is a purely ritual requirement (ta'abbudi) not based on securing certainty, as even seventy thousand witnesses would still require tazkiyah. The proof is that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not stone a woman who confessed without witnesses, saying he would only stone her with witnesses. Al-Baqillani's argument relies on a principle of the Mu'tazila (Abu al-Husayn) that if a number gives knowledge in one case, it does so in another, but the author rejects this as false and points out that the effect of a number varies with the subject, the reporters, and other circumstances. The Hanafi position, though not explicitly stated here, tends towards the view that the number is not fixed by textual analogy but is determined by custom (as stated earlier in the conditions lesson).

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Mass transmission of a report that yields certainty; the minimum number is disputed.
قياس (qiyās): Analogy used to determine the minimum number: from zina (four) and li'an (five).
تزكية (tazkiyah): Credibility screening of witnesses; required even if certainty is achieved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the main argument of al-Qadi al-Baqillani against the number four for tawatur?
A) Four is too few to prevent collusion
B) If four produce certainty, then zina witnesses would not need tazkiyah
C) Four is only for zina, not for other reports
D) The Prophet used five witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not fix a specific number for tawatur by qiyas; the number is determined by customary certainty and the ritual nature of tazkiyah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
