Objection on Universal Possibility in Tawatur Ma'nawi
Logical argument defending tawatur ma'nawi against an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logical objection against tawatur ma'nawi and analyze the Hanafi response using the universal-particular distinction.

Core Idea
A universal meaning can be certain even if each particular report is possibly false.

In this lesson, we examine a sophisticated objection raised against the concept of tawatur ma'nawi. The objection uses a logical premise about universals and particulars to argue that the common meaning cannot be certain. The Hanafi response leverages the same logical framework to defend tawatur ma'nawi. Understanding this argument is key to grasping how Hanafi usul grounds the authority of mass-transmitted meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection's premise
Understand that the objection assumes: if each individual of a universal can be nonexistent individually and collectively, then the universal itself is possibly nonexistent.
This premise is presented as a necessary logical consequence.
2
Understand the consequence of denying the premise
If the universal were necessarily existent despite individual nonexistence, it would imply Platonic ideals (muthul Aflatuniyya), which is considered problematic.
The text mentions this to show the absurdity of the alternative.
3
Apply the premise to tawatur ma'nawi
Each report (khabar wahid) in tawatur ma'nawi is possibly false individually, and there is no necessary relation between them that would make the falsity of one imply the truth of another.
The text explicitly states 'no connection between them such that the negation of one entails the existence of another'.
4
Conclude the validity of tawatur ma'nawi
Therefore, the universal meaning derived from these reports can be known with certainty despite the potential falsity of each individual report.
This is the Hanafi position defended in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول : ههنا إشكال موقوف على مقدمة وهي : أن الكلي إذا كان كل واحد من أفراده جائز العدم انفراداً ، ومعاً كان هذا الكلي (أيضاً جائز الانتفاء، وإلا) يكن جائز لعدم لزم جواز المثل (الأفلاطونية وهي الماهيات الموجودة معراة الملازمة أنه إذا جاز وجود الكلي مع انتفاء جميع الأفراد بدلاً ومعاً فقد جاز وجود الكلي، من غير تشخص وهي المثل، وإذا تمهد هذا فنقول ههنا كذلك أي في متواتر المعنى يجوز انتفاء كل خبر انفراداً ومعاً (أما) انتفاؤه (انفراداً فالبفرض) لأنه قد فرض أن كلاً منها آحاد جائز العدم والكذب لعدم اليقين (وأما) انتفاؤها (معاً فلأنه لا علاقة بينها بحيث يلزم من انتفاء واحد منها وجود الآخر لأن هذا إنما يكون في المتنافيين ولا تنافي ،ههنا ثم هذا يجري في المتواتر لفظاً أيضاً، لأنه لا علاقة بين الأخبارات يوجب انتفاء واحد تحقق الآخر، ولك أن تمنع اختصاص
I say: Here is an objection dependent on a premise: that if every individual of a universal is possibly nonexistent individually and collectively, then that universal is also possibly nonexistent; otherwise, if not, then the Platonic ideal would be necessary (the essences existing stripped of individuation). If it is possible for the universal to exist while all individuals are nonexistent separately and together, then the universal can exist without particularization, which are the ideals. Having established this, we say: the same applies here—in meaning-based tawatur, it is possible for each report to be false individually and collectively. As for individually, it is by assumption because each is a solitary report, possibly false. As for collectively, because there is no connection between them such that the negation of one entails the existence of another; that only occurs between contradictories, and there is no contradiction here. The same applies to word-for-word tawatur, because there is no connection between reports that would make the negation of one necessitate the truth of another. But you may deny the specific nature...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: if each individual report in tawatur ma'nawi could be false, how can the universal meaning be certain? The response uses a logical premise: for a universal (like 'generosity'), if each particular instance could be nonexistent, it does not necessarily mean the universal itself is nonexistent. This is similar to Platonic ideals, where a universal can exist without every particular being actualized. In tawatur ma'nawi, there is no necessary mutual relation between the reports; the falsity of one does not imply the truth of another. Therefore, the collective agreement on a common meaning gives certainty despite the possibility of each being false individually. The objection also applies to tawatur lafzi, but the same resolution works. The text is cut off but indicates the argument continues about distinguishing between cases.

Key Terms
الكلي (al-kulli): The universal attribute or meaning derived from multiple reports (e.g., generosity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The objection against tawatur ma'nawi assumes that if each particular report could be false, then the universal meaning cannot be known. How does the author respond?
A) By requiring that each report be mutawatir individually
B) By stating that the universal can exist without all particulars being true
C) By denying that the reports are solitary
D) By invoking the authority of the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends tawatur ma'nawi using the logical principle that a universal can be certain even if every particular report is possibly false.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Validity of Qiyas in Matters of Widespread Affliction
Refuting an objection about qiyas in 'umum al-balwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on the use of qiyas in matters of 'umum al-balwa and construct a counter-argument against the objection that qiyas should yield to a report.

Core Idea
In matters of widespread affliction, analogy remains valid unless a report is actually widespread—absence of transmission disproves the report's authenticity.

This passage tackles a key dispute in Hanafi usul: can qiyas be used when a matter is so common that a ruling should have been known? The opponent argues that if qiyas is accepted despite being weaker than a report, the report itself should be accepted. The Hanafi response reveals a deeper principle: the lack of widespread transmission of a report in such a case indicates it is not authentic, so qiyas remains operative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's objection
Find the line where the opponent argues that accepting qiyas (which is inferior to a report) in matters of 'umum al-balwa implies that the report should be accepted even more readily.
Look for the phrase: 'إذا قبل ما هو دون الخبر فلأن يقبل هو فيه أولى'.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
Locate the Hanafi rebuttal: they deny that a genuine report exists in such matters because custom dictates that if a prophetic ruling were truly revealed, it would have been widely transmitted.
The key phrase: 'لا نسلم أنه الخبر فيما عم به البلوى'.
3
Analyze the role of custom in determining report authenticity
Understand how 'umum al-balwa triggers a presumption: the widespread occurrence of the matter would have necessitated transmission of any relevant report. Its absence proves the report is not authentic.
The text says: 'العادة قاضية بنقله وإشاعته بعد العلم به فيما عم به البلوى'.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Consider a fiqh example like impurity from a wound. Hanafis use qiyas to derive the ruling, while opposing schools may require an explicit report. The practical difference hinges on whether the report is considered authentic.
The text mentions 'خروج النجاسة من غير السبيلين' as an example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح، لأنه دون الرجل قلما يفصد إلا عند عروض المرض والقهقهة في الصلاة لا تكاد توجد إلا نادراً من ليس له تثبت لأمر الصلاة وقد يقال : العذر في القهقهة القهقهة صحيح، وأما في الفصد فلا ليس الكلام في خصوص الفصد بل فيما يخرج من غير السبيلين والناس يبتلون به كثيراً ولا يذهب عليك أن خروج النجاسة من غير السبيلين غير معتاد وإنما يبتلى به صاحب المرض فلا يشتد الحاجة على أنه إن سلم أنه فيما يتكرر به البلوى لكن من أين علم أنه مخالف لعمل الأكثر حتى يكون من الباب، وعلى التنزل فالانتقاض به ثابت بالقياس وهو مقبول فيما يتكرر البلوى والاستدلال بالخبر إلزام فافهم (و) قالوا :(ثالثاً: قبل فيه أي فيما عم البلوى (القياس و) الحال إنه هو دونه فإذا قبل ما هو دون الخبر فلأن يقبل هو فيه أولى (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه الخبر فيما عم به البلوى، بل القياس يوجب الظن بخلاف خبر الواحد فيما تعم به البلوى إلا إذا اشتهر أو لم يخالف) عملهم (وقد يقال في تقرير كلامهم (عموم البلوى يقتضي عادة سبق معرفة حكمه على القياس وإذا لم يعملوا بمقتضى القياس علم أن الحكم فيه ليس ما أفاد القياس، فلا يفيد القياس الظن فيه أصلاً (أقول) لا نسلم أن قضاء العادة معرفة الحكم القياسي من قبل بل لا تكليف إلا بعد ظهور الرأي بخلاف الخبر فإنه يتوجه التكليف من حين نزوله (فلا حاجة إلى معرفة الحكم قبله اكتفاء بالإباحة (الأصلية واطلاع أهل الابتلاء الذين هم قبل القائس غير لازم كما قال عليه وآله السلام : رب حامل فقه غير فقيه» رواه البخاري، وأما الخبر فالعادة قاضية بنقله وإشاعته بعد العلم به فيما عم به البلوى فإذا لم يشع فيهم وعملوا بخلافه علم أنه غير صالح للاحتجاج فافهم .
It is valid because it is less than a man. He rarely undergoes phlebotomy except when illness occurs, and laughter during prayer is rarely found except from one who lacks steadfastness in prayer. It may be said: The excuse for laughter is valid, but for phlebotomy it is not. The discussion is not specifically about phlebotomy but about what exits from other than the two passages, and people are frequently afflicted by that. Do not be unaware that the exit of impurity from other than the two passages is not habitual; only the sick person is afflicted by it, so the need is not severe. Even if it is conceded that it is a matter of repeated affliction, from where is it known that it contradicts the practice of the majority so that it falls under this category? At best, the rebuttal is established by analogy, and analogy is acceptable in matters of repeated affliction, while inference from the report is conclusive. Understand. (And they said) Thirdly: Analogy was accepted in matters of widespread affliction, even though it is inferior to report. So if what is inferior to report is accepted, then the report itself should be accepted more readily. (We say) We do not concede that it is a report in matters of widespread affliction. Rather, analogy produces probability contrary to the single report in matters of widespread affliction unless it has become widespread or does not contradict their practice. (It may be said in framing their argument) Widespread affliction customarily implies that knowledge of its ruling preceded analogy. If they did not act according to the result of the analogy, it is known that the ruling is not what analogy indicated, so analogy does not produce probability in it at all. (I say) We do not concede that custom necessitates prior knowledge of the ruling by analogy. Rather, there is no obligation except after the opinion appears, unlike the report, for obligation attaches from the time of its revelation. There is no need for prior knowledge of the ruling, being content with the original permissibility. The awareness of the afflicted people who are prior to the analogist is not necessary, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Many a carrier of understanding is not understanding.' Narrated by Bukhari. As for the report, custom necessitates its transmission and dissemination after it is known in matters of widespread affliction. So if it is not disseminated among them and they act contrary to it, it is known that it is not valid for argument. Understand.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is part of a debate about whether analogy (qiyas) can be used to refute a report (khabar) in matters of widespread affliction (umum al-balwa). The author begins by addressing an objection: it is argued that if a report is accepted in general, then in cases of widespread affliction, a report would have been widely known, so failing to act on it indicates the report is not genuine. The author counters that analogy is still valid in such cases unless the report is actually widespread or does not contradict the practice of the people. The core argument is that widespread affliction would normally necessitate the transmission of a report if it were true; its absence indicates the report is not authentic. The author concludes that analogy does not provide true probability here because custom indicates that the ruling would have been known. The final note emphasizes that the report's lack of dissemination shows it is not suitable for argumentation. The Hanafi position is that qiyas is valid when the report is not widely known and when the ruling is not contradicted by practice.

Key Terms
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A matter that afflicts the general public frequently, such that the ruling would normally be widely known.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning to derive a ruling based on an effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when does a report override analogy in matters of widespread affliction?
A) Never; analogy always prevails.
B) Only when the report has become widespread or does not contradict the practice of the people.
C) Always; the report is always superior.
D) Only if the report is mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas remains operative in matters of 'umum al-balwa unless a report is actually widespread; the lack of transmission undermines the report's authenticity.

Critiquing Rational Arguments for Khabar al-Wahid
Critiquing rational arguments for acting on khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate three rational arguments for obligating khabar al-wahid and apply the Hanafi critique that such obligation is based on Shari'ah, not reason alone.

Core Idea
Rational arguments alone cannot obligate acting on khabar al-wahid; only Shari'ah establishes that obligation.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents and refutes three rational arguments for the obligation of acting on single-narrator reports. The arguments—harm avoidance, precaution, and the danger of events being devoid of rulings—are each shown to be insufficient. The Hanafi position is that such obligation is based on revelation, not reason. We will examine each argument and its rebuttal to understand how Hanafi usul delimits the role of reason in establishing legal duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rational arguments
List the three arguments presented: (1) harm avoidance, (2) precaution, (3) necessity (khalw al-waqai). Understand the premise and conclusion of each.
The arguments are attributed to 'those who hold to obligation by reason'—likely referring to certain Mu'tazila or rationalist thinkers.
2
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal for each argument
For each argument, extract the key critique: (1) Harm avoidance shows preference (awla) not obligation; (2) Precaution is not absolutely obligatory—even day of doubt fasting is not required; (3) The danger of events having no rulings is solved by original permissibility (ibahah asliyyah) or by consensus and analogy.
The commentator also notes that reason does not deem it impossible for events to lack rulings; only Shari'ah fills gaps.
3
Understand the epistemological principle
The passage establishes a core usul principle: rational obligation (wujub aqli) is not recognized as a source of legal duty; legal obligation (wujub shar'i) must come from revealed sources. Rational arguments may indicate preference or justification but not binding requirement.
This aligns with the Hanafi view that reason alone cannot create a hukm taklifi without a textual basis.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a situation where a single trustworthy person reports that a certain food is harmful. According to the rational argument, one must avoid it. Apply the Hanafi critique: avoiding is recommended (preferential) but not obligatory unless supported by a Shari'ah evidence (e.g., a hadith commanding preservation of life).
This illustrates the distinction between 'awla' and 'wajib' in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المتشبثون بوجوب التعبد به بالعقل فمنهم من قال : وجوب الاجتناب عن المضار معلوم عقلاً، وهذا أصل كلي يعتقده الخاصة والعامة والعمل بالظن في تفاصيل مقطوع الأصل واجب عقلاً، كأخبار واحد بمضرة طعام وسقوط حائط) فإنه واجب القبول، وقول الرسول مبين للمضار والمنافع، فإن ظن به وجب العمل قطعاً (وهو مبني على حكم العقل بالوجوب، وقد مر من قبل فلا ينتهض حجة ممن لا يقول به على أن الوجوب) وجوب العمل بالظن في تفاصيل مقطوع الأصل عقلاً ممنوع (بل) هذا العمل (أولى) عقلاً، نعم : وجوب هذا الأمر ثابت شرعاً (ومنهم من استدل أولاً أن صدقه مظنون) ضرورة (فيجب) العمل به احتياطاً، يمنع كون الاحتياط واجباً) مطلقاً ألا ترى لم يجب الصوم بالشك) في رؤية هلال رمضان الشريف، ولا يذهب عليك أنه ما ادعى وجوب الاحتياط مطلقاً، بل الاحتياط في المظنون ولا شك فيه وأما عدم وجوب صوم يوم الشك فلعدم الظن هناك، فالأحرى منع كون الاحتياط واجباً عقلاً بل إنما يجب فيما يجب سمعاً (و) استدل (ثانياً: لو لم يجب العمل بخبر الواحد (الخلت الوقائع أكثرها ( عن الأحكام ، لأن القرآن والمتواتر) من السنة (لا يفيان بجميع الوقائع بل ما يفيان به أقل القليل والجواب منع الملازمة، لأن حكم عند عدم الدليل عدم الحكم بالشرع وهذا يشتمل جميع الوقائع الخالية عن القطع إذ هو الدليل فيتوقف أو يعمل بالإباحة الأصلية على اختلاف القولين، كما قد مر ، والأظهر الإباحة فيما لا دليل فيه بالشرع، فلم تخل الوقائع (أقول : على أن في تشريع الإجماع والقياس الوفاء بالأكثر) فلا خلل إلا في أقل القليل وفي كونهما وافيين تأمل أما الإجماع فلكونه في وقائع معدودة، وأما القياس فلأنه لا بد له من الأصل المقيس عليه وهو لا يكون إلا من القرآن أو المتواتر من السنة والإجماع وهي غير كافية فتدبر ، وقد يمنع بطلان التالي عقلاً) فإن استحالة خلو الوقائع عن الأحكام لا تظهر عند العقل وإنما هي بالشرع لكن الاستحالة تظهر بالتشبث بالحسن والقبح العقليين في الأفعال، فإنهما يستلزمان تعلق الحكم بها من الشارع كما هو التحقيق عند محققي مشايخنا فتأمل. الروافض ومن وافقهم قالوا : (أولاً) التعبد بخبر الواحد اتباع الظن، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْم [الإسراء : ٣٦] و : وإن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا
As for those who hold to the obligation of acting on it by reason, some of them said: The obligation of avoiding harms is known rationally. This is a universal principle believed by elites and commoners. Acting on conjecture in the details of a definitively established origin is rationally obligatory, like a single report of harm from food or a wall collapsing. For it is obligatory to accept. And the words of the Messenger explain harms and benefits. If it is conjectured, acting on it becomes obligatory definitively. This is based on the rational ruling of obligation; it has passed before and does not stand as proof against those who do not accept it. Moreover, the obligation of acting on conjecture in details of a definitively established origin is rationally prohibited. Rather, this action is rationally preferred. Yes, the obligation of this matter is established by Shari'ah. Some of them argued first that his truthfulness is conjectured necessarily, so acting on it is obligatory as precaution. He denies that precaution is obligatory absolutely. Do you not see that fasting is not obligatory on the day of doubt (seeing the crescent of Ramadan)? It is not hidden from you that no one claimed precaution is obligatory absolutely, rather precaution in the conjectural is without doubt. As for the absence of obligation to fast on the day of doubt, it is due to the absence of conjecture there. So it is more appropriate to deny that precaution is obligatory rationally; rather it is obligatory only in what is obligatory by revelation. He argued secondly: If acting on a single-narrator report were not obligatory, most events would be devoid of rulings. For the Quran and mutawatir (from Sunnah) do not cover all events; rather what they cover is the least of little. The answer is denial of the correlation. Because the ruling when there is no evidence is the absence of a Shari'ah ruling. And this includes all events devoid of certainty, for that is the evidence. So one stops or acts on original permissibility according to the difference of two opinions, as has passed. And the most apparent is permissibility in what has no evidence in Shari'ah. So events are not devoid. I say: Indeed, in the legislation of consensus and analogy there is sufficiency for the most. So there is no vacancy except in the least of little. And their sufficiency is questionable. As for consensus, it is only on enumerated events. As for analogy, it requires an original case to be analogized upon, and that is only from the Quran or mutawatir from Sunnah and consensus, which are insufficient. So ponder. And it may be denied that the consequent is false rationally. For the impossibility of events being devoid of rulings is not apparent to reason; it is only by Shari'ah. But the impossibility appears by adhering to rational good and evil in actions, for they necessitate the attachment of rulings to them from the Lawgiver, as is the verification by the verifiers of our teachers. So reflect. The Rawafid and those who agree with them said: First, acting on a single-narrator report is following conjecture, and Allah has said: 'Do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (al-Isra 17:36), and 'They follow nothing but...'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage surveys rational arguments for the obligation of accepting khabar al-wahid. First, there is the argument from harm avoidance: reason dictates avoiding harm, and a report from a single person can indicate harm (e.g., spoiled food, a collapsing wall). Since the Prophet's words clarify harms and benefits, if a report gives conjecture of harm, reason demands acting on it. However, the commentator rebuts that this assumes rational obligation, which is contested; at best, it shows preference ('awla), not obligation. The actual obligation is established by Shari'ah, not reason. Second, the argument from precaution (ihtiyat): if a report is conjecturally true, precaution requires acting on it. This is refuted: precaution is not absolutely obligatory; for example, fasting on the day of doubt (whether Ramadan has started) is not obligatory because there is no conjecture (only doubt). Precaution in the conjectural may be recommended, not obligatory by reason; obligation only comes from revelation. Third, the argument from necessity (khalw al-waqai): without khabar al-wahid, most events would have no rulings since the Quran and mutawatir hadith are limited. The response: absence of evidence means absence of a ruling, or one resorts to original permissibility (ibahah asliyyah). Moreover, consensus and analogy (qiyas) cover many events, so the problem is not acute. The commentator also notes that even if events were left without rulings, reason does not deem that impossible; only Shari'ah fills the gaps. Finally, the Rawafid (Shia) object that khabar al-wahid involves following conjecture, which is prohibited by Quran 17:36. The passage cuts off but implies the Hanafi response. This section demonstrates that rational arguments alone are insufficient; they must be complemented by textual proofs and usul principles.

Key Terms
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; acting on a conjectural report to be safe.
إباحة أصلية (ibahah asliyyah): Original permissibility; the default ruling for acts in the absence of evidence.
أولى (awla): Preferable; indicates rational preference but not legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi response to the argument that events would be devoid of rulings without khabar al-wahid?
A) Consensus and analogy cover all events completely.
B) Absence of evidence means absence of a ruling, or original permissibility applies.
C) The Quran and mutawatir are sufficient for all events.
D) The argument is accepted; thus khabar al-wahid is necessary.

Key Takeaway
Rational arguments for the obligation of acting on khabar al-wahid are insufficient; legal obligation is established only by Shari'ah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

8 min
Refuting the Claim that Qiyas Yields Stronger Probability than Khabar
Refutation of two arguments claiming qiyas gives stronger probability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the two opponents' arguments for the superiority of qiyas over khabar, and apply the Hanafi critique to each.

Core Idea
The probability from qiyas is not inherently stronger; its premises are themselves probable and often weak.

This lesson dissects two arguments advanced by scholars who prioritize qiyas over khabar (hadith). The first argument claims that qiyas generates probability from itself, making it more reliable than khabar which depends on external trust. The second invokes consensus (ijma) to bolster qiyas's authority. The Hanafi refutation exposes the fragility of both claims, showing that the premises of qiyas are themselves probabilistic and that the logical principle 'the necessary of the stronger is stronger' fails when the premise is weak. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping the Hanafi ordering of legal sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first opponent argument
The opponents argue that qiyas produces probability from itself (because it generates the ruling directly), while khabar's probability depends on an external factor (the truthfulness of the informant). They claim self-generated probability is more reliable.
This argument relies on the intuition that what depends on itself is stronger than what depends on others.
2
Analyze the Hanafi refutation of the first argument
The Hanafi response is that we do not accept that self-generated probability is automatically stronger. The premises of qiyas (such as the ruling of the original case, the attribute, and the cause) are themselves probable (maznun) and may be weak. If the premises are weak, the resulting probability is also weak, so qiyas is not necessarily stronger than khabar.
The strength of the conclusion follows the strength of the premises.
3
Identify the second opponent argument
The opponents argue that qiyas is established as a proof by ijma (consensus), and since ijma is stronger than khabar al-wahid, the necessary consequence (the probability of qiyas) must also be stronger.
This uses the logical maxim: 'The necessary of the stronger is stronger.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi refutation of the second argument
The Hanafi scholar points out that qiyas is not proven by definitive ijma; the ijma on qiyas itself may be based on probable evidence. Moreover, the 'necessary of the stronger' principle only holds if the premise (here, the consensus) is definitively strong. If the consensus is weak, the conclusion is not necessarily strong.
The text ends before completing the refutation, but the critique focuses on the conditional strength of the premise.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position on source hierarchy
Based on this critique, the Hanafi school maintains that khabar al-wahid takes precedence over qiyas. A mujtahid must first look for a hadith, and only if no textual evidence is found may he resort to qiyas.
This ordering reflects the relative strength and reliability of each source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمون للقياس (قالوا: أولاً ظن القياس) حاصل من قبل نفسه) فإنه ينتج الحكم نفسه (و) الظن (في الخبر) ينشأ (من غيره بواسطة ظن أنه قول المخبر الصادق (وهو) حال كونه حاصلاً منه (بنفسه أوثق) من الحاصل بغيره فظن القياس أوثق فيكون مقدماً على الخبر (و) قالوا: (ثانياً: القياس حجة بالإجماع، والإجماع أقوى من خبر الواحد، ولازم الأقوى أقوى فالقياس أقوى فيكون مقدماً على الخبر (ولا يخفى (ضعفهما) أما ضعف الأول فأولاً لأنا لا نسلم أن الظن الحاصل بنفسه أوثق مما يحصل بعد ملاحظة مقدمة، بل يجوز أن يكون مقدماته مظنونة ظناً ضعيفاً، فظن به،
Those who give precedence to qiyas said: First, the probability of qiyas arises from itself, for it produces the ruling itself, and the probability in khabar arises from something else by means of the probability that it is the statement of a truthful informant. And being obtained from itself is more reliable than that obtained from something else, so the probability of qiyas is more reliable, thus it is to be given precedence over khabar. And they said: Secondly, qiyas is a proof by consensus, and consensus is stronger than khabar al-wahid, and the necessary of the stronger is stronger, so qiyas is stronger, thus it is to be given precedence over khabar. And their weakness is not hidden. As for the weakness of the first: first, we do not accept that the probability obtained from itself is more reliable than that obtained after considering a premise; rather, it is possible that its premises are themselves probable with weak probability, so probability [is obtained] from it...
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments from scholars who prioritize qiyas over khabar (hadith), followed by their refutation. The opponents first argue that qiyas generates probability from itself because it directly produces the ruling, whereas khabar's probability relies on external confidence in the truthfulness of the informant. They claim self-generated probability is stronger. Second, they argue that qiyas is established as a proof by ijma (consensus), and since ijma is stronger than khabar al-wahid, qiyas must be stronger as a necessary consequence. The author immediately dismisses both as weak. For the first, he points out that qiyas's own premises (like hukm al-asl, attribute) are themselves probable and often weak, so the probability generated is not necessarily stronger. For the second, he likely refutes that qiyas is not proven by definitive ijma; the logic of 'necessary of the stronger' fails because qiyas's basis in ijma may be weak. The text ends abruptly, but the author's refutation continues in the original work.

Key Terms
ظن القياس (dhann al-qiyas): The probabilistic ruling produced by qiyas from its own premises without external input.
لازم الأقوى أقوى (lazim al-aqwa aqwa): The logical principle that the necessary consequence of something stronger is itself stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the opponents' first argument that qiyas's probability is self-generated and thus stronger?
A) He argues that khabar's probability is also self-generated.
B) He states that the premises of qiyas are themselves probable and often weak, so the resulting probability is not necessarily stronger.
C) He claims that qiyas is not a valid source of law.
D) He says that the Prophet's approval is stronger than any qiyas.

Key Takeaway
The probability of qiyas is not inherently stronger than that of khabar because its own premises are probable and may be weak.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Applying al-Asl When Evidences Conflict: Su'r al-Himar
Illustrating the principle of original state (al-asl) in ta'arud using donkey's leftover water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of al-asl (original state) to resolve conflicting evidences and derive the Hanafi ruling for su'r al-himar.

Core Idea
When evidences conflict and neither overrides, the original state is retained, requiring both water and tayammum.

In the Hanafi usul framework, when two hadiths appear contradictory and neither can be clearly preferred or abrogated, the scholar reverts to the original state (al-asl) before revelation. The case of the donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar) is a classic illustration. This lesson will walk you through the conflict, the failure of qiyas, and the application of al-asl to produce the Hanafi ruling of combining water and tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting evidences
Note the prohibition hadith (forbidding donkey meat, implying impurity) and the permission hadith (allowing riding, implying purity). These create a ta'arud (conflict) regarding the purity of the donkey's leftover water.
The hadiths are not quoted verbatim but referenced from Sahihayn and Bukhari.
2
Assess the possibility of qiyas (analogy)
The text considers analogizing to a cat (severe necessity) or predators (no necessity) and finds them unsuitable. The donkey's necessity is intermediate, so qiyas fails.
3
Revert to al-asl (original state)
Since the proofs conflict and both are inferior, the original states are restored: water is originally pure (so it remains pure), and the person is originally in hadath (so hadath is not removed by doubt).
Al-asl is a foundational Hanafi principle: certainty is not overridden by doubt.
4
Derive the ruling from al-asl
Because water remains pure, it must be used for wudu. But because its ability to remove hadath is doubtful (due to the conflict), tayammum is added to remove hadath with certainty. Thus, both water and tayammum are obligatory.
This is a precautionary (ihtiyati) ruling.
5
Address the objection of abrogation
Sheikh Ibn al-Humam argued that the prohibition hadith abrogates the permission, so no conflict exists. The Hanafi response: abrogation is not established because both hadiths are equally valid and the prohibition does not explicitly mention impurity. The conflict remains, so al-asl applies.
This intra-Hanafi dispute shows the importance of al-asl when abrogation is uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا وجد الأدنى فالعمل بالأصل لازم (كما في سؤر الحمار) فإنه نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم عن لحوم الحمر الأهلية خيبر كما في الصحيحين، وقد عارضه قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم للسائل عن أكل لحوم الحمر الأهلية كل من سمان أموالك رواه البخاري والحرمة آية النجاسة، والحل آية الطهارة، فقد تعارضا، وليس ههنا أصل يقاس عليه فإن كان الهرة فالعلة فيه الضرورة الشديدة وليست مثلها في الحمار لأنها تدخل المضايق بخلافه، وإن كان السباع فليس فيها ضرورة أصلاً بخلاف الحمار، فقررنا الأصول، وهو أن الماء وجد في الأصل طاهراً فلا يتنجس بالشك ولا يطهر المتوضىء لأنه كان محدثاً في الأصل، فلا يزول بالشك، فبقي كما كان ذلك احتمال زوال الحدث قائم فوجب استعمال الماء وضم التيمم كذا قالوا مع ولا يرد عليه أن الحرمة يجوز أن تكون للكرامة وليس الحل من لوازم الطهارة قطعاً، لأن التعليل بكونه الركوب مذكور في حديث التحريم فلا احتمال للكرامة . وههنا بحث، فإن حديث الحرمة ناسخ لحديث الحل فلا تعارض أصلاً، ولأجل ذلك غير الشيخ ابن الهمام وقال : التحريم يدل على النجاسة والضرورة توجب الطهارة فقد تعارضا. وفيه أولاً : أن الطهارة حينئذ ثبتت بالتعليل والنجاسة بالنص فلا تعارض، وثانياً : المعتبر الضرورة الشديدة كما في الهرة، وقد مر وليست فالأولى أن يقال : عارضه حديث الركوب على الحمار، ولا يخلو من المخالطة بالعرق ولا قياس وبحث آخر هو أن الماء لما كان طاهراً عملاً بالأصل فلا بد من استعماله لإزالة الحدث ولا وجه لضم التيمم، كيف لا ومعنى تقرير الأصول أن يهدر الحجتان ويعمل بالأصل، وإذا هدر الحجتان صار الحادثة كأن لم ينزل فيها شيء، والماء كان في الأصل طاهراً فيبقى على طهارته، فإذا لاقى العضو أزال الحدث فلم يبق في اليد شيء يحكم بضم التيمم إلا الاحتياط بقيام احتمال بقاء النجاسة في الماء، فقام احتمال عدم زوال الحدث، ثم ليس مقتضى الاحتياط ضم التيمم، لأنه وإن كان مزيلاً للحدث لكنه ليس مزيلاً للخبث واستعمال هذا الماء كما أقام احتمال عدم زوال الحدث أقام احتمال تنجس الأعضاء فالتيمم لا يغني بل مقتضى الاحتياط لو اعتبر اراقة الماء ثم التيمم وهذا الإشكال وإن استصعبه الأذكياء لكن يراه هذا العبد سهل الاندفاع، فإنا سلمنا أن تقرير الأصول يقتضي إهدار الحجتين من البين وأن الحادثة كأنها لم ينزل فيها شيء إلا أنهما كما تدلان على نجاسة الماء وطهارته كذلك تدلان على زوال الحدث باستعماله وعدم زواله، فإذا أهدرا كان كأن لم ينزل في النجاسة والطهارة شيء وكذا في زوال الحدث وعدمه، كأنه لم ينزل شيء، والأصل في الماء الطهارة، فحكم بها، والأصل في البدن الحدث، فحكم به وبعدم زواله باستعمال هذا الماء، وكيف وليس الحكم بزوال الحدث إلا أمراً تعبدياً بإبانة الشرع، وإذا أهدر الحجتان ارتفع من البين والتيمم عرف مزيلاً فوجب. ثم إن الماء الطاهر موجود البتة . واحتمال إزالته قائم فوجب استعماله للاحتياط، فاستعمال الماء للاحتياط، وأما ضم التيمم فأمر حتم، ولما حكمنا بسقوط الحجتين وحكمنا ببقاء طهارة الماء بالأصل، فاحتمال نجاسته كاحتمال وقوع النجاسة في ماء موضوع من الليل، وهذا الاحتمال مهدر رعاً، فلا وجه للاحتياط بالإراقة فافهم، فقد ظهر لك مما قررنا أن الشك ههنا في الطهورية لا في الطهارة، ثم أورد بحث آخر هو أن الحجتين إذ قد تعارضتا فواحدة منهما منسوخة في نفس الأمر أو باطلة، فلا حكم في نفس الأمر إلا لواحدة، فالإشكال في السؤر ليس في الشارع، بل منا بجهلنا، فهذا الحكم منالاً من الشارع ولك أن تجيب عنه أنه ليس المقصود أن قد أشكل بل المقصود أنه لا بد ههنا من تقرير الأصول وهو يقتضي أن يكون الحكم كذا، ويظن أن حكم الشارع في سؤر الحمار والبغل استعمال الماء وضم التيمم، وهذا أمر ممكن لا
Otherwise, when the inferior is found, action by the original (al-asl) is necessary, as in the case of the donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar). For the Messenger of God, peace be upon him and his family and companions, forbade the meat of domestic donkeys at Khaybar, as in al-Sahihayn. This was countered by his saying to the questioner about eating domestic donkey meat: 'Eat from the fat of your wealth' narrated by al-Bukhari. Prohibition is a sign of impurity, and permission is a sign of purity; so they conflicted. There is no source (asl) to be analogized here. If the cat, the cause is severe necessity, and it is not similar regarding the donkey because the cat enters narrow places unlike it. If the predators, there is no necessity at all unlike the donkey. So we established the principles: that water was originally pure, so it does not become impure by doubt, nor does it make the performer of ablution pure because he was originally in a state of hadath, so it does not remove by doubt. So it remains as it was, with the probability of removal of hadath existing. So using water and adding tayammum became obligatory. Thus they said, and it is not refuted that prohibition could be for honor and permission is not a necessary consequence of purity, because the reasoning being riding is mentioned in the hadith of prohibition, so there is no probability of honor. And here there is a discussion: indeed the hadith of prohibition abrogates the hadith of permission, so there is no conflict at all. Therefore, Sheikh Ibn al-Humam changed and said: Prohibition indicates impurity, and necessity necessitates purity, so they conflicted. In it: First, purity is then established by reasoning (ta'lil) and impurity by text, so no conflict. Second, severe necessity is considered as in the cat, and it has passed, and it is not. So it is better to say: The hadith of riding the donkey countered it, and it is not free from mixing with sweat, nor measurement. Another discussion is that since water is pure by acting on the original, it must be used to remove hadath, and there is no basis for adding tayammum. How so? The meaning of establishing al-usul is that both proofs are dropped and action by the original is taken. When both proofs are dropped, the incident becomes as if nothing was revealed about it. Water was originally pure, so it remains on its purity. When it contacts the limb, it removes hadath, so nothing remains in the hand to judge adding tayammum except precaution due to the probability of remaining impurity in the water. So the probability of non-removal of hadath arose. Then the requirement of precaution is not to add tayammum, because although it removes hadath, it does not remove impurity. Using this water, as it raised the probability of non-removal of hadath, also raised the probability of impurity of the limbs. So tayammum does not suffice; rather, the requirement of precaution, if considered, would be to pour out the water and then perform tayammum. This objection, though the intelligent find difficult, this servant considers it easy to rebut. For we concede that establishing al-usul requires dropping both proofs from the middle, and the incident is as if nothing was revealed about it, except that just as they indicate the impurity and purity of water, so too they indicate the removal of hadath by using it and its non-removal. So when they are dropped, it is as if nothing was revealed about impurity and purity, and similarly about removal of hadath and its non-removal—as if nothing was revealed. The original for water is purity, so it is judged. The original for the body is hadath, so it is judged that it does not remove by using this water. How not? The judgment of removal of hadath is only a matter of worship by legislation of the Law. When the two proofs are dropped, it is removed from the middle, and tayammum is known to be a remover, so it becomes obligatory. Then, pure water definitely exists, and the probability of its removal exists, so it must be used for precaution. So using water is for precaution, but adding tayammum is a mandatory matter. Since we judged the fall of both proofs and we judged the remaining purity of water by the original, the probability of its impurity is like the probability of impurity falling into water placed overnight. This probability is disregarded, so there is no basis for precaution by pouring. So understand. Thus it appeared to you from what we established that the doubt here is about tahuriyya (ability to purify) not about tahara (purity). Then another discussion was raised: that since the two proofs conflicted, one of them is abrogated in actuality or false, so there is no ruling in actuality except for one. So the problem in the leftover water is not from the Lawgiver, but from us due to our ignorance. So this ruling is attainable from the Lawgiver. But you can answer that the intention is not that it is problematic; rather, the intention is that here it is necessary to establish al-usul, and it requires that the ruling be thus. And it is presumed that the ruling of the Lawgiver regarding the leftover water of donkey and mule is to use water and add tayammum, and this is possible.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul rule, demonstrating the principle of al-asl (original state) when two conflicting evidences are both considered inferior. The example is the leftover water of a donkey (su'r al-himar): hadiths conflict, one prohibiting domestic donkey meat (implying impurity) and one permitting riding (implying purity). Without an analogical basis, the Hanafis revert to al-asl: water is originally pure, so it does not become impure by doubt; the person is originally in hadath, so it does not remove by doubt. Hence both water (for purity) and tayammum (to remove hadath) are required. The text addresses objections, e.g., that the prohibition hadith may abrogate the permission, or that tayammum alone is sufficient. It defends the combined use of water and tayammum as a precautionary measure.

Key Terms
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water (or saliva) from a donkey's mouth after drinking.
الأصل (al-asl): The original state or default ruling in the absence of overriding evidence. Here, water is originally pure, and a person is originally in hadath.
ضم التيمم (damm al-tayammum): Adding the performance of tayammum (dry ablution) alongside the use of water, as a precaution when water's purificatory capacity is doubtful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analysis of su'r al-himar, why is the use of water combined with tayammum required?
A) Because the water is definitely impure, so only tayammum can be used.
B) Because the water is definitely pure, so no tayammum is needed.
C) Because the conflicting hadiths leave the water's purity uncertain, so the original state of water purity and body impurity are both considered, leading to combined use.
D) Because the hadith of prohibition is abrogated, making water pure and tayammum unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
When evidences conflict and neither overrides, the Hanafi usul reverts to the original state (al-asl), leading to precautionary combined actions such as using both water and tayammum.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Obligation of Taharri in Conflicting Qiyas
Hanafi rule for conflicting qiyas and obligation of taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule for conflicting qiyas and contrast it with the Shafi'i position on taharri.

Core Idea
When qiyas conflict, taharri is obligatory — the heart's perspicacity guides the mujtahid to the stronger proof.

This lesson explores what a mujtahid must do when two analogical proofs (qiyas) contradict each other and neither is clearly stronger. The Hanafis require taharri (seeking the closest) before choosing, while the Shafi'is allow arbitrary choice. Understanding the reasoning behind each position will sharpen your grasp of how Hanafi usul prioritises certainty in ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two qiyas conflict with no tarjih (preference) between them. The initial ruling is takhayyur (choice).
2
Recognise the Hanafi position
After the initial choice, taharri becomes wajib (obligatory) to select one of the two qiyas.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that taharri is not obligatory; the mujtahid may choose whichever qiyas he wishes arbitrarily.
4
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis cite the hadith on firasa (believer's perspicacity) and argue that neglecting taharri risks acting on the weaker proof, so effort is required.
The hadith: 'Fear the perspicacity of the believer, for he sees with the light of Allah.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي ، (وأما) التعارض الواقع في القياس ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر (فالتخيير) فيهما (ابتداء) أي قبل التحري بأن يعمل بأحدهما بالتحري (ويجب التحري) فيعمل به (خلافاً للشافعي فإنه يقول : لا يجب التحري، بل للمجتهد أن يعمل بأيهما شاء: إذ لا هدر، لأنه ليس دليلاً منتجه حتى يعمل به، إذ الأصل ليس دليلاً ولا يتعين أحدهما للعمل لعدم الترجيح، أنه لا يعمل بأحدهما لا على التعيين وهو التخيير، لكن لا بد من التحري، فإن الشهادة القلب تأثيراً لأنه ينظر بنور الله ، كما ورد في الخبر الصحيح : اتقوا فراسة المؤمن فإنه ينظر بنور الله وقد يقال : لم يبق للمؤمن فراسة، حيث تعارض الأدلة مع القطع بفساد أحدها ولم يعين الفساد، فحينئذ لا اعتبار للتحري وجوابه : أن المقصود أنه لم يطلع على الفساد بالاستدلال، وهذا لا يبطل الفراسة فإنها معينة على التعيين بما وقع التحري إليه، فهو متفرس به من الفراسة يتأمل فيه كما في القبلة (وقول الصحابيين عند من يقول بحجيته (وإن كان قبل القياس) لكنه (كقياسين، فلا مصير إلى القياس بأن يسقطا ويعمل بالقياس (بل يعمل) المجتهد بما شاء) لكن ينبغي أن يتحرى فيهما أيضاً. وفيه ما فيه لأنّ القياس على الكتاب والسنة يقتضي سقوطهما والمصير إلى القياس لأنه حجة دونه وقد يفرق بأن قولهما عند الاختلاف لا يكون بالسماع البتة بل الرأي فرجعا إلى القياسين ولا تساقط فيهما، فتدبر. كذا في «الحاشية» . واعلم أن الحنفية الكرام استدلوا على عدم تساقط القياسين وتساقط النصين أن الكتاب والسنة إنما وضعهما الشارع لإفادة ما هو حكم عنده تعالى قطعاً، فيجب العمل به، وإن تخلف في بعض النصوص، كأخبار الآحاد والعام المخصوص، فالقصور منافي النقل أو الفهم، فإذا تعارضا، ومن المعلوم قطعاً أن الشارع لا يحكم بحكمين متناقضين معاً، فأحدهما منسوخ بالآخر، لكن المنسوخ لم يتعين بالجهل، فلم يحصل لنا علم بالحكم، فلا يجب العمل بأحدهما بل يحرم بهما لما كان المقصود بهما العلم بما هو حكم عنده تعالى، وأما القياس فما وضعه الشارع لمعرفة حكم الله تعالى لأنه لا يفيد أن هذا الحكم هو ما عنده تعالى، ومع ذلك أوجب العمل بحسبه، وإن كان خطأ في الواقع، فإذا تعارضا ولا ترجيح ولا يعلم فساد أحدهما وإن كان فاسداً في الواقع فيجب العمل بهما كما كان لأن التعارض لا يوجب إلا كون أحدهما فاسداً، وذا لا يمنع وجوب العمل، فالتعارض لا يمنع العمل بهما أصلاً، ولما كان صحتهما معاً معلوم الانتفاء وجب أن لا يعمل بهما معاً وإلا لزم العمل بالخطأ بيقين
Remains. (And as for) the conflict occurring in qiyas with no preference for one over the other, (then there is choice) in them (initially), i.e., before taharri, that he acts by one by taharri, (and taharri is obligatory) so he acts by it, (contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he says: Taharri is not obligatory; rather, the mujtahid may act by whichever he wishes. Since there is no waste, because it is not a proof that produces [certainty] so that he acts by it. For the original [principle] is not a proof, and neither is determined for action due to lack of preference. He does not act by either not specifying, and that is choice. But taharri is necessary, for the testimony of the heart has effect because it sees by the light of Allah, as came in the authentic report: 'Fear the perspicacity of the believer, for he sees by the light of Allah.' And it may be said: There remains no perspicacity for the believer when evidences conflict with the certainty that one of them is corrupt but the corruption is not identified. Then taharri is not considered. Its answer: The intended point is that he has not discovered the corruption by inference, and this does not nullify perspicacity, for it assists in specifying whatever taharri has reached. So he is perspicacious about it by perspicacity, reflecting on it as in the case of the qibla. (And the statement of two Companions, according to those who consider it authoritative,) (even if it is before qiyas,) but it is (like two qiyas), so there is no recourse to qiyas such that they both drop and one acts by qiyas. (Rather, the mujtahid acts) by whichever he wishes, but it is appropriate that he perform taharri in them as well. In it is what is in it, because qiyas on the Book and the Sunnah necessitates dropping them and resorting to qiyas because it is proof without them. And it may be distinguished: Their statement when differing is not by hearing at all, but rather opinion, so they revert to two qiyas, and there is no dropping in them. So ponder. This is from al-Hashiyah. And know that the noble Hanafis deduced the non-cancellation of two qiyas and the cancellation of two texts: the Book and the Sunnah were placed by the Lawgiver to convey what is His ruling, definitely, so acting by them is obligatory, even if there is deficiency in some texts, like ahad reports and the general made specific, the deficiency is from the transmission or understanding. So when they conflict, and it is certainly known that the Lawgiver does not rule with two contradictory rulings together, so one is abrogated by the other. But the abrogated is not specified due to ignorance, so we have no knowledge of the ruling, so it is not obligatory to act by either; rather, it is prohibited to act by both, because the purpose of them was knowledge of what is His ruling. As for qiyas, it was not placed by the Lawgiver to know Allah's ruling, because it does not convey that this ruling is what is with Him. Nevertheless, He obligated acting by it, even if it is mistaken in reality. So when they conflict with no preference and the corruption of one is not known, although it is corrupt in reality, it is obligatory to act by both as before, because conflict only necessitates that one of them is corrupt, and that does not prevent the obligation of acting. Thus conflict does not prevent acting by them at all. And since the correctness of both together is known to be impossible, it is necessary not to act by both together, otherwise acting by error with certainty would be necessary.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule for when two analogical proofs (qiyas) conflict and neither is clearly stronger. The mujtahid has a choice initially but must perform taharri (seeking the closest) to determine which qiyas to follow. This is opposed to Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that taharri is not obligatory and that the mujtahid may simply choose. The Hanafis justify taharri by citing the hadith on the believer's perspicacity (firasa) and the principle that the heart's inclination, guided by reflection, can distinguish truth. The text then distinguishes between conflicting texts (nusus) and conflicting qiyas. For texts, because they are from the Lawgiver and must convey His actual ruling, conflict implies abrogation, and since we cannot know which is abrogated, we cannot act on either (act is prohibited). For qiyas, because they are only zanni (probable) and the Lawgiver commands us to act on them even if mistaken, conflict does not nullify them; both remain valid for action. However, acting on both simultaneously is impossible if they yield opposite rulings, so the mujtahid must choose through taharri. The passage also discusses the status of companion statements (qawl al-sahabi), which some consider hujja; when they conflict, they are treated like two qiyas. The overall lesson is the Hanafi principle that conflicting qiyas do not collapse, but conflicting texts do, reflecting the different epistemological weights of these sources.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharri): The effort of a mujtahid to determine the stronger or more likely proof when evidence conflicts.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared cause (illa).
التخيير (al-takhayyur): The permissibility to choose between two or more options, here initially before taharri.
الفراسة (al-firasa): Perspicacity; the believer's insightful perception, often guided by divine light, used in ijtihad to discern the stronger proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, what must a mujtahid do when two qiyas conflict without preference?
A) Abandon both and seek another proof.
B) Choose arbitrarily whichever he wishes.
C) Perform taharri to determine the stronger one.
D) Act on both simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis require taharri (seeking the closest) in conflicting qiyas, supported by the hadith on the believer's perspicacity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Distinction Between Conflicting Texts and Conflicting Qiyas
Hanafi rationale for non-cancellation of qiyas vs cancellation of texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for why conflicting texts (nusus) cancel each other while conflicting qiyas do not.

Core Idea
Texts convey God's actual ruling, so conflict implies abrogation; qiyas are zanni and not for certainty, so both remain actionable.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi principle that two conflicting qiyas do not become void, whereas two conflicting texts do. The key lies in the different epistemological status of these sources. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying ijtihad correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Two texts (Quran or Sunnah) conflict, and two qiyas conflict. We compare the rulings for each.
2
Recall the ruling for texts
Conflicting texts cancel each other (tasaqut) — neither can be acted upon because we know one is abrogated but don't know which.
3
Recall the ruling for qiyas
Conflicting qiyas do not cancel; both remain valid for action after performing taharri.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rationale
Texts are placed by the Lawgiver to convey His actual ruling definitively; conflict forces abrogation. Qiyas are not designed to convey certainty; the Lawgiver commands action even if mistaken.
5
Apply to companion statements
Companion statements in conflict are treated like two qiyas, not like texts, because they are based on opinion (ra'y), not direct hearing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي ، (وأما) التعارض الواقع في القياس ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر (فالتخيير) فيهما (ابتداء) أي قبل التحري بأن يعمل بأحدهما بالتحري (ويجب التحري) فيعمل به (خلافاً للشافعي فإنه يقول : لا يجب التحري، بل للمجتهد أن يعمل بأيهما شاء: إذ لا هدر، لأنه ليس دليلاً منتجه حتى يعمل به، إذ الأصل ليس دليلاً ولا يتعين أحدهما للعمل لعدم الترجيح، أنه لا يعمل بأحدهما لا على التعيين وهو التخيير، لكن لا بد من التحري، فإن الشهادة القلب تأثيراً لأنه ينظر بنور الله ، كما ورد في الخبر الصحيح : اتقوا فراسة المؤمن فإنه ينظر بنور الله وقد يقال : لم يبق للمؤمن فراسة، حيث تعارض الأدلة مع القطع بفساد أحدها ولم يعين الفساد، فحينئذ لا اعتبار للتحري وجوابه : أن المقصود أنه لم يطلع على الفساد بالاستدلال، وهذا لا يبطل الفراسة فإنها معينة على التعيين بما وقع التحري إليه، فهو متفرس به من الفراسة يتأمل فيه كما في القبلة (وقول الصحابيين عند من يقول بحجيته (وإن كان قبل القياس) لكنه (كقياسين، فلا مصير إلى القياس بأن يسقطا ويعمل بالقياس (بل يعمل) المجتهد بما شاء) لكن ينبغي أن يتحرى فيهما أيضاً. وفيه ما فيه لأنّ القياس على الكتاب والسنة يقتضي سقوطهما والمصير إلى القياس لأنه حجة دونه وقد يفرق بأن قولهما عند الاختلاف لا يكون بالسماع البتة بل الرأي فرجعا إلى القياسين ولا تساقط فيهما، فتدبر. كذا في «الحاشية» . واعلم أن الحنفية الكرام استدلوا على عدم تساقط القياسين وتساقط النصين أن الكتاب والسنة إنما وضعهما الشارع لإفادة ما هو حكم عنده تعالى قطعاً، فيجب العمل به، وإن تخلف في بعض النصوص، كأخبار الآحاد والعام المخصوص، فالقصور منافي النقل أو الفهم، فإذا تعارضا، ومن المعلوم قطعاً أن الشارع لا يحكم بحكمين متناقضين معاً، فأحدهما منسوخ بالآخر، لكن المنسوخ لم يتعين بالجهل، فلم يحصل لنا علم بالحكم، فلا يجب العمل بأحدهما بل يحرم بهما لما كان المقصود بهما العلم بما هو حكم عنده تعالى، وأما القياس فما وضعه الشارع لمعرفة حكم الله تعالى لأنه لا يفيد أن هذا الحكم هو ما عنده تعالى، ومع ذلك أوجب العمل بحسبه، وإن كان خطأ في الواقع، فإذا تعارضا ولا ترجيح ولا يعلم فساد أحدهما وإن كان فاسداً في الواقع فيجب العمل بهما كما كان لأن التعارض لا يوجب إلا كون أحدهما فاسداً، وذا لا يمنع وجوب العمل، فالتعارض لا يمنع العمل بهما أصلاً، ولما كان صحتهما معاً معلوم الانتفاء وجب أن لا يعمل بهما معاً وإلا لزم العمل بالخطأ بيقين
Remains. (And as for) the conflict occurring in qiyas with no preference for one over the other, (then there is choice) in them (initially), i.e., before taharri, that he acts by one by taharri, (and taharri is obligatory) so he acts by it, (contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he says: Taharri is not obligatory; rather, the mujtahid may act by whichever he wishes. Since there is no waste, because it is not a proof that produces [certainty] so that he acts by it. For the original [principle] is not a proof, and neither is determined for action due to lack of preference. He does not act by either not specifying, and that is choice. But taharri is necessary, for the testimony of the heart has effect because it sees by the light of Allah, as came in the authentic report: 'Fear the perspicacity of the believer, for he sees by the light of Allah.' And it may be said: There remains no perspicacity for the believer when evidences conflict with the certainty that one of them is corrupt but the corruption is not identified. Then taharri is not considered. Its answer: The intended point is that he has not discovered the corruption by inference, and this does not nullify perspicacity, for it assists in specifying whatever taharri has reached. So he is perspicacious about it by perspicacity, reflecting on it as in the case of the qibla. (And the statement of two Companions, according to those who consider it authoritative,) (even if it is before qiyas,) but it is (like two qiyas), so there is no recourse to qiyas such that they both drop and one acts by qiyas. (Rather, the mujtahid acts) by whichever he wishes, but it is appropriate that he perform taharri in them as well. In it is what is in it, because qiyas on the Book and the Sunnah necessitates dropping them and resorting to qiyas because it is proof without them. And it may be distinguished: Their statement when differing is not by hearing at all, but rather opinion, so they revert to two qiyas, and there is no dropping in them. So ponder. This is from al-Hashiyah. And know that the noble Hanafis deduced the non-cancellation of two qiyas and the cancellation of two texts: the Book and the Sunnah were placed by the Lawgiver to convey what is His ruling, definitely, so acting by them is obligatory, even if there is deficiency in some texts, like ahad reports and the general made specific, the deficiency is from the transmission or understanding. So when they conflict, and it is certainly known that the Lawgiver does not rule with two contradictory rulings together, so one is abrogated by the other. But the abrogated is not specified due to ignorance, so we have no knowledge of the ruling, so it is not obligatory to act by either; rather, it is prohibited to act by both, because the purpose of them was knowledge of what is His ruling. As for qiyas, it was not placed by the Lawgiver to know Allah's ruling, because it does not convey that this ruling is what is with Him. Nevertheless, He obligated acting by it, even if it is mistaken in reality. So when they conflict with no preference and the corruption of one is not known, although it is corrupt in reality, it is obligatory to act by both as before, because conflict only necessitates that one of them is corrupt, and that does not prevent the obligation of acting. Thus conflict does not prevent acting by them at all. And since the correctness of both together is known to be impossible, it is necessary not to act by both together, otherwise acting by error with certainty would be necessary.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule for when two analogical proofs (qiyas) conflict and neither is clearly stronger. The mujtahid has a choice initially but must perform taharri (seeking the closest) to determine which qiyas to follow. This is opposed to Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that taharri is not obligatory and that the mujtahid may simply choose. The Hanafis justify taharri by citing the hadith on the believer's perspicacity (firasa) and the principle that the heart's inclination, guided by reflection, can distinguish truth. The text then distinguishes between conflicting texts (nusus) and conflicting qiyas. For texts, because they are from the Lawgiver and must convey His actual ruling, conflict implies abrogation, and since we cannot know which is abrogated, we cannot act on either (act is prohibited). For qiyas, because they are only zanni (probable) and the Lawgiver commands us to act on them even if mistaken, conflict does not nullify them; both remain valid for action. However, acting on both simultaneously is impossible if they yield opposite rulings, so the mujtahid must choose through taharri. The passage also discusses the status of companion statements (qawl al-sahabi), which some consider hujja; when they conflict, they are treated like two qiyas. The overall lesson is the Hanafi principle that conflicting qiyas do not collapse, but conflicting texts do, reflecting the different epistemological weights of these sources.

Key Terms
النص (al-nass): A text from the Quran or Sunnah that provides a clear ruling.
المنسوخ (al-mansukh): An abrogated ruling; one of the two conflicting texts is abrogated but which is unknown.
الفراسة (al-firasa): Perspicacity; the believer's insightful perception used in taharri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do conflicting texts cancel each other according to Hanafis?
A) Because they are contradictory.
B) Because they are from the Lawgiver and must convey His actual ruling.
C) Because they are weak.
D) Because the Companions disagreed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between conflicting texts and conflicting qiyas rests on the epistemological certainty attached to each: texts aim for certainty, qiyas only probability.

Conflict of Qiyas: Takhyir and Taharri
Conflict of Qiyas: Takhyir and Taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on conflicting qiyas without tarjih, explain the obligation of taharri, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the proof from firasa.

Core Idea
When two qiyas conflict without preponderance, the mujtahid must perform taharri — the heart's insight is binding.

When a mujtahid faces two analogical arguments (qiyas) that seem equally strong, how does he proceed? The Hanafi school holds that he must not choose arbitrarily; rather, he must seek preponderance in his heart (taharri), guided by the divine light of faith. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence from the hadith of firasa, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage deals with two conflicting qiyas where no external preponderance (tarjih) exists. The mujtahid cannot simply discard both; he must choose one by a specific method.
This is not a case of conflicting definitive proofs, but of probable arguments (zanni).
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that takhyir (initial choice) is allowed only before taharri, but taharri is obligatory. The mujtahid must seek the inclination of his heart and act accordingly.
Takhyir here is temporary; it does not mean free choice without further effort.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that taharri is not obligatory; the mujtahid may freely choose either qiyas because conflict does not nullify the evidence.
This is a fundamental methodological difference about the role of subjective insight.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Beware of the firasa of the believer, for he sees by the light of Allah.' This indicates that the heart can perceive truth, making taharri a valid and necessary tool.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the Hanafi school accepts it as sufficient for establishing obligation in this context.
5
Address the objection and conclusion
A possible objection is that firasa fails when one knows one of the qiyas is corrupt but cannot identify which. The response: the corruption was not discovered by inference, so firasa still functions. Thus, taharri remains valid.
Analogous to determining the qibla when in doubt — the heart's inclination guided by knowledge of signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعارض الواقع في القياس ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر فالتخيير فيهما ابتداء أي قبل التحري بأن يعمل بأحدهما بالتحري ويجب التحري فيعمل به خلافاً للشافعي فإنه يقول لا يجب التحري بل للمجتهد أن يعمل بأيهما شاء إذ لا هدر لأنه ليس دليلاً منتجه حتى يعمل به إذ الأصل ليس دليلاً ولا يتعين أحدهما للعمل لعدم الترجيح أنه لا يعمل بأحدهما لا على التعيين وهو التخيير لكن لا بد من التحري فإن الشهادة القلب تأثيراً لأنه ينظر بنور الله كما ورد في الخبر الصحيح اتقوا فراسة المؤمن فإنه ينظر بنور الله وقد يقال لم يبق للمؤمن فراسة حيث تعارض الأدلة مع القطع بفساد أحدها ولم يعين الفساد فحينئذ لا اعتبار للتحري وجوابه أن المقصود أنه لم يطلع على الفساد بالاستدلال وهذا لا يبطل الفراسة فإنها معينة على التعيين بما وقع التحري إليه فهو متفرس به من الفراسة يتأمل فيه كما في القبلة وقول الصحابيين عند من يقول بحجيته وإن كان قبل القياس لكنه كقياسين فلا مصير إلى القياس بأن يسقطا ويعمل بالقياس بل يعمل المجتهد بما شاء لكن ينبغي أن يتحرى فيهما أيضاً وفيه ما فيه لأن القياس على الكتاب والسنة يقتضي سقوطهما والمصير إلى القياس لأنه حجة دونه وقد يفرق بأن قولهما عند الاختلاف لا يكون بالسماع البتة بل الرأي فرجعا إلى القياسين ولا تساقط فيهما فتدبر كذا في الحاشية
As for the conflict occurring in qiyas without preponderance of one over the other, there is takhyir (choice) between them initially, i.e., before taharri (seeking preponderance), by acting with one of them after taharri. And taharri is obligatory, so he acts upon it, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he says: taharri is not obligatory; rather the mujtahid may act with whichever he wishes, because it (conflict) does not nullify [the evidence]; since qiyas is not a definitive proof that compels action, the original state does not necessitate a specific one for action due to lack of preponderance, so he acts with one of them without specification, which is takhyir. But taharri is necessary, because the heart's testimony [inclination] has an effect, for it (the heart) sees by the light of Allah, as reported in the authentic hadith: 'Beware of the firasa (insight) of the believer, for he sees by the light of Allah.' It might be said: there remains no firasa for the believer when evidences conflict with certainty that one is corrupt but the corruption is not identified; then taharri is of no consideration. The answer: the intended meaning is that he did not become aware of the corruption through inference, and this does not nullify firasa, for it helps him identify what he inclines to by taharri; he uses firasa for it, contemplating it as in the case of the qibla. And the statement of the two Companions (Abu Bakr and 'Umar), according to those who consider it (their statement) authoritative, even if it precedes qiyas, it is like two qiyases; so there is no resorting to qiyas by discarding both and acting on qiyas; rather the mujtahid acts with whichever he wishes, but he should perform taharri in them also. It has its own considerations because qiyas upon the Book and Sunnah would necessitate discarding them and resorting to qiyas because it is a proof without them. It might be distinguished that their statements in case of disagreement are not based on hearing (direct transmission) at all, but on opinion; thus they refer to two qiyases, and there is no tasaqut (falling away) in them, so reflect. Thus in al-Hashiya.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the conflict of two qiyas when there is no preponderant factor (tarjih). The text states that initially there is takhyir (choice) before taharri, but taharri is obligatory, and the mujtahid must act on the one his heart inclines to. This is contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that taharri is not obligatory; the mujtahid may freely choose. The Hanafi proof is the hadith about firasa (insight) of the believer, that the heart sees by divine light. To a possible objection that firasa fails when one knows one of the conflicting evidences is corrupt but cannot identify which, the answer is that the corruption was not discovered by inference, so firasa still works to guide the heart to the correct one, like in determining the qibla. Then the text discusses the statements of the two Companions (Abu Bakr and 'Umar) for those who consider them authoritative: their statements, though prior to qiyas, are treated as equivalent to two qiyases, so they do not cause tasaqut but require taharri. The reasoning is that their statements in case of disagreement are based on opinion, not direct hearing, so they are like qiyas. Therefore, they do not fall away, and the mujtahid uses taharri.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhyīr): The initial choice between conflicting qiyas before taharri; the mujtahid may select either.
تحري (taḥarrī): Seeking preponderance of the heart through insight (firasa) to choose one of the conflicting qiyas.
فراسة (firāsa): The believer's insight by divine light, used to determine the preponderant opinion in taharri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a mujtahid do when two qiyas conflict and there is no external preponderance?
A) Declare both invalid and seek a third proof.
B) Perform taharri and act on the one his heart inclines to.
C) Choose arbitrarily without taharri.
D) Follow the qiyas that agrees with the majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
When two qiyas conflict without tarjih, the Hanafi school requires taharri — seeking the heart's inclination through divine insight — based on the hadith of firasa.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Resolving Conflicting Qiyas through Heart's Judgment (Tahkim al-Qalb)
Expanding the rule of heart's judgment for conflicting qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tahkim al-qalb to resolve conflicting qiyas and evaluate the objections against it.

Core Idea
When two qiyas conflict and neither preponderates, the heart's inclination determines which to follow.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas (analogical deduction) is a proof that obligates action based on probability (zann). But what happens when two conflicting qiyas arise, and neither has an external preponderant? This passage presents the Hanafi solution: resort to the heart's judgment (tahkim al-qalb). The author defends this rule against three objections, explaining why neither arbitrary choice nor discarding both is valid, and why this approach differs from conflict in textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the problem of conflicting qiyas
Identify that two qiyas conflict and neither has a preponderant factor. Recognize that both produce probability (zann) individually, but together they cannot both be acted upon.
The passage assumes obligation to act upon qiyas when it yields strong probability.
2
Understand the necessity of choosing one
Discarding both is not an option because the Lawgiver established qiyas to be acted upon. Abandoning both would mean acting without evidence. Therefore, one must be selected.
The author argues that if conflict necessitated discarding both, it would lead to abandoning the proof set up by the Lawgiver.
3
Apply the heart's judgment (tahkim al-qalb)
Since no external preponderant exists, the mujtahid must consult his inner conviction. The heart's judgment provides the decisive inclination, making one qiyas preponderate over the other.
This is not arbitrary; it is a valid epistemological tool when external criteria are exhausted.
4
Refute the objection of arbitrary choice (takhayyur)
One might argue that since both qiyas are equally probable, one can choose arbitrarily without heart's judgment. But the author rejects this because each qiyas individually obligates action; the conflict necessitates a specific selection mechanism, not mere choice.
The heart's judgment provides a principled basis for selection.
5
Differentiate from conflict in textual proofs
Texts (Book and Sunnah) are set up to convey actual rulings; conflict in texts destroys their authority because we know one is wrong. Qiyas, however, is set up only for probabilistic action, so conflict does not nullify both. Hence, the heart's judgment applies only to qiyas.
This distinction is crucial: the same approach does not apply to conflicting texts.
