الأصل الثاني/ السنة وهو باطل ضرورة من الدين وأيضاً إيجاب العمل بالقياس مشروط بكونه مفيد الظن قوي، وعند قيام كل فات الظن فيلزم أن يهدر أحدهما ليبقى الآخر قائماً فيعمل به، وليس في نفس القياسين ترجيح بالفرض فلا بد من تحكيم القلب، فما يحكم القلب بصحته يترجح على الآخر فيهدر هذا الآخر فيفيد ما يشهد القلب به الظن فيعمل به، وبما قررنا اندفع ما أورد أن الفساد الغير المعلوم لما لم يمنع وجوب العمل فيعمل بكل تخييراً، ولا حاجة إلى تحكيم القلب فافهم. واندفع أيضاً أن القياس دليل من دلائل الشرع نتيجته الوجوب والحرمة، فهو أيضاً دليل مقام لمعرفة حكم الله تعالى وجه الاندفاع أنه دليل، لكنه موضوع لإيجاب العمل بنتيجته، لا لأن نتيجته ثابتة في نفس الأمر، بل وضعه لأن يعمل به، وإن كان خطأ بنتيجته، لأن الظن في صلبه، وغاية التعارض العلم بأن أحدهما خطأ لا على التعيين وكل بنفسه موجب للظن الذي مناط الحكم، ولا يوجب كون أحدهما بخصوصه خطأ، فالتعارض فيه لا ينافي وجوب هو العمل بواحد واحد، وإنما ينافي العمل بهما معاً، فلذا أوجبنا العمل بواحد منهما بعد شهادة القلب، ثم إنه لو ضر التعارض العمل بهما هدر أو عمل بالأصل لزم العمل من غير دليل، وترك ما نصبه الشارع ليعمل به فافهم واندفع أيضاً ما قيل: إن القياس مقدم على بعض الكتاب، كالعام المخصوص وبعض السنن، فهو أقوى في إفادة الحكم منهما، فالعام المخصوص ونظائره أيضاً وضع للعمل به، وإن كان خطأ فلا بد أن يخير في تعارضهما، وجه الاندفاع أن الكتاب والسنة مطلقاً إنما وضعا لإفادة حكم الله تعالى في حدود أنفسهما، والظن إنما جاء لقصورنا بفهم المراد أو جهلنا بالنسخ ولم يوضعنا للعمل بهما وإن كان خطأ، فالتعارض فيهما يقعد الحجية للقطع بخطأ أحدهما وهو يسري في كل واحد واحد فيضر الحجية. ويوجب الرجوع إلى ما وضع للعمل بنتيجته. وإن كانت خطأ فاتضح الفرق فافهم. وهذا الدليل بعينه جار في أقوال الصحابة، إذ أقوالهم لم توضع لإفادة الحكم لاحتمال الخطأ. وإنما وجب العمل كالقياسين عند من أوجب عنده، ظناً بإصابة رأيهم، فليس أحدهما منسوخاً بالآخر، بل يكونان موضوعين لإيجاب العمل فصارا كالقياسين فتأمل .
The second principle / the Sunnah, and it is false necessarily from religion. Also, obligation to act upon qiyas is conditioned upon it producing strong probability (zann). When each of them [the two conflicting qiyas] brings loss of probability, it necessitates that one of them be discarded so that the other remains operative and is acted upon. But there is no preponderance in the two qiyas themselves by assumption, so there is no alternative but to resort to the heart's judgment (tahkim al-qalb). So whatever the heart judges to be correct preponderates over the other, and this other is discarded. Thus what the heart testifies to yields probability (zann) and is acted upon. By what we have established, the objection that unknown corruption does not prevent obligation to act, so one acts upon each by way of choice (takhayyur), and there is no need for the heart's judgment, is repelled. So understand. Also repelled is [the objection] that qiyas is a proof from the proofs of the Shari'a, its result being obligation and prohibition; so it is also a proof established for knowing the ruling of Allah, may He be exalted. [But] the point of repelling it is that it is a proof, but it is set up to obligate action upon its result, not because its result is established in actual reality; rather, it is set up to be acted upon, even if its result is wrong, because probability (zann) is ingrained in it. The limit of conflict is knowing that one of them is wrong but not specifically determined, and each in itself causes probability which is the basis of the ruling. It does not necessitate that one of them specifically is wrong. So conflict in them does not negate the obligation of acting upon one alone, but only negates acting upon both together. Hence we obligated acting upon one of them after the heart's testimony. Then if conflict necessitated discarding action upon both or acting upon the original [ruling], it would necessitate acting without evidence and abandoning what the Lawgiver established to be acted upon. So understand. Also repelled is what is said: that qiyas is given precedence over some of the Book, like the general text that is specified, and some of the Sunnah, so it is stronger in conveying the ruling than them. So the general text that is specified and its likes are also set up to be acted upon, even if wrong, so there must be choice (takhayyur) when they conflict. The point of repelling it is that the Book and Sunnah absolutely are set up to convey the ruling of Allah, may He be exalted, within their own bounds. Probability (zann) only arises due to our deficiency in understanding the intended meaning or our ignorance of abrogation. They were not set up for us to act upon them even if wrong. So conflict in them nullifies authority (hujjiyya) due to certainty that one of them is wrong, and that [certainty] pervades each one and harms authority. It necessitates resorting to what is set up to act upon its result, even if it is wrong. Thus the difference is clear, so understand. And this same proof applies to the sayings of the Companions (aqwal al-sahaba), for their sayings were not set up to convey the ruling due to possibility of error. And action upon them is only obligatory, for those who hold it obligatory, probabilistically hoping to hit their opinion. So neither of them is abrogated by the other; rather, they are set up to obligate action, so they become like two qiyas. So reflect.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage addresses the methodology for resolving conflict between two analogical deductions (qiyas) when neither has an inherent preponderance. The Hanafi position presented is that one must rely on the heart's inclination (tahkim al-qalb) to determine which qiyas to act upon. The author refutes three objections: (1) that one could arbitrarily choose any; (2) that qiyas is a proof so conflict should invalidate both; and (3) that qiyas is sometimes stronger than textual evidence, so conflict should allow choice. The author explains that qiyas is designed to be acted upon probabilistically, even if wrong, whereas textual proofs are designed to convey actual rulings, so conflict in texts destroys their authority, necessitating resort to what is set up for action. This principle is then extended to the sayings of Companions, which are like qiyas in this regard. The passage is an expansion (sharh) of a base text, providing rational arguments for the usul rule.

Key Terms
تحكيم القلب (tahkim al-qalb): Resorting to one's inner conviction or heart's judgment to determine preponderance between two conflicting qiyas when no external preponderant exists.
تخيير (takhayyur): Arbitrary choice or selection without a criterion. The passage rejects this as a valid method for resolving conflicting qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does conflict in texts (Book/Sunnah) destroy their authority, whereas conflict in qiyas does not?
A) Because texts are stronger than qiyas
B) Because texts are set up to convey actual rulings, while qiyas is set up for probabilistic action
C) Because qiyas are not real proofs
D) Because texts are infallible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of tahkim al-qalb provides a non-arbitrary method for choosing between conflicting qiyas based on the mujtahid's inner conviction, grounded in the distinct epistemic purpose of qiyas versus textual proofs.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Hanafi Definition of Tarjih and the Rejection of Preference by Multiplicity
Defines tarjih and contrasts Hanafi and Shafi'i views with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tarjih, explain why Hanafis reject tarjih by multiplicity of evidences, and contrast it with the Shafi'i definition.

Core Idea
Tarjih is manifesting an increase in one evidence over another by a factor that is not an independent proof.

The concept of tarjih (preferring one evidence over another) is central to resolving conflicts in usul al-fiqh. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition and the key dispute with the Shafi'is regarding whether multiplicity of evidences can itself be a preferring factor.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shafi'i definition
The Shafi'is define tarjih as the association of evidence with a preferring factor that gives it preponderance over its opposite in producing probability.
They also allow tarjih by multiplicity of evidences.
2
Recognize the Hanafi definition
According to the majority of Hanafis, tarjih is the manifestation of an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by that which does not stand alone as a proof.
This definition precludes tarjih by mere number of evidences.
3
Analyze the example of Aisha's report
The text gives the example that the report of Aisha (water is only from water) is preferred over the report of the Ansar because she was more knowledgeable, not because of number of narrators.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih by other factors.
4
Examine the objection about testimony
An objection is raised: if two testimonies are stronger than one, why not prefer four testimonies over two? The Hanafi response distinguishes testimony from narration; testimony has a complete cause (nisaab) that does not increase effect with more witnesses.
This shows that tarjih factors differ by type of evidence.
5
See the nuance in qiyas
Hanafis do permit tarjih by multiplicity of principles (usul) in qiyas, because that strengthens the illa (cause), which is the actual evidence. This does not contradict the rule because the extra principles add strength to the single cause.
This distinguishes between number of independent dalils and number of indicators for one cause.

Chapter: On Tarjih. It has passed. (It is in Shafi'i terminology: the association of evidence with that by which it is preferred over its opposite in producing probability, since there is no conflict in certainties according to them. These permitted tarjih by multiplicity of evidences also. (And it) i.e. tarjih (necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the preponderated (according to the majority) of usul scholars, due to certainty from the Companions and after them, so it is consensual. Also: considering the preponderated with the existence of the preponderant is contrary to reason. But then what the Shafi'is claimed is invalidated: that in a particularizer there must be participation in the origin of probability not in amount, so they permitted particularizing a general by something lower in probability. (And from it) i.e. from tarjih (is their preference) in practice (of the report of the Mother of the Believers Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, over the statement of the Ansar that 'Water is only from water' because the purified wives are more knowledgeable of this matter. (And it was objected to them (the testimony of four with the testimony of two contrary to that. For the first testimony was strengthened by the addition of its like without the second, so it should be preponderant. (They are equal. (And it was answered by commitment) to the preponderance of the first and dropping the second (as is the saying of Malik in al-Taysir and al-Shafi'i. (And) it was also answered, after conceding no preponderance, (by the distinction) between testimony and narration. How many a preference for narration does not prefer by testimony. I say: because the quorum of testimony is a complete cause for judgment, and judgment is obligatory when two testimonies exist. (And it) i.e. the complete cause (does not increase or decrease). So four and two are equal in obligating judgment, so no preference of one over the other in obligation. So understand. (And according to the majority of Hanafis, tarjih is the manifestation of an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by that which does not stand alone as a proof. So there is no tarjih by multiplicity of evidences. The apparent meaning of this statement indicates that the invalidity of tarjih by multiplicity of evidences is based on this interpretation, and it is permissible on the first. But it is not so: the dispute about tarjih by multiplicity of evidences is a conceptual dispute that does not differ with difference in interpretation; rather the two interpretations are equal in their view. For preponderance does not occur by multiplicity of evidences, because one evidence as it opposes one, opposes more. So with multiplicity of evidences, nothing is associated with the evidence by which it is preponderant. They only turned from the interpretation to this to manifest what is reality for them because it is more indicative of the intent, unlike the Shafi'i interpretation, for it has no indication to this. If you say: why do they prefer by multiplicity of principles? He said: (Preference of one analogy over another by multiplicity of principles is only valid, because the evidence is the analogy alone; for that which necessitates judgment is the cause, and it is one evidence, not the principles which are many. By multiplicity of principles, strength occurs in the cause, so it becomes preponderant over the cause of the other analogy. Then tarjih occurring between [reports of] practices is either in the text or in the chain. (Then in the text) it is by strength of indication: like muhkam (according to us is preponderant over mufassar, and on this analogize: mufassar over nass, nass over zahir, khafi over mushkil. And it is not permissible to oppose a mujmal against its divisions except after clarification, so it becomes clear in indication. Mutashabih is unknown in meaning, so there is no opposition to any of the divisions. And it has passed. (And consensus) is preponderant (over nass). And its explanation has passed. (And the general that is not particularized is preponderant over the general that is particularized, like the prohibition of sale with a condition, narrated by Abu Hanifa, and it was opposed by His statement 'And Allah has permitted sale' (Quran 2:275). So the prohibition was given precedence because it is general not particularized, and the secret is what preceded: that the unparticularized general is certain, and the particularized is probabilistic. (And the confirmed ruling) is over others because the unconfirmed is likely to be interpretable, and the confirmed does not admit interpretation or it is far. (And the narration by wording) is preponderant over meaning, i.e. narration by meaning, due to possibility of error in conveying meaning. (And what happened in his presence and he remained silent) is preponderant over what reached him and he remained silent, because the former is more indicative of approval than the latter and less probable. Like a common term between two is preponderant over one that is more probable, like common between three or more. Know that tarjih is mentioned in Shafi'i books, and there is consideration: because the common between two and the common between more, if each is accompanied by a context equally and the intended is determined, all are equal. If the context for determining the intended in one is clearer than the other, then tarjih is by clarity and obscurity, and there is no role for quantity of probability. (And the closer metaphor) is preponderant over the farther, meaning the text used in a metaphor is valid.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive chapter on tarjih (preferring one evidence over another). It begins by defining tarjih in Shafi'i terminology as associating evidence with that by which it is preferred over its opposite in producing probability, noting that they allow tarjih by multiplicity of evidences. The text then states that tarjih necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the preponderated, according to the majority of usul scholars, and it is consensual from the Companions. It then gives an example: the Hadith of Aisha that 'water is only from water' (i.e., wudu is not required unless water is discharged) is preferred over the Hadith of the Ansar, because Aisha was more knowledgeable. Objection is raised: why not prefer testimony of four over two? The answer is that testimony has a complete cause (nisaab) that does not increase or decrease, so four and two are equal in effect. The Hanafi definition is then given: tarjih is manifestation of an increase of one evidence over another by something that is not independent proof. Hence, Hanafis do not allow tarjih by number of evidences, because each evidence is considered individually; multiple evidences do not strengthen. However, they do allow tarjih by multiplicity of principles (usul) in qiyas, because the cause (illa) is strengthened. Then the text explains tarjih in the text (matn) by strength of indication: muhkam over mufassar, mufassar over nass, nass over zahir, khafi over mushkil. Mujmal cannot oppose its divisions until clarified. Mutashabih has no opposition. Then other rules: consensus over nass, unparticularized general over particularized general (example: prohibition of sale with condition over the general permission of sale), confirmed rulings over unconfirmed, narration by wording over meaning, what happened in his presence and he remained silent over what reached him and he remained silent (because presence indicates approval). Also, a common term (mushtarak) between two meanings is preferred over one with more meanings, but this is not absolute; if context clarifies, all equal. Finally, closer metaphor (majaz aqrab) is preferred over farther. This passage is foundational for understanding how Hanafi usul resolves conflicts between evidences.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): In Hanafi usul: manifesting an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by that which does not stand alone as a proof.
المحكم (al-muhkam): Text that is clear and cannot be abrogated; the highest in the Hanafi hierarchy.
العام غير المخصوص (al-amm ghayr al-makhsus): A general text that has not been particularized; it is considered qat'i (definitive) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis, is tarjih by multiplicity of evidences valid?
A) Yes, it is valid in all cases.
B) No, it is never valid.
C) Only in the case of qiyas.
D) Only if the evidences are from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in the Hanafi school is not about counting proofs but about the strength of each proof's indication.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Hanafi Hierarchy of Textual Strength for Tarjih
Lists the textual categories and rules for preference based on strength of indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of textual strength (muhkam, mufassar, nass, zahir, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih) to determine which evidence is preponderant when they conflict.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school ranks texts by clarity: muhkam is strongest, then mufassar, nass, zahir, khafi, mushkil, with mujmal and mutashabih not usable for opposition.

When two texts conflict, the Hanafi school does not simply count evidence; it evaluates the strength of the indication (dalala). This lesson presents the hierarchy of textual categories established by the Hanafi usul scholars, from the clearest (muhkam) to the most ambiguous (mutashabih).

Guided Path
1
List the textual categories
From the passage, identify the seven categories mentioned: muhkam, mufassar, nass, zahir, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, and mutashabih. Note the order of strength.
Mutashabih is the weakest; mujmal requires clarification before it can be used.
2
Understand the hierarchy
The text states that muhkam is preponderant over mufassar, mufassar over nass, nass over zahir, khafi over mushkil. This is a chain of preference based on clarity of indication.
These categories are defined by how many possibilities of interpretation they admit.
3
Apply the rule for general texts
An unparticularized general (amm ghayr makhsus) is qat'i and takes precedence over a particularized general (amm makhsus) which is zanni.
Example: the prohibition of sale with condition (general not particularized) vs. the verse 'Allah has permitted sale' (general but particularized by practice).
4
Recognize other tarjih rules
Additional rules: consensus over nass, confirmed ruling over unconfirmed, narration by wording over meaning, silent approval in presence over absent, common term between two meanings over one with more, closer metaphor over farther.
These are all factors that make one evidence stronger than another.
5
Practice identifying preponderant evidence
Given two conflicting texts, classify each according to the hierarchy and apply the relevant rule to determine which is preponderant.
Remember that mujmal and mutashabih cannot oppose other categories.

Chapter: On Tarjih. It has passed. (It is in Shafi'i terminology: the association of evidence with that by which it is preferred over its opposite in producing probability, since there is no conflict in certainties according to them. These permitted tarjih by multiplicity of evidences also. (And it) i.e. tarjih (necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the preponderated (according to the majority) of usul scholars, due to certainty from the Companions and after them, so it is consensual. Also: considering the preponderated with the existence of the preponderant is contrary to reason. But then what the Shafi'is claimed is invalidated: that in a particularizer there must be participation in the origin of probability not in amount, so they permitted particularizing a general by something lower in probability. (And from it) i.e. from tarjih (is their preference) in practice (of the report of the Mother of the Believers Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, over the statement of the Ansar that 'Water is only from water' because the purified wives are more knowledgeable of this matter. (And it was objected to them (the testimony of four with the testimony of two contrary to that. For the first testimony was strengthened by the addition of its like without the second, so it should be preponderant. (They are equal. (And it was answered by commitment) to the preponderance of the first and dropping the second (as is the saying of Malik in al-Taysir and al-Shafi'i. (And) it was also answered, after conceding no preponderance, (by the distinction) between testimony and narration. How many a preference for narration does not prefer by testimony. I say: because the quorum of testimony is a complete cause for judgment, and judgment is obligatory when two testimonies exist. (And it) i.e. the complete cause (does not increase or decrease). So four and two are equal in obligating judgment, so no preference of one over the other in obligation. So understand. (And according to the majority of Hanafis, tarjih is the manifestation of an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by that which does not stand alone as a proof. So there is no tarjih by multiplicity of evidences. The apparent meaning of this statement indicates that the invalidity of tarjih by multiplicity of evidences is based on this interpretation, and it is permissible on the first. But it is not so: the dispute about tarjih by multiplicity of evidences is a conceptual dispute that does not differ with difference in interpretation; rather the two interpretations are equal in their view. For preponderance does not occur by multiplicity of evidences, because one evidence as it opposes one, opposes more. So with multiplicity of evidences, nothing is associated with the evidence by which it is preponderant. They only turned from the interpretation to this to manifest what is reality for them because it is more indicative of the intent, unlike the Shafi'i interpretation, for it has no indication to this. If you say: why do they prefer by multiplicity of principles? He said: (Preference of one analogy over another by multiplicity of principles is only valid, because the evidence is the analogy alone; for that which necessitates judgment is the cause, and it is one evidence, not the principles which are many. By multiplicity of principles, strength occurs in the cause, so it becomes preponderant over the cause of the other analogy. Then tarjih occurring between [reports of] practices is either in the text or in the chain. (Then in the text) it is by strength of indication: like muhkam (according to us is preponderant over mufassar, and on this analogize: mufassar over nass, nass over zahir, khafi over mushkil. And it is not permissible to oppose a mujmal against its divisions except after clarification, so it becomes clear in indication. Mutashabih is unknown in meaning, so there is no opposition to any of the divisions. And it has passed. (And consensus) is preponderant (over nass). And its explanation has passed. (And the general that is not particularized is preponderant over the general that is particularized, like the prohibition of sale with a condition, narrated by Abu Hanifa, and it was opposed by His statement 'And Allah has permitted sale' (Quran 2:275). So the prohibition was given precedence because it is general not particularized, and the secret is what preceded: that the unparticularized general is certain, and the particularized is probabilistic. (And the confirmed ruling) is over others because the unconfirmed is likely to be interpretable, and the confirmed does not admit interpretation or it is far. (And the narration by wording) is preponderant over meaning, i.e. narration by meaning, due to possibility of error in conveying meaning. (And what happened in his presence and he remained silent) is preponderant over what reached him and he remained silent, because the former is more indicative of approval than the latter and less probable. Like a common term between two is preponderant over one that is more probable, like common between three or more. Know that tarjih is mentioned in Shafi'i books, and there is consideration: because the common between two and the common between more, if each is accompanied by a context equally and the intended is determined, all are equal. If the context for determining the intended in one is clearer than the other, then tarjih is by clarity and obscurity, and there is no role for quantity of probability. (And the closer metaphor) is preponderant over the farther, meaning the text used in a metaphor is valid.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive chapter on tarjih (preferring one evidence over another). It begins by defining tarjih in Shafi'i terminology as associating evidence with that by which it is preferred over its opposite in producing probability, noting that they allow tarjih by multiplicity of evidences. The text then states that tarjih necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the preponderated, according to the majority of usul scholars, and it is consensual from the Companions. It then gives an example: the Hadith of Aisha that 'water is only from water' (i.e., wudu is not required unless water is discharged) is preferred over the Hadith of the Ansar, because Aisha was more knowledgeable. Objection is raised: why not prefer testimony of four over two? The answer is that testimony has a complete cause (nisaab) that does not increase or decrease, so four and two are equal in effect. The Hanafi definition is then given: tarjih is manifestation of an increase of one evidence over another by something that is not independent proof. Hence, Hanafis do not allow tarjih by number of evidences, because each evidence is considered individually; multiple evidences do not strengthen. However, they do allow tarjih by multiplicity of principles (usul) in qiyas, because the cause (illa) is strengthened. Then the text explains tarjih in the text (matn) by strength of indication: muhkam over mufassar, mufassar over nass, nass over zahir, khafi over mushkil. Mujmal cannot oppose its divisions until clarified. Mutashabih has no opposition. Then other rules: consensus over nass, unparticularized general over particularized general (example: prohibition of sale with condition over the general permission of sale), confirmed rulings over unconfirmed, narration by wording over meaning, what happened in his presence and he remained silent over what reached him and he remained silent (because presence indicates approval). Also, a common term (mushtarak) between two meanings is preferred over one with more meanings, but this is not absolute; if context clarifies, all equal. Finally, closer metaphor (majaz aqrab) is preferred over farther. This passage is foundational for understanding how Hanafi usul resolves conflicts between evidences.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): In Hanafi usul: manifesting an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by that which does not stand alone as a proof.
المحكم (al-muhkam): Text that is clear and cannot be abrogated; the highest in the Hanafi hierarchy.
العام غير المخصوص (al-amm ghayr al-makhsus): A general text that has not been particularized; it is considered qat'i (definitive) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of text can never be used to oppose another according to the Hanafi hierarchy?
A) Mujmal
B) Mutashabih
C) Khafi
D) Mushkil

Key Takeaway
The strength of a text's indication determines its place in the hierarchy, with mujmal and mutashabih having no power to oppose clearer texts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Definition of Tarjih and Preponderance by Number of Evidences
Usul rule on the definition of tarjih and the dispute over preponderance by number of evidences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tarjih, explain why abundance of evidences does not cause preponderance, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf with the opposing view.

Core Idea
Tarjih is an increase by something that is not an independent proof — therefore numbers alone never preponderate.

This passage introduces the foundational Hanafi definition of tarjih. The author immediately applies it to the question: does having more pieces of evidence make one side stronger? The Hanafi answer is no, because the minimum number that establishes a ruling is a complete cause; adding more does not strengthen it. This leads to a direct disagreement with Malik and al-Shafi'i, who accept preponderance by number in testimony. Understanding this definition unlocks the entire system of tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Hanafi definition of tarjih
Find the phrase where tarjih is defined: 'showing an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by what is not an independent proof if it stood alone.' Write it in your own words.
This definition is quoted from 'most Hanafis'.
2
Identify the consequence: no preponderance by abundance
From the definition, the author concludes that there is no tarjih simply because there are more evidences. Why? Because the 'increase' must be by something that is not an independent proof — mere repetition does not qualify.
The opposing argument from testimony is addressed.
3
Examine the opponent's position (Malik and al-Shafi'i)
The text mentions that Malik and al-Shafi'i argued that the first testimony is strengthened by the addition of another like it, so it becomes preponderant. The author presents their view and then the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi response uses the concept of a complete cause (illa tamma).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response: the nisab as a complete cause
The author explains that the minimum requirement for testimony (two witnesses) is a complete cause — it does not increase or decrease. Therefore, four witnesses are no stronger than two; both fulfill the complete cause equally.
This is the key difference: the cause is wholly satisfied by the minimum.
5
Distinguish between testimony and analogy
The text later notes that in analogy (qiyas), abundance of principles can cause preponderance because they strengthen the cause itself, not merely repeat it. This is an exception to the general rule.
This shows the nuance: it's about the nature of the 'increase'.

الشرط) تترجح على النكرة في سياق (النفي وغيرها من الألفاظ العامة لإفادة التعليل) أي لإفادة صيغة الشرط تعليل الحكم المعلق به دون النكرة والحكم المعلل أقوى من غير المعلل . وقد يخص منه النكرة التي بعد لا التي لنفي الجنس لكونه نصاً في العموم من صيغ الشرط، وهو الأظهر (والجمع المحلى باللام (والموصول) يترجح (على المفرد (المعرف باللام أو الإضافة لأنه ربما يستعمل في الخصوص بخلاف الجمع والموصول، فإن استعمالهما فيه أقل القليل (و) الترجيح في المتن قد يكون (بالأهمية) بأن يكون الحكم المفاد بأحدهما أهم في نظر الشارع من الحكم المستفاد من الآخر، فالأهم أرجح من غيره ( كالتكليفي) من الحكم يترجح (على) الحكم الوضعي على) المذهب (الصحيح) لأن التكليفي أهم (والمقتضى للصدق على الشرعية) أي الثابت بالاقتضاء لأجل صدق الكلام يترجح على الثابت اقتضاء لأجل المشروعية عند التعارض، فإن الصدق أهم (والنهي) يترجح على الأمر، لأن دفع المفسدة المستفادة من النهي (أهم من جلب المنفعة) المستفاد من الأمر، ولذا رجح أئمتنا حديث النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة على قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها فإن ذلك وقتها» رواه مسلم فيما تعارضا والتحريم) يترجح على غيره من الأحكام لذلك والاحتياط، ولذا قدموا حديث النهي المذكور على حديث إباحة ذلك في الجمعة وقت الاستواء أو في مكة مطلقاً وقيل : بتقديم الإباحة وترجيحها على غيرها مطلقاً، وهو مختار الشيخ الأكبر صاحب الفتوحات قدس سره ) لأنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام كان يحب التخفيف على أمته والظاهر بقاء الأحكام على ما يحبه (وقيل: المحرم والموجب متساويان لا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر لأن ترجيح التحريم كان للاحتياط، وليس ههنا، لأن ترك الواجب وارتكاب الحرام بمنزلة واحدة هذا ومثبت درء الحد يترجح (على موجبه) لأن الدرء كان أهم ألا ترى أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم كيف كان يحتال
(In Shariah) - Fawatih al-Rahmut Sharh Musallam al-Thubut Part Two. With that, the first testimony is strengthened by the addition of another like it, while the second is not, so it should be preponderant; they are equal. (And it was answered by commitment) to the preponderance of the first and the fall of the second (as is the saying of Malik) in 'al-Taysir' and al-Shafi'i. (And) it was also answered, after conceding no preponderance, (by the distinction) between testimony and narration: many preponderators for narration do not preponderate testimony. I say: the issue is that the minimum requirement for testimony is a complete cause for the ruling, and the ruling is obligatory upon the existence of testimony of two (and it) i.e. the complete cause does not increase or decrease). So four and two are equal in imposing the ruling, so there is no preponderance of one over the other in imposition, so understand. (And according to most Hanafis) preponderance is (showing) an increase of one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by what is not independent) a proof if it were alone, so) there is no preponderance according to them by abundance (of evidences. The apparent meaning of this statement indicates that the invalidity of preponderance by abundance of evidences is branched on this interpretation, and it is permissible on the first, but it is not so. Indeed, the dispute about preponderance by abundance of evidences is a meaningful dispute that does not differ by difference of interpretation; rather, the two interpretations are equal according to their view, for preponderance does not occur according to them by abundance of evidences. Indeed, a single evidence as it opposes one, it opposes more. So when there is abundance of evidences, according to us, there has not accompanied the evidence what would make it preponderant. They only turned away from the interpretation to this to show what is actual according to them because it is more indicative of the intended meaning, contrary to the interpretation of the Shafi'is, for there is no indication of this in it. If you say: why then do they preponderate by abundance of principles? He said: (And it is only valid) preponderance of one of two analogies by abundance of principles, because the evidence is the analogy alone), for what necessitates the ruling is the cause, and it is a single evidence, not the principles which are many. By abundance of principles only occurs strength in the cause, so it becomes preponderant over the cause of the other analogy. Then the preponderance that occurs between the Sunnahs is either in the text or in the chain of transmission. (Then it is in the text) by strength of indication, like the muhkam (according to us it is preponderant over the mufassar, and upon this analogize, meaning the mufassar over the nass, and the nass over the zahir, and the khafi over the mushkil. And it is not valid to oppose the mujmal to its divisions except after clarification, so it becomes clear in indication. And the mutashabih is unknown in intent, so no opposing it to any of the divisions at all. And it has passed. (And ijma) is preponderant (over the nass) and its explanation has passed. (And the general, a general that is not specified, is preponderant (over) the general that is specified) like the prohibition of a sale with a condition, reported by Abu Hanifa, and it was opposed by His saying the Exalted: (And Allah has permitted sale) [al-Baqarah 275]. So the prohibition was given precedence because it is a general that is not specified, and the secret in it is what preceded: that the general not specified is qati'i, and the specified is zanni. (And) the ruling that is emphasized (is preponderant over others because the unemphasized is subject to interpretation, and the emphasized does not admit it or it is far-fetched. (And narration by wording) is preponderant over meaning (i.e., narration by meaning due to the possibility of error in conveying the meaning. (And what occurred in his presence and he remained silent) is preponderant over what reached him and he remained silent, because the first is stronger in indicating satisfaction than the second. And what is less probable, like a common term between (two) is preponderant over the more probable, like a common term between three or more. Know that preponderance is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is, and there is a consideration in it, because the common term between two and the common term between more: if each is accompanied by a context equally and the intended meaning is determined, then all are equal. If the context for determining the intended meaning in one is more evident than the other, then preponderance is by evidency and obscurity, and there is no role for fewness or multiplicity of probability. (And the closer metaphor) is preponderant over the farther, meaning that a text used in a metaphor that is closer is preponderant over another text used in a farther metaphor when they conflict. This preponderance is also mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is (because) i.e., the closer metaphor is often stronger in understanding than the farther metaphor. (So it repels what was said: that the (real) meaning is abandoned in each of them by evidence, and the metaphorical meaning is definite in each) of them (by evidence), so their indication of the metaphorical meaning is equal, so there is no effect of closeness and distance in strength of indication and weakness, so there is no basis for preponderance. The repelling is that the closer is stronger in understanding. And this repelling is itself repelled, because the farther metaphor with its specific context rushes to the mind upon hearing that text, like the rushing to the closer, because the basis of speed is the context. And it may be said: the intended meaning of preponderance of the closer metaphor over the farther is when a single speech carries both and their contexts exist, then it is interpreted as the closer. This is clear, but it has no relation to what we are concerned with, because the discussion is about conflict of two texts. The summary of what this speaker mentioned is that there is no ambiguity in a word that can bear two metaphorical meanings with a context diverting from the real, one closer and the other farther; then the closer is preponderant. (And) the metaphor (more famous in relationship and usage) is preponderant (over others). This is also mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is, and what passed applies to it. (And the conditional form) is preponderant over the indefinite in the context of (negation and other general expressions because it gives explanation) i.e., the conditional form gives explanation of the ruling attached to it, unlike the indefinite, and the explained ruling is stronger than the unexplained. Exception may be made for the indefinite after 'la' for negation of genus because it is explicit in generality from conditional forms, and that is the more apparent. (And the plural with 'al' (and the relative pronoun) is preponderant (over the singular) defined with 'al' or addition, because it may be used for particularity, unlike the plural and relative, for their use for particularity is very rare. (And) preponderance in the text may be (by importance) i.e., the ruling conveyed by one of them is more important in the view of the Lawgiver than the ruling derived from the other, so the more important is preponderant over others. (Like the taklifi) ruling is preponderant (over) the wad'i ruling according to the (correct) school, because the taklifi is more important. (And what is necessitated for truth over legality) i.e., what is established by necessity for the sake of truthfulness of speech is preponderant over what is established as a necessity for the sake of legality when they conflict, because truthfulness is more important. (And prohibition) is preponderant over command, because repelling evil derived from prohibition (is more important than attracting benefit) derived from command. Hence our imams preponderated the hadith of prohibition of prayer in disliked times over his saying (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time' reported by Muslim, when they conflicted. And prohibition) is preponderant over other rulings due to that and due to precaution. Hence they preferred the mentioned hadith of prohibition over the hadith permitting that on Friday at midday or in Mecca absolutely. And it was said: giving precedence to permissibility and preponderating it over others absolutely, and it is the choice of the greatest shaykh, author of al-Futuhat, may his secret be sanctified, because he (peace be upon him and upon his family and companions) loved to make things easy for his nation, and the apparent is that rulings remain upon what He loves. And it was said: the forbidden and the obligatory are equal, no preponderance of one over the other, because preponderance of prohibition was due to precaution, and here it is not, because abandoning the obligatory and committing the forbidden are of the same level. This, and the establisher of repelling punishment is preponderant over its establisher, because repelling was more important. Do you not see how the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) used to resort to stratagems?
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut provides a comprehensive discussion of the principles of tarjih (preponderance) in usul al-fiqh. The author begins by addressing the issue of whether increasing the number of evidences (kathrat al-adilla) can cause preponderance. He explains that according to most Hanafis, tarjih is defined as showing an increase in one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by something that is not an independent proof if it stood alone. Consequently, preponderance is not achieved by merely having more evidences, because a single proof can oppose multiple proofs. The author then contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Malik and al-Shafi'i, who accepted preponderance by number in testimony. The Hanafi position is defended by noting that the minimum requirement for testimony (nisab) is a complete cause (illa tamma) that does not increase or decrease in effect; thus four witnesses are no stronger than two. Next, the author discusses preponderance in the text (matn) of hadith. In the Hanafi school, the hierarchy of textual clarity determines preponderance: muhkam is stronger than mufassar, mufassar than nass, nass than zahir, and khafi than mushkil. Mujmal cannot oppose the other categories until it is clarified, and mutashabih is not subject to opposition at all. Then the author turns to preponderance by ijma (consensus), which takes precedence over a clear text (nass). A general term (amm) that has not been specified is preponderant over a general term that has been specified, because the former is qat'i (definitive) while the latter is zanni (speculative). An example is the hadith prohibiting a sale with a condition (reported by Abu Hanifa) which is given precedence over the Quranic verse 'And Allah has permitted sale' (2:275) because the prohibition is a general that is not specified. Emphasized rulings preponderate over unemphasized ones due to the possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) in the latter. Narration by exact wording (riwaya bil-lafz) is preponderant over narration by meaning (riwaya bil-ma'na) because of the risk of error in conveying meaning. A matter that occurred in the Prophet's presence and he remained silent is stronger in indicating approval than a matter that reached him and he remained silent. A word that is ambiguous between two meanings (mushtarak bayn ithnayn) is preponderant over one that is ambiguous among three or more, although the author notes that this principle is contested; if each is accompanied by a context, they may be equal. The author then addresses preponderance by metaphorical closeness and fame. A closer metaphor (majaz aqrab) is preponderant over a farther one, even though both abandon the real meaning, because the closer is quicker to the understanding. The author acknowledges that some object that with a clear context, both metaphors are equally quickly understood, but he defends the principle by saying it applies when a single text carries both possibilities. Similarly, a more famous metaphor (ashhar) is preponderant. Conditional forms (sigha al-shart) are preponderant over indefinite expressions in negation because they indicate the reason (ta'lil) for the ruling. An exception is the indefinite after 'la' for negation of genus, which is explicit in generality. Plurals with 'al' and relative pronouns (al-mawsul) are preponderant over singulars defined with 'al' or idafa because the latter are sometimes used for particularity. Preponderance can also be by importance: taklifi rulings (obligation, prohibition, etc.) are more important than wad'i rulings (conditions, causes, etc.), and rulings necessitated for truthfulness of speech preponderate over those necessitated for legislation. Prohibition takes precedence over command because repelling harm is more important than acquiring benefit. The author gives the example of the hadith prohibiting prayer at certain times conflicting with the hadith allowing a missed prayer to be made up at any time; the Hanafi imams preferred the prohibition. Similarly, prohibitory rulings (tahrim) are preponderant over others due to precaution. Finally, the principle of 'der' al-hudud' (repelling punishments) is preponderant over establishing punishments because avoiding punishment is more important, as shown by the Prophet's practice of seeking ways to avoid applying hadd penalties.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Showing an increase in one of two similar conflicting evidences over the other by what is not an independent proof if it stood alone.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum number required for testimony (two witnesses) which is a complete cause (illa tamma) for the ruling.
العلة التامة (al-illa al-tamma): A complete cause that does not increase or decrease in its effect; fulfilling the minimum satisfies it entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that four witnesses are not stronger than two in testimony?
A) Because four witnesses are less reliable than two.
B) Because the minimum requirement (nisab) is a complete cause that does not increase in effect.
C) Because testimony is not subject to preponderance at all.
D) Because the Quran requires only two witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of tarjih excludes preponderance by independent proofs, so abundance of evidences alone never creates preponderance; the increase must be qualitative, not quantitative.

Tarjih by Predominance: Specification over Interpretation
Explaining tarjih by predominance: preference of specification over interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that takhsis is preferred over ta'wil when reconciling conflicting texts and explain that this preference is based on the greater frequency of takhsis in the Shariah.

Core Idea
When reconciling conflicting texts, specification (takhsis) outweighs interpretation (ta'wil) because it is the more common method.

In Hanafi usul, when two texts appear contradictory, mujtahids must reconcile them. Two primary methods are specification (making one an exception) and interpretation (reinterpreting). This lesson explores why the Hanafi school prefers specification: it is more frequent in the Shariah and thus yields stronger conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the conflict
Identify two texts that seem to contradict each other.
2
Identify reconciliation methods
Two methods are possible: takhsis (specifying one text as an exception) or ta'wil (interpreting one text figuratively).
3
Apply the tarjih rule
According to the Hanafi school, takhsis is given preponderance over ta'wil because it is more common in the Shariah.
This is a tarjih by predominance (al-aghalliyya).
4
Understand the epistemological basis
Conjecture (zann) follows the majority pattern; since most reconciliation in the Quran and Sunnah occurs through specification, the zann from takhsis is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الترجيح في المتن قد يكون بالأغلبية كالتخصيص) يترجح (على التأويل) يعني إذا تعارض نصان وتعارض وجوه جمعهما كتخصيص أحدهما وتأويل الآخر يترجح التخصيص على التأويل لكثرة التخصيص بالنسبة إلى التأويل كما تقدم أنه يجمع بتخصيص عند معارضة الخاص وموافقة القياس) تترجح على المخالفة) يعني إذا تعارض نصان وأحدهما موافق للقياس والآخر مخالف له، فالموافق مرجح (على) المذهب (الأصح) لا لأن الموافق يترجح بانضمام القياس إليه، كيف والقياس حجة لو انفرد بنفسه وما يكون حجة بانفراده لا يقع به الترجيح، بل لأن الغالب في الأحكام ما يكون معللاً، ويقاس عليه غيره، والظن تابع للأغلب، فالظن بثبوته أقوى
And preponderance in the text may be by predominance: specification is preponderant over interpretation. That is, if two texts conflict and the methods of reconciliation conflict—such as specifying one and interpreting the other—specification is given preponderance over interpretation due to its greater frequency relative to interpretation, as previously mentioned that they reconcile by specification when a specific opposes a general. And agreement with analogy (qiyas) is preponderant over opposition. That is, if two texts conflict and one agrees with qiyas and the other opposes it, the one that agrees is preferred, according to the soundest madhhab. This is not because the agreeing text gains strength from qiyas joining it—since qiyas is a proof by itself and a proof by itself does not confer preponderance—but because the majority of rulings are rationalized (mu'allal) and analogized to others, and conjecture follows the majority, so conjecture about its establishment is stronger.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers two tarjih principles based on predominance (aghlabiyya). First: specification (takhsis) is preferred over interpretation (ta'wil) when reconciling conflicting texts, because specification is a more common method. Second: a text that agrees with qiyas is preferred over one that opposes it. The reason is not that qiyas adds weight (since it is a standalone proof), but rather that most Islamic rulings are based on a rational cause and are analogized; therefore, what aligns with the majority pattern carries stronger conjecture. This reflects a Hanafi methodological stance that the majority of rulings are mu'allal (attached to an effective cause).

Key Terms
التخصيص (al-takhsīs): The specification of a general text (amm) by a specific text (khass).
التأويل (al-ta'wīl): Interpretation that diverts a word from its apparent meaning to a secondary meaning based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prefer specification (takhsis) over interpretation (ta'wil) when reconciling conflicting texts?
A) Because specification is more logically sound.
B) Because specification is more frequent in the Shariah.
C) Because interpretation is a weaker argument.
D) Because specification always preserves the literal meaning.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when two reconciliation methods conflict, the more common one (specification) is given preponderance.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Tarjih by Predominance: Agreement with Qiyas over Opposition
Explaining tarjih by predominance: preference of agreement with qiyas over opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that a text agreeing with qiyas is preferred over one opposing it, and identify the basis as the prevalence of mu'allal rulings in the Shariah.

Core Idea
A text that aligns with qiyas is preponderant over one that opposes it, because most Shariah rulings are based on rational cause (mu'allal) and analogical reasoning is the norm.

When two texts conflict and one agrees with analogical reasoning (qiyas) while the other does not, the Hanafi school gives preference to the one in agreement. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: it is not because qiyas adds authority, but because the majority of rulings in the Shariah are mu'allal—attached to a cause—so what aligns with the norm carries stronger conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting texts
Find two texts that appear contradictory, one of which aligns with qiyas and the other opposes it.
2
Recognize the tarjih principle
The text that agrees with qiyas is given preponderance over the one that opposes it.
This is the soundest view of the madhhab.
3
Understand the reason
The reason is not that qiyas adds weight, but because the majority of Shariah rulings are mu'allal (have rational causes) and are analogized to others.
Thus, what agrees with the majority pattern is more likely.
4
Apply the rule
When faced with a choice, opt for the interpretation that aligns with qiyas, as it yields stronger conjecture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الترجيح في المتن قد يكون بالأغلبية كالتخصيص) يترجح (على التأويل) يعني إذا تعارض نصان وتعارض وجوه جمعهما كتخصيص أحدهما وتأويل الآخر يترجح التخصيص على التأويل لكثرة التخصيص بالنسبة إلى التأويل كما تقدم أنه يجمع بتخصيص عند معارضة الخاص وموافقة القياس) تترجح على المخالفة) يعني إذا تعارض نصان وأحدهما موافق للقياس والآخر مخالف له، فالموافق مرجح (على) المذهب (الأصح) لا لأن الموافق يترجح بانضمام القياس إليه، كيف والقياس حجة لو انفرد بنفسه وما يكون حجة بانفراده لا يقع به الترجيح، بل لأن الغالب في الأحكام ما يكون معللاً، ويقاس عليه غيره، والظن تابع للأغلب، فالظن بثبوته أقوى
And preponderance in the text may be by predominance: specification is preponderant over interpretation. That is, if two texts conflict and the methods of reconciliation conflict—such as specifying one and interpreting the other—specification is given preponderance over interpretation due to its greater frequency relative to interpretation, as previously mentioned that they reconcile by specification when a specific opposes a general. And agreement with analogy (qiyas) is preponderant over opposition. That is, if two texts conflict and one agrees with qiyas and the other opposes it, the one that agrees is preferred, according to the soundest madhhab. This is not because the agreeing text gains strength from qiyas joining it—since qiyas is a proof by itself and a proof by itself does not confer preponderance—but because the majority of rulings are rationalized (mu'allal) and analogized to others, and conjecture follows the majority, so conjecture about its establishment is stronger.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers two tarjih principles based on predominance (aghlabiyya). First: specification (takhsis) is preferred over interpretation (ta'wil) when reconciling conflicting texts, because specification is a more common method. Second: a text that agrees with qiyas is preferred over one that opposes it. The reason is not that qiyas adds weight (since it is a standalone proof), but rather that most Islamic rulings are based on a rational cause and are analogized; therefore, what aligns with the majority pattern carries stronger conjecture. This reflects a Hanafi methodological stance that the majority of rulings are mu'allal (attached to an effective cause).

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning, extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).
المعلل (al-mu'allal): A ruling that is attached to a rational cause (illa), as opposed to a purely devotional ruling (ta'abbudi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prefer a text that agrees with qiyas over one that opposes it?
A) Because qiyas is a decisive proof.
B) Because the majority of Shariah rulings are mu'allal and analogized.
C) Because disagreement with qiyas makes the text unreliable.
D) Because qiyas overrides textual evidence.

Key Takeaway
Agreement with qiyas gives preponderance not due to qiyas' own authority, but because the Shariah predominantly operates through cause-based rulings.

Qiyas as a Valid Basis for Ijma: Hanafi Proof and Rebuttal
Arguing that qiyas can serve as a shar'i basis for ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument that qiyas can be a mustanad for ijma and distinguish it from the textual implication (dalalat al-nass) view, applying the proof chain approach.

Core Idea
Qiyas, even though zanni, can ground ijma just as zanni Quranic texts do.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a central usul question: can analogical reasoning (qiyas) serve as the evidentiary basis (mustanad) for an ijma? The Hanafi school affirms, against the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir, and backs it with the Companions' reasoning for Abu Bakr's caliphate. You will unpack the proof structure and the counterarguments, learning how the Hanafi usul framework validates qiyas as a legitimate source for consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and parties
State the mas'alah: can qiyas be a valid mustanad for ijma? Note the opposing views: Zahiris and Ibn Jarir either forbid it rationally or deny its occurrence.
The Hanafi position is that it is permissible and has occurred.
2
Analyze the Hanafi position and key premise
The Hanafi's main argument: the speculative nature of qiyas is not a disqualifier, since even apparent meanings of the Quran are speculative and yet can be bases for ijma.
This parallels the Hanafi classification of zanni adillah.
3
Examine the historical evidence
Review the Companions' reasoning for Abu Bakr's caliphate: they analogized from his leading prayer (religious matter) to his suitability for worldly leadership, citing 'radiya li amri dinina afala nardaka li amri dunyana'.
This is qiyas jaliy, as per Hanafi classification.
4
Evaluate the objection of textual implication
Some argue that this reasoning is not qiyas but dalalat al-nass (implication of the text), because the priority is understood from language itself. Understand the objection.
This objection was raised in al-Tahrir.
5
Assess the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: understanding the ratio legis (manat) here is not purely linguistic but requires intellectual inference, making it qiyas. The Companions' hesitation about the caliphate shows no clear text, so it must be qiyas.
The author also points to the hadith in Sahih Muslim as indirect indication.

مسألة: جاز كون المستند قياساً خلافاً للظاهرية وابن جرير الطبري (فبعضهم منع الجواز) عقلاً (وبعضهم منع الوقوع) وإن جاز عقلاً (والآحاد ) أي أخبار الآحاد (قيل: كالقياس) اختلافاً لنا لا مانع يقدّر في القياس من وقوعه سنداً (إلا الظنية) وإلا فهو حجة من الله تعالى (وليست) الظنية (مانعة كظاهر الكتاب فإنه ظني، وقد يقع سنداً للإجماع (وقد وقع قياس الإمامة الكبرى وهي الخلافة العامة (على إمامة الصلاة فقيل : رضيك لأمر ديننا أفلا نرضاك لأمر دنيانا) في «التيسير»: قال ابن مسعود : لما قبض النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم قال الأنصار : منا أمير ومنكم أمير ، فأتاهم عمر فقال : ألستم تعلمون أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم أمر أبا بكر أن يصلي بالناس، فأيكم تطيب نفسه أن يتقدم أبا بكر؟ فقالوا نعوذ بالله أن نتقدم أبا بكر حديث حسن أخرجه أحمد والدارقطني عن أمير المؤمنين علي قال له قائل حدثنا عن أبي بكر قال : ذاك رجل سماه الله الصديق على لسان جبريل خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم رضيه لديننا فنرضاه لدنيانا (قيل) في «التحرير» (فيه نظر لأنهم أثبتوه بأولى فإن من إمامة الصلاة فدلالة النص ما يكون فهم المناط فيه لغة وأما ههنا (ففهم المناط لغة ممنوعة لتوقف أمير المؤمنين (علي) وغيره واتفاقهم على عدم النص في الخلافة فافهم وفيه شيء، فإن صلوح أمير المؤمنين الصديق الأكبر للإمامة كان ثابتاً عندهم قطعاً، وإنما كان بحثهم في الأولوية من الصالحين ولا شك أن من كان أولى بإمامة الصلاة فإنه لكونه أفضل . ومن هو أفضل أولى بالإمامة الكبرى فاندفع الأول، والأمر بالتقديم فيما كان أهم وموجباً للصفات الكاملة الفاضلة يفهم منه عرفاً أنه أولى في أمر فيه مدخل لتلك الصفات، وأما توقف أمير المؤمنين علي فلم يكن لشبهة في أولويته بالإمامة بل لما مر فعدم فهمه ممنوع ولو سلم عدم الفهم فالدلالة ربما تكون ظنية وأما قولهم إنه لا نص فمعناه لا نص جلي على هذا، والحق أن أمره صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إياه بإمامة الصلاة كان إشارة إلى تقدمه في الإمامة الكبرى على ما يقتضيه ما في صحيح مسلم : ادعي أبا بكر أباك وأخاك حتى أكتب كتاباً إني أخاف أن يتمنى متمن ويقول أنا أولى ويأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر وفي رواية : أنا ولا ويأبى الله الخ، قال ذلك جواباً لما قالت أم المؤمنين : أبو بكر لا يملك نفسه حين يقوم
Issue: It is permissible for the basis to be qiyas, contrary to the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. Some of them forbade it rationally, and some forbade its occurrence even if rationally permissible. And ahad hadith was said to be like qiyas in terms of disagreement. For us: There is no impediment in qiyas from occurring as a basis except its speculative nature. Otherwise it is a proof from Allah. And speculative nature is not a preventative, like the apparent meaning of the Book, which is speculative and yet occurs as a basis for ijma. And indeed, there occurred the qiyas of the greater imamate, i.e., the general caliphate, upon the imamate of prayer. So it was said: He approved you for our religious matters, should we not approve you for our worldly matters? In al-Taysir: Ibn Mas'ud said: When the Prophet (peace be upon him) passed away, the Ansar said: An amir from us and an amir from you. So Umar came to them and said: Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) commanded Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer? So which of you can bear to step forward ahead of Abu Bakr? They said: We seek refuge with Allah from stepping forward ahead of Abu Bakr. A hasan hadith narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni from the Commander of the Faithful Ali: A questioner asked him: Tell us about Abu Bakr. He said: That man whom Allah called al-Siddiq upon the tongue of Jibril, the Caliph of the Messenger of Allah (SAW), he approved him for our religion so we approve him for our worldly affairs. It was said in al-Tahrir: There is a problem because they established it by priority (firstness): whoever is preferred in a religious matter is more deserving to be preferred in a worldly matter. And this is the implication of the text, not qiyas. So the basis then is the text, not qiyas. I say: We do not accept the priority of leading prayer in all cases. A man may be more deserving to lead prayer without being more deserving for worldly leadership. Even if we accept the priority of leading prayer, the implication of the text is understanding the ratio legis through language. But here, understanding the ratio legis through language is precluded due to the hesitation of the Commander of the Faithful Ali and others and their agreement that there is no explicit text about the caliphate. Ponder. There is something: The suitability of the greatest truthful commander for the imamate was established for them with certainty; they were only disputing about priority among those suitable. And there is no doubt that whoever is more deserving to lead prayer, it is because he is better. And whoever is better is more deserving of the greater imamate. So the first objection is removed. And the command to give precedence in what is most important and necessitates complete virtuous qualities is understood customarily that he is more deserving in a matter where those qualities are relevant. The hesitation of Ali was not due to doubt about his priority but for other reasons. So the lack of understanding is prevented. Even if we accept the lack of understanding, the indication may be speculative. And their saying that there is no text means there is no clear text on this. The truth is that the Prophet's command for Abu Bakr to lead prayer was an indication of his precedence in the greater imamate, as required by what is in Sahih Muslim: 'Call for me Abu Bakr your father and your brother so that I may write a document, for I fear that someone will wish and say I am more deserving, but Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And in another narration: 'I refuse and Allah refuses etc.' He said that in response to Aisha's saying: Abu Bakr cannot control himself when he stands...
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific mas'alah: Can qiyas (analogy) serve as a valid basis (mustanad) for ijma? The Hanafi position is yes, against the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari who either deny its rational permissibility or its actual occurrence. The author argues that the speculative nature of qiyas is not a disqualifier, since even the apparent meaning of the Quran is speculative and yet it can be a basis for ijma. A historical example is given: the selection of Abu Bakr as caliph was based on qiyas from his leading prayer. The author discusses objections: some claimed it was not qiyas but textual implication (dalalat al-nass). The author defends the qiyas view by analyzing the hadith and the reasoning of the Companions. The passage shows the complexity of identifying the type of evidence used in ijma, and how Hanafi usul recognizes qiyas as a legitimate source.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction deriving a ruling from an original case to a new case based on common illah.
الإمامة الكبرى (al-imama al-kubra): The greater imamate, i.e., the general caliphate.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): Implication of the text where the ratio legis is understood from the language itself.
المستند (al-mustanad): The evidentiary basis upon which an ijma is founded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main example used in this passage to argue that qiyas can be a basis for ijma?
A) The prohibition of wine.
B) The caliphate of Abu Bakr.
C) The number of prayers.
D) The inheritance of grandparents.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates qiyas as a legitimate mustanad for ijma, exemplified by the Companions' reasoning for Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Qiyas as a Valid Sanad for Ijma': Hanafi Position and Evidence
Defending qiyas as a valid sanad for ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position that qiyas can be a sanad for ijma', apply the speculative nature argument, and analyze the historical examples to defend the position.

Core Idea
Qiyas, though speculative, can be a sanad for ijma', just like the apparent meaning of the Qur'an.

In this passage, the author defends the permissibility of qiyas as a basis for consensus against the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. The key argument is that speculation (zanniyya) does not prevent a proof from being used as a sanad, as we see with the apparent meaning of the Qur'an. To support this, two historical examples are cited: the appointment of Abu Bakr based on his leading prayer, and the punishment for drinking being equated with slander. We will examine these proofs and the Hanafi reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing views
State the Zahiri and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari positions: some reject qiyas as sanad rationally, some reject its occurrence.
2
Examine the zanniyya argument
Understand that the author uses the analogy of zahir al-kitab (apparent meaning of Quran) which is also speculative but used as sanad.
Key phrase: 'وليست الظنية مانعة كظاهر الكتاب'.
3
Analyze the Abu Bakr example
Determine whether the Companions' reasoning was qiyas or dalalah al-nass. The author argues it was indication, not direct text.
Consider the hadith from Sahih Muslim.
4
Analyze the wine punishment example
Examine the analogy of drinking to slander based on intoxication leading to slander. Note that some claim it's istidlal, not qiyas.
Ali's statement: 'إذا شرب سكر، وإذا سكر هذى، وإذا هذى افترى'.
5
Conclude the Hanafi proof
Synthesize that both examples demonstrate that qiyas can be a valid sanad, and speculation does not invalidate it.
The Hanafi response to the first objection: opposition to qiyas is not universal; consensus can override.

المفترين) قيل (هذا استدلال لا قياس أقول : الاستدلال إنما يتم لو ثبت أن كل مفتر قطعاً أو ظناً، فعليه ثمانون) لأنه لا بد من كلية الكبرى (ولم يثبت ، نعم يصح أن الشارب كأنه قاذف لأن المظنة كالمئنة) فأعطى ما يفضي إلى الشيء حكمه كتحريم مقدمات الزنا) لكن لا بد حينئذ من اثبات أن حكم القذف ثابت فيما يفضي إليه وفي المشهور أنه قياس الشرب على القذف بجامع الافتراء، وفيه أنه يلزم أن يثبت الحد في كل افتراء، وجوابه أنه قياس بجامع الافتراء الخاص فتأمل فيه (ثم أقول المستند أعم من (المثبت لأن الشيء ربما يكون مستنداً، ولا يكون مثبتاً (كقطعي سنده ظني) فإن هذا السند لا يكون مثبتاً للقطع ومن ههنا لا يكون القياس مثبتاً للحد عندنا للحد وذلك لأن الإجماع رافع للشبهة المانعة عن إثبات الحدّ فالحد ههنا ثبت بالإجماع والقياس مستند (فاندفع توهم التناقض بين الكلامين الحدود لا تثبت بالقياس، والقياس يصلح سنداً للإجماع لاثبات الحدود (كما في التقرير وهذا لا يسمن ولا يغني من جوع. فإن الفتوى لما كان حراماً من غير دليل، فأهل الإجماع من أين علموا الحدّ من القياس؟ فهو المثبت أو من غيره، وهو مفروض الانتفاء، وإن قيل : القياس ليس بمثبت بل مظهر، قلت: الكلام في هذا الإظهار، فإن الحنفية يمنعونه في الحدود، بل نقول : الصحابة أجمعوا بهذا القياس على حد الشرب، فإثباته الحدّ مجمع عليه ولا مخلص إلا أن يمنعوا كونه قياساً يقولوا إنه حكم بأن هذه المظنة قائمة مقام المئنة بالسماع، فإنه قد ثبت إقامة الحد في زمن الرسول ، فهذا نقل بحاصله فتأمل فيه المنكرون (قالوا: (أولاً) لو وقع القياس سنداً لما مخالفته، لأن المخالفة حينئذ مخالفة الإجماع و(الإجماع منعقد على جواز مخالفته، قلنا لا نسلم الإجماع على جواز مخالفته مطلقاً، بل على جواز مخالفته قبل: الإجماع، أقول) انعقد الإجماع على جواز مخالفته من حيث إنه قياس وههنا إنما امتنع مخالفته من حيث إنه مجمع عليه (و) قالوا (ثانياً) القياس اختلف فيه فلا يخلو عصر ما من نفاته) فلا ينعقد على طبقه
