الإجماع، فإن النافي لا يستدل به قلنا : الخلاف حادث فلا نسلم عدم خلو العصر عن نفاته (و) أيضاً الدليل (منقوض بالعموم فإنه أيضاً مختلف فيه أقول : على أن عدم الخلو ممنوع) بعد تسليم الاختلاف من القديم أيضاً، فإنه يجوز أن لا يبقى في عصر من يتمذهب بنفيه تأمل فيه، والأولى أن يقال : إن عدم خلو عصر عن نفاته لا يلزم أن يكون النافي ممن هو أهل الإجماع، بل يجوز أن يكون من المبتدعة أو غير مجتهد فافهم.
Arguments. Issue: It is permissible for the proof to be qiyas, contrary to the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. Some of them prohibit it rationally, some prohibit its occurrence even if rationally permissible. And ahad (i.e. solitary reports) were said to be like qiyas in disagreement. For us, there is no preventing factor in qiyas from occurring as a proof except its speculation. Otherwise it is a proof from Allah. And speculation is not a preventer, like the apparent meaning of the Book (zahir al-kitab) which is speculative, yet it occurs as a proof for consensus. And indeed there occurred the analogy of the greater leadership (i.e. the general caliphate) upon the leadership of prayer. So it was said: ‘He is pleasing to you for our religious matters; should we not please him for our worldly matters?’ In al-Taysir: Ibn Mas'ud said: When the Prophet was taken, the Ansar said: An amir from us and an amir from you. Then Umar came to them and said: Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah ordered Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer? So which of you would be pleased to step ahead of Abu Bakr? They said: We seek refuge in Allah from stepping ahead of Abu Bakr. A good hadith narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni from Amir al-Mu'minin Ali: someone asked him about Abu Bakr, he said: That man whom Allah called al-Siddiq by the tongue of Jibril, the successor of the Messenger of Allah, he pleased him for our religion, so we please him for our world. It was said in al-Tahrir: There is consideration in this, because they established it by awla (priority): whoever is advanced in a religious matter is more entitled to be advanced in a worldly one. That is dalalah al-nass (textual indication), not qiyas. So the proof is the text, not qiyas. I (the author) say: We do not accept the priority of leading prayer, for a man may be more entitled to lead prayer without being more entitled to worldly leadership. And even if priority of leading prayer is granted, dalalah al-nass is understanding the legal cause (manat) linguistically, but here understanding the legal cause linguistically is prevented because of the hesitation of Amir al-Mu'minin Ali and others and their agreement that there is no text on the caliphate, so understand. And there is something in it: the suitability of Amir al-Mu'minin al-Siddiq al-Akbar for leadership was definitely established among them, and their discussion was only about priority among the suitable. No doubt that whoever is more entitled to lead prayer is because he is more excellent, and whoever is more excellent is more entitled to the greater leadership. So the first objection is refuted. The command to advance in what is most important and necessitates perfect virtuous qualities is understood customarily as being more entitled in a matter where those qualities are relevant. As for the hesitation of Amir al-Mu'minin Ali, it was not due to doubt about his priority but for reasons mentioned, so lack of understanding is not accepted. Even if lack of understanding is accepted, the indication might be speculative. As for their saying that there is no text, it means there is no explicit text on this. The truth is that the Prophet's order to him to lead prayer was an indication of his precedence in the greater caliphate, as required by what is in Sahih Muslim: 'Call Abu Bakr, your father and brother, so that I may write a document; I fear that someone may wish and say I am more entitled, but Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' In another narration: 'I and Allah refuses...' etc. He said that in response to the Mother of the Believers saying: 'Abu Bakr cannot control himself when he stands.' The third principle of consensus: (in your position if you would order, O Umar). And this clearly indicates that his advancement for prayer was so that no one would say: I am more entitled to leadership. So preserve it and verify it, for it is the truth and will benefit you on the Day of Judgment. And indeed there occurred the analogy of the punishment for drinking upon the punishment for slander. Amir al-Mu'minin Ali, may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, said when Amir al-Mu'minin Umar consulted about the man who drinks wine: I think we should punish him eighty stripes, for when he drinks he becomes intoxicated, when intoxicated he raves, when raves he slanders, so I see upon him the punishment of slanderers. It was said: This is istidlal (deduction from principle) not qiyas. I say: The deduction is only complete if it is established that every slanderer definitely or speculatively receives eighty stripes, because the major premise must be universal, but that is not established. Yes, it is correct that the drinker is like a slanderer because the mazinnah (presumptive indication) is like the mi'innah (certain indication). Thus, something that leads to a thing is given its ruling, like the prohibition of preliminaries to zina. But then it must be established that the ruling of slander is established for what leads to it. In the well-known view, it is qiyas of drinking on slander by the commonality of slander. In it, it necessitates that the punishment is established for every slander. Its answer is that it is qiyas by the commonality of specific slander, so ponder. Then I say: The proof is more general than the establisher, because something may be a proof but not an establisher, like something whose chain is qat'i but its text is zanni, for this proof does not establish certainty. And from here, qiyas does not establish the punishment for us, because consensus removes the doubt preventing the establishment of the punishment. So the punishment here is established by consensus, and qiyas is the proof. Thus the accusation of contradiction between the two statements—'punishments are not established by qiyas' and 'qiyas is valid as a proof for consensus to establish punishments'—is repelled. As in al-Taqrir: This neither fattens nor satisfies hunger. For when giving a fatwa is prohibited without a proof, how did the people of consensus know the punishment from qiyas? It is the establisher or something else, but the latter is assumed absent. If it is said: qiyas is not an establisher but a revealer, I say: The discussion is about this revealing, for the Hanafis forbid it in punishments. Rather we say: The Companions agreed by this qiyas on the punishment for drinking, so its establishment is a matter of consensus. There is no escape except to deny that it is qiyas, saying that it is a ruling that this mazinnah stands in place of the mi'innah by hearing (sam'), for the establishment of punishment in the time of the Messenger is confirmed, so this is a transmission of its essence, so ponder. The deniers said: Firstly, if qiyas occurs as a proof, it would be impossible to oppose it, because opposition then would be opposition to consensus, and consensus is established on the permissibility of opposing it (i.e., qiyas). We say: We do not accept that consensus is established on the permissibility of opposing it absolutely, but on the permissibility of opposing it before consensus. I (the author) say: Consensus was established on the permissibility of opposing it insofar as it is qiyas, but here opposition is prohibited because it is a matter of consensus. And they said: Secondly, qiyas is disputed; there is no era devoid of those who reject it, so consensus cannot be formed upon it, because the rejecter cannot be used as evidence. We say: The disagreement is recent, so we do not accept that there is no era devoid of its rejecters. Also the argument is refuted by generality (al-umum), which is also disputed. I say: That there is no era devoid of rejecters is prevented even if pre-existing disagreement is granted, because it is possible that in an era there remains no one who adopts its rejection. Ponder. The better way to say is that the lack of an era devoid of its rejecters does not necessitate that the rejecter is among the people qualified for consensus; rather it is possible that he is an innovator or non-mujtahid, so understand.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive usul dispute on whether qiyas (analogy) can serve as a sanad (proof basis) for ijma' (consensus), against the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. The author first states the Hanafi position that qiyas is permissible as a sanad, just like ahad reports, because its speculative nature (zanniyya) does not prevent it—similar to the zahir (apparent meaning) of the Qur'an which is also speculative yet used as sanad. Two historical examples are given: (1) The appointment of Abu Bakr as caliph (imamah kubra) based on his leading prayer (imamah sughra)—some claim this is qiyas, others claim it is dalalah al-nass (textual implication). The author engages in detailed analysis, ultimately arguing that the Prophet's action was an indication of Abu Bakr's precedence. (2) The punishment for drinking wine being set at eighty lashes by analogy with qadhf (slander), based on the statement attributed to Ali. Some argue this is not qiyas but istidlal. The author then discusses the relationship between the sanad and the 'muthbit' (establishing proof), asserting that qiyas can be a sanad even if it does not directly establish the ruling; consensus removes doubt. Finally, the objections of the deniers are rebutted: (a) that consensus would make opposition impossible but consensus allows opposing qiyas—answer: consensus is only on opposing before consensus; (b) that qiyas is always disputed so consensus cannot be formed—answer: possible that no rejecters remain, or rejecters may be non-mujtahids. The passage ends with the conclusion that qiyas can indeed be a sanad for ijma'.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause (illa).
مستند (sanad): The evidentiary basis that supports a ruling; can be qiyas, ahad report, etc.
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of mujtahids on a ruling; when formed on a qiyas-based opinion, the qiyas becomes part of the ijma'.
ظنية (zanniyya): Speculative or probable, as opposed to qat'i (definitive).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author compare qiyas to zahir al-kitab in the passage?
A) To show that both are qat'i.
B) To argue that speculative proofs can be sanad for ijma'.
C) To prove that qiyas is stronger than the apparent meaning.
D) To reject both as sources.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas, though speculative, can serve as a valid sanad for ijma', just like the apparent meaning of the Qur'an.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Refuting Objections to Qiyas as Sanad for Ijma'
Refuting objections to qiyas as sanad for ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main objections raised against qiyas as a sanad for ijma' and articulate the Hanafi responses to each.

Core Idea
Objections to qiyas as sanad fail because consensus overrides opposability and rejecters may be unqualified.

The passage presents two objections from the deniers: (1) if qiyas were a sanad, opposition would be impossible, yet consensus allows opposing qiyas; (2) qiyas is always disputed so no era is free of rejecters. The Hanafi school refutes both, showing that consensus only prohibits opposition after it is formed, and that rejecters may be non-mujtahids or may disappear. We will analyze these rebuttals.

Guided Path
1
State the first objection
The deniers say: if qiyas is a sanad for ijma', then opposing that ijma' would be impossible, but consensus allows opposing qiyas because qiyas itself is not binding.
Objection 1: 'لو وقع القياس سنداً لما مخالفته لأن المخالفة حينئذ مخالفة الإجماع والإجماع منعقد على جواز مخالفته'
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to the first objection
The Hanafi response distinguishes between opposing qiyas before consensus and after. Consensus itself prohibits opposition, not the qiyas qua qiyas.
Key: 'قلنا لا نسلم الإجماع على جواز مخالفته مطلقاً، بل على جواز مخالفته قبل الإجماع.'
3
State the second objection
The deniers argue that qiyas is always disputed, so there is never an era without its rejecters, making consensus impossible.
Objection 2: 'القياس اختلف فيه فلا يخلو عصر ما من نفاته'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the second objection
The Hanafi response: disagreements may be of recent origin; it is possible that in some era no rejecters remain; furthermore, rejecters may be non-mujtahids or innovators, not counted in consensus.
Key: 'الخلاف حادث' and 'يجوز أن لا يبقى في عصر من يتمذهب بنفيه' and 'يجوز أن يكون من المبتدعة أو غير مجتهد'
5
Evaluate the overall strength
The Hanafi responses effectively show that the objections do not preclude the possibility of qiyas forming a valid sanad for ijma'. Consider the nuance: opposition is allowed before consensus, and rejecters may not be qualified.

صح
الإجماع، فإن النافي لا يستدل به قلنا : الخلاف حادث فلا نسلم عدم خلو العصر عن نفاته (و) أيضاً الدليل (منقوض بالعموم فإنه أيضاً مختلف فيه أقول : على أن عدم الخلو ممنوع) بعد تسليم الاختلاف من القديم أيضاً، فإنه يجوز أن لا يبقى في عصر من يتمذهب بنفيه تأمل فيه، والأولى أن يقال : إن عدم خلو عصر عن نفاته لا يلزم أن يكون النافي ممن هو أهل الإجماع، بل يجوز أن يكون من المبتدعة أو غير مجتهد فافهم.
Arguments. Issue: It is permissible for the proof to be qiyas, contrary to the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. Some of them prohibit it rationally, some prohibit its occurrence even if rationally permissible. And ahad (i.e. solitary reports) were said to be like qiyas in disagreement. For us, there is no preventing factor in qiyas from occurring as a proof except its speculation. Otherwise it is a proof from Allah. And speculation is not a preventer, like the apparent meaning of the Book (zahir al-kitab) which is speculative, yet it occurs as a proof for consensus. And indeed there occurred the analogy of the greater leadership (i.e. the general caliphate) upon the leadership of prayer. So it was said: ‘He is pleasing to you for our religious matters; should we not please him for our worldly matters?’ In al-Taysir: Ibn Mas'ud said: When the Prophet was taken, the Ansar said: An amir from us and an amir from you. Then Umar came to them and said: Do you not know that the Messenger of Allah ordered Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer? So which of you would be pleased to step ahead of Abu Bakr? They said: We seek refuge in Allah from stepping ahead of Abu Bakr. A good hadith narrated by Ahmad and al-Daraqutni from Amir al-Mu'minin Ali: someone asked him about Abu Bakr, he said: That man whom Allah called al-Siddiq by the tongue of Jibril, the successor of the Messenger of Allah, he pleased him for our religion, so we please him for our world. It was said in al-Tahrir: There is consideration in this, because they established it by awla (priority): whoever is advanced in a religious matter is more entitled to be advanced in a worldly one. That is dalalah al-nass (textual indication), not qiyas. So the proof is the text, not qiyas. I (the author) say: We do not accept the priority of leading prayer, for a man may be more entitled to lead prayer without being more entitled to worldly leadership. And even if priority of leading prayer is granted, dalalah al-nass is understanding the legal cause (manat) linguistically, but here understanding the legal cause linguistically is prevented because of the hesitation of Amir al-Mu'minin Ali and others and their agreement that there is no text on the caliphate, so understand. And there is something in it: the suitability of Amir al-Mu'minin al-Siddiq al-Akbar for leadership was definitely established among them, and their discussion was only about priority among the suitable. No doubt that whoever is more entitled to lead prayer is because he is more excellent, and whoever is more excellent is more entitled to the greater leadership. So the first objection is refuted. The command to advance in what is most important and necessitates perfect virtuous qualities is understood customarily as being more entitled in a matter where those qualities are relevant. As for the hesitation of Amir al-Mu'minin Ali, it was not due to doubt about his priority but for reasons mentioned, so lack of understanding is not accepted. Even if lack of understanding is accepted, the indication might be speculative. As for their saying that there is no text, it means there is no explicit text on this. The truth is that the Prophet's order to him to lead prayer was an indication of his precedence in the greater caliphate, as required by what is in Sahih Muslim: 'Call Abu Bakr, your father and brother, so that I may write a document; I fear that someone may wish and say I am more entitled, but Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' In another narration: 'I and Allah refuses...' etc. He said that in response to the Mother of the Believers saying: 'Abu Bakr cannot control himself when he stands.' The third principle of consensus: (in your position if you would order, O Umar). And this clearly indicates that his advancement for prayer was so that no one would say: I am more entitled to leadership. So preserve it and verify it, for it is the truth and will benefit you on the Day of Judgment. And indeed there occurred the analogy of the punishment for drinking upon the punishment for slander. Amir al-Mu'minin Ali, may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, said when Amir al-Mu'minin Umar consulted about the man who drinks wine: I think we should punish him eighty stripes, for when he drinks he becomes intoxicated, when intoxicated he raves, when raves he slanders, so I see upon him the punishment of slanderers. It was said: This is istidlal (deduction from principle) not qiyas. I say: The deduction is only complete if it is established that every slanderer definitely or speculatively receives eighty stripes, because the major premise must be universal, but that is not established. Yes, it is correct that the drinker is like a slanderer because the mazinnah (presumptive indication) is like the mi'innah (certain indication). Thus, something that leads to a thing is given its ruling, like the prohibition of preliminaries to zina. But then it must be established that the ruling of slander is established for what leads to it. In the well-known view, it is qiyas of drinking on slander by the commonality of slander. In it, it necessitates that the punishment is established for every slander. Its answer is that it is qiyas by the commonality of specific slander, so ponder. Then I say: The proof is more general than the establisher, because something may be a proof but not an establisher, like something whose chain is qat'i but its text is zanni, for this proof does not establish certainty. And from here, qiyas does not establish the punishment for us, because consensus removes the doubt preventing the establishment of the punishment. So the punishment here is established by consensus, and qiyas is the proof. Thus the accusation of contradiction between the two statements—'punishments are not established by qiyas' and 'qiyas is valid as a proof for consensus to establish punishments'—is repelled. As in al-Taqrir: This neither fattens nor satisfies hunger. For when giving a fatwa is prohibited without a proof, how did the people of consensus know the punishment from qiyas? It is the establisher or something else, but the latter is assumed absent. If it is said: qiyas is not an establisher but a revealer, I say: The discussion is about this revealing, for the Hanafis forbid it in punishments. Rather we say: The Companions agreed by this qiyas on the punishment for drinking, so its establishment is a matter of consensus. There is no escape except to deny that it is qiyas, saying that it is a ruling that this mazinnah stands in place of the mi'innah by hearing (sam'), for the establishment of punishment in the time of the Messenger is confirmed, so this is a transmission of its essence, so ponder. The deniers said: Firstly, if qiyas occurs as a proof, it would be impossible to oppose it, because opposition then would be opposition to consensus, and consensus is established on the permissibility of opposing it (i.e., qiyas). We say: We do not accept that consensus is established on the permissibility of opposing it absolutely, but on the permissibility of opposing it before consensus. I (the author) say: Consensus was established on the permissibility of opposing it insofar as it is qiyas, but here opposition is prohibited because it is a matter of consensus. And they said: Secondly, qiyas is disputed; there is no era devoid of those who reject it, so consensus cannot be formed upon it, because the rejecter cannot be used as evidence. We say: The disagreement is recent, so we do not accept that there is no era devoid of its rejecters. Also the argument is refuted by generality (al-umum), which is also disputed. I say: That there is no era devoid of rejecters is prevented even if pre-existing disagreement is granted, because it is possible that in an era there remains no one who adopts its rejection. Ponder. The better way to say is that the lack of an era devoid of its rejecters does not necessitate that the rejecter is among the people qualified for consensus; rather it is possible that he is an innovator or non-mujtahid, so understand.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive usul dispute on whether qiyas (analogy) can serve as a sanad (proof basis) for ijma' (consensus), against the Zahiris and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. The author first states the Hanafi position that qiyas is permissible as a sanad, just like ahad reports, because its speculative nature (zanniyya) does not prevent it—similar to the zahir (apparent meaning) of the Qur'an which is also speculative yet used as sanad. Two historical examples are given: (1) The appointment of Abu Bakr as caliph (imamah kubra) based on his leading prayer (imamah sughra)—some claim this is qiyas, others claim it is dalalah al-nass (textual implication). The author engages in detailed analysis, ultimately arguing that the Prophet's action was an indication of Abu Bakr's precedence. (2) The punishment for drinking wine being set at eighty lashes by analogy with qadhf (slander), based on the statement attributed to Ali. Some argue this is not qiyas but istidlal. The author then discusses the relationship between the sanad and the 'muthbit' (establishing proof), asserting that qiyas can be a sanad even if it does not directly establish the ruling; consensus removes doubt. Finally, the objections of the deniers are rebutted: (a) that consensus would make opposition impossible but consensus allows opposing qiyas—answer: consensus is only on opposing before consensus; (b) that qiyas is always disputed so consensus cannot be formed—answer: possible that no rejecters remain, or rejecters may be non-mujtahids. The passage ends with the conclusion that qiyas can indeed be a sanad for ijma'.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause (illa).
مستند (sanad): The evidentiary basis that supports a ruling; can be qiyas, ahad report, etc.
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of mujtahids on a ruling; when formed on a qiyas-based opinion, the qiyas becomes part of the ijma'.
ظنية (zanniyya): Speculative or probable, as opposed to qat'i (definitive).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the objection that if qiyas were a sanad for ijma', opposition would be prohibited?
A) They agree and say qiyas cannot be used.
B) They say opposition is only prohibited after ijma'.
C) They say opposition is always allowed.
D) They say the objection is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Objections to qiyas as sanad are refuted by distinguishing temporal contexts and by noting that rejecters may be unqualified.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Linguistic and Technical Definition of Qiyas
Presents the primary definition of qiyas with its linguistic roots and technical conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of qiyas and explain why the illah must not be linguistically understood.

Core Idea
Qiyas is equality in the effective cause, not in magnitude; the cause must not be linguistically self-evident.

This lesson opens the fourth principle of usul al-fiqh: Qiyas. We begin with its linguistic meaning of 'estimation' and then move to the precise technical definition, focusing on equality in the illah and the crucial restriction that the illah must not be linguistically understood. Mastering this definition is the gateway to applying analogical reasoning correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
Qiyas linguistically means estimation (taqdir), as in measuring cloth with a cubit. It implies comparing two things to determine equality.
The verb qāsa is used for physical measurement.
2
State the technical definition
The author defines qiyas as 'the equality of the unstated (far‘) to the stated (asl) in the effective cause (illah) of the ruling.' Equality is in the illah itself, not in its magnitude (the illah may be stronger or weaker in the far‘).
The Arabic: مساواة المسكوت للمنصوص في علة الحكم.
3
Understand the restriction on the illah
The illah must be non-linguistically understood (ghayr mafhūma lughatan). If the connection is purely linguistic, it falls under mafhūm al-muwāfaqah (concept of agreement), not qiyas.
This prevents qiyas from overlapping with textual inference.
4
Differentiate from other inferential methods
Qiyas requires identifying a shared illah that is not apparent from language alone, unlike direct textual analogy.
Contrast with mafhūm al-mukhālafah and istihsān.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع: القياس
(وهو لغة : التقدير) يقال : قست الثوب بالذراع، وقست النعل بالنعل (وشاع) بحيث يفهم من غير قرينة ( في التسوية بين الشيئين (ولو) كانت ( معنوياً) وفيه إشارة إلى أنه في التسوية منقول لا أنه مشترك بينهما (و) هو (اصطلاحاً مساواة المسكوت للمنصوص في علة الحكم أي في نفس علة الحكم لا في قدرها فإنها قد تكون في الفرع أقوى، وقد تكون أضعف، وقد تكون مساوياً، ولا بد في العلة من تقييد هو كونها غير مفهومة لغة لئلا يرد النقض بمفهوم الموافقة (ثم عند المصوبة الذين يرون كل مجتهد مصيباً (لا مساواة في الواقع إلا بنظر (المجتهد فإن ما يحصل بنظره فهو واقعي وليس عندهم مساواة واقعية قد يجدها المجتهد وقد يخطىء (والرجوع) منه (كالنسخ) فلا يكون ما أدى إليه النظر الأول باطلاً عندهم، بل ينتهي بهذا النظر فلا يحتاجون إلى زيادة قيد في نظر المجتهد كما في «المختصر» وغيره، لأنه وإن كان المتبادر من المساواة المساواة الواقعية لكنها ملازمة للمساواة في نظره، ثم إنه بهذا القيد تخرج المساواة الواقعية التي لم ينلها نظر المجتهد إلا أنه لا اعتداد به ولم يتعلق الغرض بالبحث عنه فافهم بخلاف المخطئة) فإن المساواة الواقعية قد ينالها المجتهد فيصيب وقد لا ينالها فيخطىء (فيخرج) القياس (الفاسد) الذي ليس مطابقاً للواقع، لأن المتبادر من المساواة المساواة الواقعية (ولو عم) الحد القياس الفاسد (زيد) قيد (في نظره) أي المجتهد وقيل : مساواة المسكوت للمنصوص في العلة في نظره لكن يخرج مساواة لا يراها المجتهد حينئذ إلا أن يقال : لا بأس به لعدم تعلق الغرض به فتدبر، وكثيراً ما يطلق) القياس (على الفعل فعل المجتهد في معرفة تلك المساواة (فقيل) القياس (تقدير) للفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة (و) قيل (تشبيه الفرع بالأصل في علة حكمه، والظاهر أن المراد تقدير المجتهد وتشبيهه ويمكن حمله على تقديره تعالى وتشبيهه (و) قيل (بذل) المجتهد في استخراج الحق، وهذا فعل المجتهد قطعاً، وهذا منقوض ببذل المجتهد في استخراج الحق من الكتاب والسنة (و) قيل (حمل ) الشيء على غيره بإجراء حكمه عليه لعلة مشتركة، وهو لأبي هاشم المعتزلي، وقيل: حمل لمعلوم على معلوم في إثبات الحكم لهما أو نفيه عنهما بأمر جامع وهو للقاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني (و) قيل (إبانة) لمثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في ، وهو للشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي قدس سره، والمراد بالعلة في الآخر حصة الوصف الموجودة فيه، وبمثله الحصة الأخرى منه الموجودة في صاحبه، وإنما حكم بالمثلية بهذا الاعتبار والإبانة تحتمل الوجهين (و) قيل (تعدية) الحكم من الأصل إلى الآخر،
The fourth principle: Qiyas.
(Linguistically: estimation.) It is said: I measured the cloth with the cubit, and I measured the sandal with the sandal. (And it became widespread) such that it is understood without a context (in equating between two things) even if (they are) (conceptual). And in it is a sign that it is transferred in equating, not that it is shared between them.
(And technically: the equality of the unstated [case] to the stated [case] in the effective cause of the ruling—i.e., in the very effective cause of the ruling, not in its magnitude, for it may be stronger in the branch, or weaker, or equal. And in the effective cause, a restriction is necessary: that it is not linguistically understood, lest the counterexample of concept of agreement arises.
(Then according to the musawwiba—those who hold every mujtahid is correct—there is no equality in reality except by the view of the mujtahid, because what is obtained by his view is real, and they do not hold a real equality that the mujtahid may find or miss. (And retraction) from it (is like abrogation); thus what the first view led to is not invalid according to them; rather it ends with this view, so they do not need to add a restriction in the view of the mujtahid, as in al-Mukhtasar and others, because even if the immediate understanding of equality is real equality, it is concomitant with equality in his view. Then by this restriction, the real equality that the mujtahid's view did not reach is excluded, but it is not considered and the purpose is not attached to seeking it. So understand, unlike the mukhatti'a.) For the real equality may be attained by the mujtahid and he is correct, or may not be attained and he errs. (Thus) invalid qiyas (which does not correspond to reality is excluded) because the immediate understanding of equality is real equality. (And if) the definition includes invalid qiyas, (the restriction “in his view” is added)—i.e., of the mujtahid. And it is said: the equality of the unstated to the stated in the effective cause in his view. But this excludes an equality that the mujtahid does not see at that time, unless it is said: no harm because the purpose is not attached to it. So reflect.
(And often qiyas is applied) to the action—the mujtahid's act of knowing that equality. (So it is said) qiyas is (estimation) of the branch to the original in the ruling and effective cause. (And) it is said (likening) the branch to the original in the effective cause of its ruling. And the apparent is that what is meant is the mujtahid's estimation and likening, and it can be carried on His estimation and likening. (And) it is said (exertion) of the mujtahid in extracting the truth. This is definitely the mujtahid's action, but it is refuted by the mujtahid's exertion in extracting the truth from the Book and Sunnah. (And) it is said (carrying) one thing to another by applying its ruling to it for a shared effective cause, and it is by Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili. And it is said: carrying a known to a known in establishing a ruling for both or negating it from both by a comprehensive matter, and it is by Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. (And) it is said (clarification) of the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned by the like of its effective cause in it, and it is by al-Shaykh al-Imam 'Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may his secret be sanctified). And what is meant by the effective cause in the other is the portion of the description existing in it, and by its like is the other portion of it existing in its companion. And he only ruled by similarity in this regard, and 'clarification' may carry both aspects. (And) it is said (transference) of the ruling from the original to the other.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage opens the fourth chapter on Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in usul al-fiqh. It begins by giving the linguistic meaning of qiyas as 'estimation' (taqdir), derived from measuring cloth or sandals. Then it gives the technical definition favored by the author: equality of the unstated case (the branch, far') with the stated case (the original, asl) in the effective cause (illah) of the ruling. The illah must be a non-linguistically understood attribute to avoid confusion with mafhum al-muwafaqah (concept of agreement, which is a different type of inference). 

The passage then discusses the debate between the musawwiba (those who hold that every mujtahid is correct) and the mukhatti'a (those who hold that there is a single correct ruling and others err). For the musawwiba, the equality in qiyas is not an objective reality independent of the mujtahid; rather, whatever the mujtahid's ijtihad yields is the valid equality for him, and retraction from a previous ijtihad is like abrogation. For the mukhatti'a, there is a real equality that the mujtahid may or may not attain. The author notes that if the definition is to exclude invalid qiyas, a restriction 'in his view' (fi nazarihi) is added.

The passage then lists several alternative definitions of qiyas from different scholars: 
- Estimation (taqdir) of the branch to the original in ruling and illah.
- Likening (tashbih) the branch to the original in the illah.
- Exertion (badhl) of effort by the mujtahid—refuted as it could apply to extracting rulings from primary texts.
- Carrying (haml) one thing to another for a shared illah (Abu Hashim).
- Carrying a known to a known for establishing or negating a ruling by a comprehensive factor (Baqillani).
- Clarification (ibana) of the like of the ruling by the like of the illah (Maturidi).
- Transference (ta'diya) of the ruling from the original to the other.

This shows the richness of the Hanafi usul tradition in defining qiyas precisely.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause or attribute common to asl and far' upon which the ruling is based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi technical definition, qiyas is the equality of the unstated (far') to the stated (asl) in what?
A) The ruling itself
B) The effective cause of the ruling
C) The magnitude of the ruling
D) The textual wording

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is defined as equality in the effective cause of the ruling, provided the cause is not linguistically understood.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Qiyas and the Musawwibah/Mukhatti'ah Debate
Defining qiyas with its linguistic and terminological meaning, including the condition of the cause and the epistemological debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas terminologically, identify the condition that the 'illa must not be linguistically understood, and distinguish between the musawwibah and mukhatti'ah positions on the nature of equality.

Core Idea
Qiyas is equating an unstated case to a stated case in the cause of the ruling.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut establishes the fourth principle of usul al-fiqh: qiyas. It begins with the linguistic meaning 'estimation' and then gives the precise terminological definition. The author also addresses a foundational epistemological debate: is the equality between the cases real and objective, or does it depend on the mujtahid's ijtihad? Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating whether a particular analogy is valid or flawed.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the linguistic meaning
Note that qiyas linguistically means 'taqdir' (estimation/measurement), as in measuring cloth or sandals. This shows the root idea of comparison.
2
2. State the terminological definition
The author defines qiyas as ' equating the unstated case (maskut) to the stated case (mansus) in the cause ('illa) of the ruling.' Emphasize that the equality is in the cause itself, not in the magnitude of the ruling.
The 'illa must be qualified as 'ghayr mafhuma lughatan' (not understood by mere language) to avoid confusion with mafhum al-muwafaqa (a fortiori reasoning).
3
3. Distinguish the musawwibah and mukhatti'ah views
The musawwibah hold that there is no objective real equality; the mujtahid's ijtihad creates the equality for him. The mukhatti'ah hold that there is an objective real equality that the mujtahid may hit or miss.
This affects how invalid qiyas is excluded: musawwibah add 'in his view' to the definition; mukhatti'ah rely on the immediate understanding of real equality.
4
4. Understand the implication for invalid qiyas
If the definition is taken as real equality, invalid qiyas (that does not correspond to reality) is excluded automatically. If not, a qualification 'in the mujtahid's view' must be added.
The author leans toward the mukhatti'ah view, as shown by the phrase 'bikhilaf al-mukhatti'a'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الحكم لهما أو نفيه عنهما بأمر جامع وهو للقاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني (و) قيل (إبانة) لمثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في ، وهو للشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي قدس سره، والمراد بالعلة في الآخر ۲۹۷

الفرع لعلة متحدة لا تدرك بمجرد اللغة وهو لصدر الشريعة (و) قيل (إثبات) لحكم الأصل للفرع مع تشريك إلى غير ذلك كما قد يقال : تسوية الفرع بالأصل في العلة والحكم (وهو) أي اطلاق القياس على الفعل (مسامحة) لأن القياس حجة الهية موضوعة من قبل الشارع لمعرفة أحكامه، وليس هو فعلا لأحد، لكن لما كانت معرفته بفعل المجتهد ربما يطلق عليه مجازاً ثم في بعض التعريفات أبحاث وجوابات تطلب من المطولات (وأورد) على عكس التعريف قياس (الدلالة وهو ما يذكر فيه ملزوم العلة دونها لأنه ليس مساواة في العلة (وقياس العكس) وهو ما ثبت فيه نقيض الحكم بنقيض العلة كقولنا لما وجب الصوم في الاعتكاف : بالنذر وجب ،بدونه كالصلاة لما لم تجب معه بالنذر لم تجب بدونه (والجواب أولاً) عنهما (منع كونهما من المحدود ولا نسميهما قياساً (إلا) (مجازاً، وثانياً) عن الأول (المساواة) المذكورة في التعريف (أعم) مما كان صريحاً أو (ضمناً والمساواة الضمنية حاصلة (مثلاً: إذا قيل في المسروق يجب الرد قائماً، فيجب الضمان ،هالكاً كالمغصوب فوجود الرد) المشترك (فيهما) وإن لم يكن علة لكنه يتضمن قصد حفظ المال وإن شئت قلت : التعدي وهو حقيقة (وما في التحرير القياس حينئذ غير المذكور) بل هو ما يذكر فيه العلة المتضمنة، لأنه المساواة في العلة حقيقة فأقول فيه : إن التجوز في الحد لا يستلزم التجوز في المحدود) وإذ قد أريد بالمساواة ما يعم الضمنية، ولو تجوز فالقياس يكون هو حقيقة، وهو ظاهر، إلا أن صاحب «التحرير» لم ينقل الجواب بالتجوز، بل نقل الجواب بأنه مردود إلى قياس العلة لتضمنه علة الحكم، فتعقب عليه بأن القياس حينئذ غير المذكور، وأما الجواب بتحمل التجوز فهو وإن كان لا يرد عليه هذا إلا أنه حينئذ يصير قياس الدلالة قياسين، ولم يقل به أحد فتأمل (و) عن الثاني بأنه كما أريد المساواة الأعم من الضمنية (كذا) يراد مساواة أعم من أن يكون (تحقيقاً أو تقريراً) وقياس العكس راجع إلى الاستدلال بالملازمة والقياس لإثباتها، ففي المثال المذكور لو لم يجب الصوم شرطاً في الاعتكاف لم يجب بالنذر كالصلاة، فإنها لما لم تجب شرطاً فيه لم تجب بالنذر، مع أنه يجب بالنذر فيجب شرطاً فيه، فالمساواة ههنا تقديرية على تقدير عدم وجوبه شرطاً فيه ومثل المصنف بمثال آخر وقال (مثلاً: إذا قيل) كما يقول الشافعية ( يثبت الاعتراض عليها إذا زوجت نفسها من غير إذن الولي (فلا يصح النكاح منها، كالرجل لما لم يثبت الاعتراض عليه إذا تزوج بنفسه (صح) نكاحه (فحاصله لو صح النكاح (منها صارت كالرجل فلا يثبت) الاعتراض عليها (وقد ثبت وإنما اختار هذا المثال إشارة إلى أن الجواب بأن المقصود قياس صوم الاعتكاف الغير المنذور عليه منذوراً بتنقيح المناط والغاء خصوص النذر، لأنه لو كان له دخل لوجب الصلاة بالنذر أيضاً، فذكر الصلاة لإلغاء الخصوصية غير واف لعدم جريانه في هذا المثال، وكذا الجواب بأن الحكم المقصود هناك تسوية حال النذر وعدمه في صوم الاعتكاف كالصلاة فافهم ( ثم أركانه أربعة أحدها الأصل المحل المشبه به وهو المتعارف) بين الفقهاء (كالخمر، بل شربه في قياس النبيذ عليه بجامع الشدة المطربة (وقيل) الأصل (دليله) دليل المشبه به فهو في المثال المذكور قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا
The Fourth Principle: Qiyas (Analogy). (Linguistically it is: estimation) one says: I measured the cloth by the cubit, and I measured the sandal by the sandal. (And it became common) so that it is understood without context (for equality between two things) even if they are (conceptual). And there is an indication that it is transferred from its original meaning in the sense of equality, not that it is shared between them. (And) it is (terminologically: equating the unstated [case] to the stated [case] in the cause ('illa) of the ruling, i.e., in the very cause of the ruling, not in its magnitude, for it may be stronger in the branch, weaker, or equal. The cause must be qualified by being not linguistically understood, to avoid rebuttal by the concept of concurrence (mafhum al-muwafaqa). Then, according to the musawwibah (those who hold that every mujtahid is correct), (there is no real equality except through the ijtihad of the mujtahid, for what is reached by his ijtihad is real for him, and they do not hold an objective real equality that the mujtahid may find or miss. And retraction from it is like abrogation, so the first ijtihad is not invalidated in their view, but rather it is abrogated by this ijtihad, so they do not need to add a qualification to the ijtihad of the mujtahid as in al-Mukhtasar and others, because even though the immediate understanding from equality is real equality, it is concomitant to equality in his view. Then by this qualification, real equality that the mujtahid did not reach is excluded, but it is not considered and the purpose is not to investigate it, so understand. Contrary to the mukhatti'ah (those who hold that only one view is correct), for real equality may be reached by the mujtahid and he is correct, or he may not reach it and err. (Thus) invalid (qiyas) that does not correspond to reality is excluded because the immediate understanding from equality is real equality. (And even if the definition included invalid qiyas), then (the qualification 'in his view' i.e., the mujtahid's view is added). And it is said: equating the unstated to the stated in the cause in his view, but then equality not seen by the mujtahid is excluded, unless it is said: no harm because the purpose is not attached to it, so ponder. And often qiyas is applied to the act of the mujtahid in knowing that equality. (So it is said) qiyas is (estimation) of the branch to the original in the ruling and the cause. (And) it is said (likening) the branch to the original in the cause of its ruling, and the apparent meaning is the estimation and likening by the mujtahid, and it can be carried to the estimation and likening by Allah Almighty. (And) it is said (exertion) of the mujtahid in extracting the truth, and this is clearly the act of the mujtahid. This is refuted by the exertion of the mujtahid in extracting the truth from the Book and Sunnah. (And) it is said (carrying) a thing to another by applying its ruling to it due to a common cause, and this is by Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili. And it is said: carrying a known to a known in establishing a ruling for both or negating it from both by a common link, and this is by al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. (And) it is said (clarifying) the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned by the like of its cause, and this is by the Imam 'Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may his secret be sanctified). The meaning of 'cause' in the latter is the share of the description present in it, and by its like is the other share of it present in its counterpart, and ruling by similarity is by this consideration, and 'clarifying' can carry both aspects. (And) it is said (transferring) the ruling from the original to the branch due to a unified cause not known merely by language, and this is by Sadr al-Shari'a. (And) it is said (establishing) the ruling of the original for the branch with partnership, and so on, as it may be said: equating the branch to the original in the cause and the ruling. (And this) i.e., applying qiyas to the act (is a leniency) because qiyas is a divine proof established by the Lawgiver for knowing His rulings, and it is not an act of anyone. But since knowing it is by the act of the mujtahid, it may be applied to it metaphorically. Then in some definitions there are investigations and responses to be sought from lengthy works. (And it is objected) to the opposite of the definition (qiyas al-dilala (indicative analogy)) which is where the concomitant of the cause is mentioned without the cause itself, because it is not equality in the cause. (And qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy)) which is where the opposite of the ruling is established by the opposite of the cause, as we say: since fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf (retreat) with a vow, it is obligatory without it? Actually, like prayer, since it is not obligatory with a vow, it is not obligatory without it. (The response is, first) regarding both (denial that they are part of the defined term, and we do not call them qiyas except metaphorically. Second, regarding the first: (the equality) mentioned in the definition (is more general) than what is explicit or (implicit, and implicit equality exists. (For example: if it is said regarding the stolen item, it is obligatory to return it while it exists, so compensation is obligatory if it perishes, like the usurped item. So the existence of return) common (in both) though not the cause, implies the intent to preserve wealth, or if you wish you may say: transgression (ta'addi) which is the real cause. (And what is in al-Tahrir: the qiyas then is other than the mentioned one), rather it is where the implied cause is mentioned, because it is equality in the cause in reality. So I say in it: metaphorical usage in the definition does not necessitate metaphorical usage in the defined term. And since equality is intended to include implicit equality, even if metaphorically, the qiyas is real, and it is apparent. However, the author of al-Tahrir did not transmit the answer by metaphor, but transmitted the answer that it is reducible to qiyas al-'illa because it includes the cause of the ruling, so it was objected that the qiyas then is other than the mentioned one. As for the answer of tolerating metaphor, although this objection does not apply, it would then make qiyas al-dilala two types of qiyas, and no one has said so, so contemplate. (And) regarding the second: just as equality is intended to be more general than implicit, (likewise) equality is intended to be more general than (realized or established). And qiyas al-'aks is reducible to inference by concomitance and qiyas to establish it. In the mentioned example: if fasting were not a condition in i'tikaf, it would not be obligatory with a vow, like prayer; since prayer was not a condition in it, it is not obligatory with a vow, while it is obligatory with a vow, so it must be a condition in it. So the equality here is hypothetical upon the hypothesis of its not being a condition. And the author gave another example, saying (for example: if it is said) as the Shafi'is say (objection [to the woman's marriage] is established if she marries herself without the guardian's permission, so the marriage from her is invalid, just as the man, since no objection is established against him if he marries himself, his marriage is valid. So the summary: if the marriage from her were valid, she would become like the man, so no objection would be established against her, but it is established. And he chose this example to indicate that the answer that the intended is qiyas of the non-vowed fast of i'tikaf upon the vowed one by refining the ratio legis (tanqih al-manat) and negating the specificity of the vow, because if it had an effect, prayer would also be obligatory with a vow, so mentioning prayer to negate specificity is insufficient for not applying in this example. Similarly, the answer that the intended ruling there is equalizing the case of vow and non-vow in the fast of i'tikaf like prayer, so understand. (Then its pillars are four: one of them: the original, the thing likened to, which is conventional) among jurists (like wine, rather drinking it in qiyas of date wine upon it due to the common intoxicating quality. (And it is said) the original (is its evidence), the evidence of the thing likened to, so in the mentioned example it is the saying of Allah Most High: "Indeed,"
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut defines qiyas (analogy), the fourth principle of usul al-fiqh. It begins with the linguistic meaning: 'taqdir' (estimation or measurement), then explains the terminological definition: equating an unstated case (maskut) to a stated case (mansus) in the cause ('illa) of the ruling. The author notes that the cause must be 'ghayr mafhuma lughatan' (not understood purely by language) to avoid confusion with mafhum al-muwafaqah (a fortiori reasoning). Then the text discusses the epistemological debate between the musawwibah (who hold that every mujtahid is correct in his own view) and the mukhatti'ah (who hold that only one ijtihad is objectively correct). According to the musawwibah, the equality referred to in the definition is not objective real equality but rather equality as determined by the mujtahid's ijtihad; thus invalid qiyas is excluded by adding 'in the view of the mujtahid.' The mukhatti'ah, however, maintain that real equality is what is intended, and the mujtahid may hit or miss it. Next, the passage presents multiple definitions of qiyas by major scholars: 'taqdir' (estimation) and 'tashbih' (likening) by the mujtahid; 'badhl' (exertion) – criticized because similar exertion is used for extracting rulings from primary sources; 'haml' (carrying) by Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili; 'haml ma'lum 'ala ma'lum' by al-Baqillani; 'ibana' (clarifying) by al-Maturidi; 'ta'diya' (transferring) by Sadr al-Shari'a; and 'ithbat' (establishing) with partnership. The author notes that applying qiyas to the act of the mujtahid is metaphorical (musamaha) because qiyas is a divine proof, not a human action. The text then deals with objections to the definition regarding qiyas al-dilala (where only the concomitant of the cause is mentioned) and qiyas al-aks (inverse analogy). The response is either to deny that these are valid types of qiyas or to broaden the definition to include implicit equality (diman) and hypothetical equality (taqdir). Examples are given: the stolen item case for qiyas al-dilala, and a Shafi'i example of a woman marrying without a guardian for qiyas al-aks. Finally, the passage begins listing the four pillars of qiyas: 1) the original (asl) – the case likened to, which is conventional among jurists (e.g., wine for qiyas on nabidh due to intoxication). There is also a view that the original is the evidence (dalil) of the case, so for wine it is the Quranic verse on prohibition.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Linguistically: estimation. Terminologically: equating an unstated case to a stated case in the cause of the ruling.
العلة (al-'illa): The attribute (wasf) that is the cause of the ruling, and it must be munasib (suitable) and not linguistically understood.
المساواة (al-musawa): Equality between the branch and the original in the cause, which according to the author is real equality according to mukhatti'ah, or equality in the mujtahid's estimation according to musawwibah.
المصوبة (al-musawwibah): Those who hold that every mujtahid is correct in his ijtihad (i.e., there is no single objectively correct ruling).
المخطئة (al-mukhatti'ah): Those who hold that there is a single objectively correct ruling, and other mujtahids may err.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must the 'illa (cause) satisfy in the terminological definition of qiyas?
A) It must be explicitly stated in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) It must be linguistically understood (mafhuma lughatan).
C) It must be not linguistically understood (ghayr mafhuma lughatan).
D) It must be stronger in the branch than in the original.

Key Takeaway
The terminological definition of qiyas requires equating the branch to the original in a cause that is not linguistically understood, and the mukhatti'ah view that equality is objective is the preferred Hanafi position.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Variants of Qiyas: Scholarly Definitions and Objections
Expanding the definition of qiyas with scholarly variants and answering objections regarding qiyas al-dilala and qiyas al-aks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify multiple definitions of qiyas given by major scholars, explain why the application of qiyas to the mujtahid's act is metaphorical, and analyze the objections regarding qiyas al-dilala and qiyas al-aks.

Core Idea
Qiyas al-dilala and qiyas al-aks are not true qiyas but metaphorical or implied forms of reasoning.

After establishing the core definition, the passage expands to show how various scholars have defined qiyas in terms of the mujtahid's action (taqdir, tashbih, etc.) and then addresses two important objections: that certain arguments called 'qiyas al-dilala' and 'qiyas al-aks' do not fit the definition. The Hanafi response clarifies that these are either reducible to real qiyas or are metaphorical extensions.

Guided Path
1
1. Review the multiple definitions of qiyas
The passage lists definitions by different scholars: taqdir (estimation), tashbih (likening), badhl (exertion), haml (carrying), ibana (clarifying), ta'diya (transferring), ithbat (establishing). Note that these all describe the act of the mujtahid.
These definitions are metaphorical (musamaha) because qiyas itself is a divine proof, not a human action.
2
2. Understand the objection to qiyas al-dilala
Qiyas al-dilala mentions the concomitant (lazim) of the cause rather than the cause itself. For example, in the stolen item case, 'return' is mentioned but the underlying cause is preservation of wealth.
The objector says this is not equality in the cause, so it shouldn't be called qiyas.
3
3. Analyze the Hanafi response to qiyas al-dilala
Two responses: (1) Deny it is real qiyas, accept it only as metaphorical; (2) Broaden the definition of equality to include implicit equality (diman). The implicit cause can be extracted.
The author notes the debate in al-Tahrir about whether this makes the qiyas 'other than the mentioned one'.
4
4. Understand qiyas al-aks (inverse analogy)
This establishes the opposite ruling from the opposite cause. Example: If fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf with a vow, then without a vow it is not obligatory (by analogy to prayer, which is not obligatory with a vow).
The Hanafi response is to consider equality here as 'established' (taqrir) or hypothetical, not real equality.
5
5. Recognize the practical implication
The Shafi'i example of a woman marrying without guardian illustrates that the Hanafi treat qiyas al-aks as inference by concomitance, not true qiyas.
The author chose this example to show that the 'vow' example's answer (tanqih al-manat) does not apply here.

الفرع لعلة متحدة لا تدرك بمجرد اللغة وهو لصدر الشريعة (و) قيل (إثبات) لحكم الأصل للفرع مع تشريك إلى غير ذلك كما قد يقال : تسوية الفرع بالأصل في العلة والحكم (وهو) أي اطلاق القياس على الفعل (مسامحة) تجوز فالقياس يكون هو حقيقة، وهو ظاهر، إلا أن صاحب «التحرير» لم ينقل الجواب بالتجوز، بل نقل الجواب بأنه مردود إلى قياس العلة لتضمنه علة الحكم، فتعقب عليه بأن القياس حينئذ غير المذكور، وأما الجواب بتحمل التجوز فهو وإن كان لا يرد عليه هذا إلا أنه حينئذ يصير قياس الدلالة قياسين، ولم يقل به أحد فتأمل (و) عن الثاني بأنه كما أريد المساواة الأعم من الضمنية (كذا) يراد مساواة أعم من أن يكون (تحقيقاً أو تقريراً) وقياس العكس راجع إلى الاستدلال بالملازمة والقياس لإثباتها، ففي المثال المذكور لو لم يجب الصوم شرطاً في الاعتكاف لم يجب بالنذر كالصلاة، فإنها لما لم تجب شرطاً فيه لم تجب بالنذر، مع أنه يجب بالنذر فيجب شرطاً فيه، فالمساواة ههنا تقديرية على تقدير عدم وجوبه شرطاً فيه ومثل المصنف بمثال آخر وقال (مثلاً: إذا قيل) كما يقول الشافعية ( يثبت الاعتراض عليها إذا زوجت نفسها من غير إذن الولي (فلا يصح النكاح منها، كالرجل لما لم يثبت الاعتراض عليه إذا تزوج بنفسه (صح) نكاحه (فحاصله لو صح النكاح (منها صارت كالرجل فلا يثبت) الاعتراض عليها (وقد ثبت وإنما اختار هذا المثال إشارة إلى أن الجواب بأن المقصود قياس صوم الاعتكاف الغير المنذور عليه منذوراً بتنقيح المناط والغاء خصوص النذر، لأنه لو كان له دخل لوجب الصلاة بالنذر أيضاً، فذكر الصلاة لإلغاء الخصوصية غير واف لعدم جريانه في هذا المثال، وكذا الجواب المطربة (وقيل) الأصل (دليله) دليل المشبه به فهو في المثال المذكور قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا
The Fourth Principle: Qiyas (Analogy). (Linguistically it is: estimation) one says: I measured the cloth by the cubit, and I measured the sandal by the sandal. (And it became common) so that it is understood without context (for equality between two things) even if they are (conceptual). And there is an indication that it is transferred from its original meaning in the sense of equality, not that it is shared between them. (And) it is (terminologically: equating the unstated [case] to the stated [case] in the cause ('illa) of the ruling, i.e., in the very cause of the ruling, not in its magnitude, for it may be stronger in the branch, weaker, or equal. The cause must be qualified by being not linguistically understood, to avoid rebuttal by the concept of concurrence (mafhum al-muwafaqa). Then, according to the musawwibah (those who hold that every mujtahid is correct), (there is no real equality except through the ijtihad of the mujtahid, for what is reached by his ijtihad is real for him, and they do not hold an objective real equality that the mujtahid may find or miss. And retraction from it is like abrogation, so the first ijtihad is not invalidated in their view, but rather it is abrogated by this ijtihad, so they do not need to add a qualification to the ijtihad of the mujtahid as in al-Mukhtasar and others, because even though the immediate understanding from equality is real equality, it is concomitant to equality in his view. Then by this qualification, real equality that the mujtahid did not reach is excluded, but it is not considered and the purpose is not to investigate it, so understand. Contrary to the mukhatti'ah (those who hold that only one view is correct), for real equality may be reached by the mujtahid and he is correct, or he may not reach it and err. (Thus) invalid (qiyas) that does not correspond to reality is excluded because the immediate understanding from equality is real equality. (And even if the definition included invalid qiyas), then (the qualification 'in his view' i.e., the mujtahid's view is added). And it is said: equating the unstated to the stated in the cause in his view, but then equality not seen by the mujtahid is excluded, unless it is said: no harm because the purpose is not attached to it, so ponder. And often qiyas is applied to the act of the mujtahid in knowing that equality. (So it is said) qiyas is (estimation) of the branch to the original in the ruling and the cause. (And) it is said (likening) the branch to the original in the cause of its ruling, and the apparent meaning is the estimation and likening by the mujtahid, and it can be carried to the estimation and likening by Allah Almighty. (And) it is said (exertion) of the mujtahid in extracting the truth, and this is clearly the act of the mujtahid. This is refuted by the exertion of the mujtahid in extracting the truth from the Book and Sunnah. (And) it is said (carrying) a thing to another by applying its ruling to it due to a common cause, and this is by Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili. And it is said: carrying a known to a known in establishing a ruling for both or negating it from both by a common link, and this is by al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. (And) it is said (clarifying) the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned by the like of its cause, and this is by the Imam 'Alam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may his secret be sanctified). The meaning of 'cause' in the latter is the share of the description present in it, and by its like is the other share of it present in its counterpart, and ruling by similarity is by this consideration, and 'clarifying' can carry both aspects. (And) it is said (transferring) the ruling from the original to the branch due to a unified cause not known merely by language, and this is by Sadr al-Shari'a. (And) it is said (establishing) the ruling of the original for the branch with partnership, and so on, as it may be said: equating the branch to the original in the cause and the ruling. (And this) i.e., applying qiyas to the act (is a leniency) because qiyas is a divine proof established by the Lawgiver for knowing His rulings, and it is not an act of anyone. But since knowing it is by the act of the mujtahid, it may be applied to it metaphorically. Then in some definitions there are investigations and responses to be sought from lengthy works. (And it is objected) to the opposite of the definition (qiyas al-dilala (indicative analogy)) which is where the concomitant of the cause is mentioned without the cause itself, because it is not equality in the cause. (And qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy)) which is where the opposite of the ruling is established by the opposite of the cause, as we say: since fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf (retreat) with a vow, it is obligatory without it? Actually, like prayer, since it is not obligatory with a vow, it is not obligatory without it. (The response is, first) regarding both (denial that they are part of the defined term, and we do not call them qiyas except metaphorically. Second, regarding the first: (the equality) mentioned in the definition (is more general) than what is explicit or (implicit, and implicit equality exists. (For example: if it is said regarding the stolen item, it is obligatory to return it while it exists, so compensation is obligatory if it perishes, like the usurped item. So the existence of return) common (in both) though not the cause, implies the intent to preserve wealth, or if you wish you may say: transgression (ta'addi) which is the real cause. (And what is in al-Tahrir: the qiyas then is other than the mentioned one), rather it is where the implied cause is mentioned, because it is equality in the cause in reality. So I say in it: metaphorical usage in the definition does not necessitate metaphorical usage in the defined term. And since equality is intended to include implicit equality, even if metaphorically, the qiyas is real, and it is apparent. However, the author of al-Tahrir did not transmit the answer by metaphor, but transmitted the answer that it is reducible to qiyas al-'illa because it includes the cause of the ruling, so it was objected that the qiyas then is other than the mentioned one. As for the answer of tolerating metaphor, although this objection does not apply, it would then make qiyas al-dilala two types of qiyas, and no one has said so, so contemplate. (And) regarding the second: just as equality is intended to be more general than implicit, (likewise) equality is intended to be more general than (realized or established). And qiyas al-'aks is reducible to inference by concomitance and qiyas to establish it. In the mentioned example: if fasting were not a condition in i'tikaf, it would not be obligatory with a vow, like prayer; since prayer was not a condition in it, it is not obligatory with a vow, while it is obligatory with a vow, so it must be a condition in it. So the equality here is hypothetical upon the hypothesis of its not being a condition. And the author gave another example, saying (for example: if it is said) as the Shafi'is say (objection [to the woman's marriage] is established if she marries herself without the guardian's permission, so the marriage from her is invalid, just as the man, since no objection is established against him if he marries himself, his marriage is valid. So the summary: if the marriage from her were valid, she would become like the man, so no objection would be established against her, but it is established. And he chose this example to indicate that the answer that the intended is qiyas of the non-vowed fast of i'tikaf upon the vowed one by refining the ratio legis (tanqih al-manat) and negating the specificity of the vow, because if it had an effect, prayer would also be obligatory with a vow, so mentioning prayer to negate specificity is insufficient for not applying in this example. Similarly, the answer that the intended ruling there is equalizing the case of vow and non-vow in the fast of i'tikaf like prayer, so understand. (Then its pillars are four: one of them: the original, the thing likened to, which is conventional) among jurists (like wine, rather drinking it in qiyas of date wine upon it due to the common intoxicating quality. (And it is said) the original (is its evidence), the evidence of the thing likened to, so in the mentioned example it is the saying of Allah Most High: "Indeed,"
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut defines qiyas (analogy), the fourth principle of usul al-fiqh. It begins with the linguistic meaning: 'taqdir' (estimation or measurement), then explains the terminological definition: equating an unstated case (maskut) to a stated case (mansus) in the cause ('illa) of the ruling. The author notes that the cause must be 'ghayr mafhuma lughatan' (not understood purely by language) to avoid confusion with mafhum al-muwafaqah (a fortiori reasoning). Then the text discusses the epistemological debate between the musawwibah (who hold that every mujtahid is correct in his own view) and the mukhatti'ah (who hold that only one ijtihad is objectively correct). According to the musawwibah, the equality referred to in the definition is not objective real equality but rather equality as determined by the mujtahid's ijtihad; thus invalid qiyas is excluded by adding 'in the view of the mujtahid.' The mukhatti'ah, however, maintain that real equality is what is intended, and the mujtahid may hit or miss it. Next, the passage presents multiple definitions of qiyas by major scholars: 'taqdir' (estimation) and 'tashbih' (likening) by the mujtahid; 'badhl' (exertion) – criticized because similar exertion is used for extracting rulings from primary sources; 'haml' (carrying) by Abu Hashim al-Mu'tazili; 'haml ma'lum 'ala ma'lum' by al-Baqillani; 'ibana' (clarifying) by al-Maturidi; 'ta'diya' (transferring) by Sadr al-Shari'a; and 'ithbat' (establishing) with partnership. The author notes that applying qiyas to the act of the mujtahid is metaphorical (musamaha) because qiyas is a divine proof, not a human action. The text then deals with objections to the definition regarding qiyas al-dilala (where only the concomitant of the cause is mentioned) and qiyas al-aks (inverse analogy). The response is either to deny that these are valid types of qiyas or to broaden the definition to include implicit equality (diman) and hypothetical equality (taqdir). Examples are given: the stolen item case for qiyas al-dilala, and a Shafi'i example of a woman marrying without a guardian for qiyas al-aks. Finally, the passage begins listing the four pillars of qiyas: 1) the original (asl) – the case likened to, which is conventional among jurists (e.g., wine for qiyas on nabidh due to intoxication). There is also a view that the original is the evidence (dalil) of the case, so for wine it is the Quranic verse on prohibition.

Key Terms
قياس الدلالة (qiyas al-dilala): A type of qiyas where the concomitant (lazim) of the cause is mentioned instead of the cause itself.
قياس العكس (qiyas al-'aks): A type of qiyas where the opposite ruling is derived from the opposite cause (inverse analogy).
المسامحة (al-musamaha): Leniency or metaphorical usage; applying the term 'qiyas' to the act of the mujtahid is considered musamaha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary objection to considering qiyas al-dilala as real qiyas?
A) It is not based on any shared attribute.
B) It mentions the concomitant of the cause, not the cause itself.
C) It is only used by later scholars, not the salaf.
D) It leads to logical contradictions.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas al-dilala and qiyas al-aks are not considered true qiyas in Hanafi usul; they are either metaphorical or reducible to real qiyas through implicit or hypothetical equality.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Qiyas: The Hanafi Usul Framework
Defining qiyas and noting the metaphorical usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas and explain why applying the term 'qiyas' to the mujtahid's act is a metaphorical concession.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a divine proof; calling the mujtahid's effort 'qiyas' is metaphorical.

This lesson unpacks the core definition of qiyas as established in Hanafi usul. We begin with the precise formulation: equating the branch with the original in cause and ruling. The passage also clarifies that qiyas is fundamentally a divine proof, not a human action, though the term may be applied metaphorically to the mujtahid's reasoning process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the formal definition
Find the exact wording: 'establishing the ruling of the original for the branch by associating them in cause and ruling.' Note that this sets the criteria for valid qiyas.
The definition includes both cause ('illa) and ruling (hukm).
2
Understand the 'musamaha' (concession)
The text says calling the mujtahid's act 'qiyas' is a concession. Recognize why: qiyas is a divine proof, but since the mujtahid engages in discovering it, the term is used metaphorically.
This distinction guards against anthropomorphizing the source of law.
3
Locate the key components of the definition
Break down the definition into: asl (original), far' (branch), 'illa (cause), hukm (ruling). Each is essential for a valid qiyas.
The 'illa must be shared and suitable (munasib).

The 'illa (cause) of the branch is for a single cause not grasped by mere language, and it is for Sadr al-Shari'ah. (And) it was said: (establishing) the ruling of the original for the branch with associating to other than that, as may be said: equalizing the branch with the original in the cause and ruling. (And it) i.e., applying qiyas to the act, is a concession, because qiyas is a divine proof placed by the Lawgiver to know His rulings, and it is not an act of anyone, but since its knowledge is by the act of the mujtahid, it may be applied metaphorically. Then in some definitions there are investigations and answers to be sought from the lengthy works. (And it was objected) to the reverse definition of qiyas al-dalala, which is what mentions the necessary of the cause without it because it is not equality in the cause, and qiyas al-'aks, which is what establishes the opposite of the ruling by the opposite of the cause, such as our saying: when fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf by vow, it is obligatory without it, like prayer, which when not obligatory with it by vow is not obligatory without it. (And the answer first) to both is preventing them from being within the defined, and we do not call them qiyas except metaphorically. And secondly regarding the first: the equality mentioned in the definition is more general than being explicit or implicit, and implicit equality is attained. For example: when it is said regarding the stolen item: it must be returned intact, so compensation is due if it is destroyed, like the usurped item; the existence of the shared term 'return' in them even if it is not the cause, but it includes the intention of preserving wealth, or if you wish you may say: transgression which is the reality. (And what is in al-Tahrir: qiyas then is not the mentioned one) rather it is what mentions the implied cause, because it is equality in the cause truly. So I say in it: metaphorical use in the limit does not necessitate metaphorical use in the limited. And since equality is intended to include implicit, even if metaphorical, then qiyas is real, and it is apparent, except that the author of al-Tahrir did not transmit the answer by metaphor, but rather transmitted the answer that it is reducible to qiyas al-'illa for including the cause of the ruling, so it was criticized that then qiyas is not the mentioned one. As for the answer by assuming metaphor, even if this is not objected to, then qiyas al-dalala becomes two qiyases, and no one has said that, so reflect. (And) regarding the second: just as equality is intended to be more general than implicit, so too equality is intended to be more general than being actual or hypothetical. And qiyas al-'aks returns to inference by entailment and qiyas to establish it. In the mentioned example, if fasting were not required as a condition in i'tikaf, it would not be required by vow like prayer, for when it is not required as a condition in it, it is not required by vow, while it is required by vow, so it must be a condition in it. So equality here is hypothetical on the hypothesis of its non-requirement as a condition. And the author gave another example and said: (for example: if it is said) as the Shafi'is say: objection is established against her when she marries without the guardian's permission, so the marriage from her is invalid, like the man, since objection is not established against him when he marries himself, his marriage is valid. So its conclusion: if the marriage from her were valid, she would become like a man, so objection would not be established against her, while it has been established. And he chose this example only to indicate that the answer that the intended is to measure the non-vowed fast of i'tikaf against a vowed one by tanqih al-manat and canceling the specificity of the vow, because if it had an effect, prayer would also be obligatory by vow, so mentioning prayer to cancel the specificity is insufficient due to its non-application in this example. Similarly, the answer that the intended ruling there is to equalize the state of vow and its absence in the fast of i'tikaf like prayer, so understand.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a definition of qiyas (analogical deduction) as understood in Hanafi usul, presented as a commentary on a previous definition. It begins by stating that the 'illa (effective cause) of the branch case is a single cause not known merely by language, which is the view of Sadr al-Shari'ah. The definition given is: establishing the ruling of the original case for the branch case by associating them in the cause and ruling, i.e., equating the branch with the original in both cause and ruling. The author notes that calling the act of a mujtahid 'qiyas' is a concession (musamaha) because qiyas is actually a divine proof, not a human action; however, since understanding it involves the mujtahid's effort, the term may be applied metaphorically.

The text then addresses objections to the definition. The first objection concerns 'qiyas al-dalala' (indicative analogy), which mentions the necessary concomitant of the cause (lazum al-'illa) rather than the cause itself, so it does not involve equality in the cause. The second objection concerns 'qiyas al-'aks' (inverse analogy), which establishes the opposite ruling by the opposite cause, such as: fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf if vowed, but not without a vow; similarly, prayer is not required even with a vow because it is not a condition in i'tikaf, so fasting must be a condition. The responses are given in detail. For both objections, the first response is a categorical denial: these are not considered qiyas in the real sense, only metaphorically. For qiyas al-dalala, a second response is that the equality in the definition includes implicit equality, i.e., even if the shared attribute is not the direct cause, it implies the cause. For example, in the stolen item case, both the returned and destroyed items share the attribute 'return', which implies preservation of wealth, which is the real cause. The text interacts with al-Tahrir's position, noting that if we allow metaphorical extension, qiyas al-dalala becomes two types of qiyas, which no one holds. For qiyas al-'aks, the response is that equality can be actual or hypothetical (taqdiriyya); the inverse reasoning relies on an assumed equality if the original ruling were absent. The author illustrates with a Shafi'i example concerning marriage without guardian consent, emphasizing that the correct answer involves tanqih al-manat (refinement of the ratio legis) and canceling the specificity of the vow in the earlier example. The passage concludes with urging understanding (fafham).

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Equating the branch with the original in cause and ruling, i.e., extending the ruling from a known case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.
مسامحة (musāmaha): Concession or metaphorical application; here, applying 'qiyas' to the mujtahid's act is a metaphorical extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Defending the Definition: Qiyas al-Dalala and Qiyas al-'Aks
Responding to objections against the definition of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul accepts qiyas al-dalala and qiyas al-'aks under the definition of qiyas by invoking implicit and hypothetical equality, and identify the responses to objections.

Core Idea
Implicit and hypothetical equality extend qiyas to borderline cases.

This lesson addresses two classic objections to the definition of qiyas: that qiyas al-dalala (indicative analogy) and qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy) do not involve direct equality in the cause. The Hanafi response reframes the definition to include implicit and hypothetical equality, thereby preserving the unity of the definition while accommodating these recognized forms of reasoning. We will examine the arguments and the nuanced interplay of metaphor and conceptual broadening.

Guided Path
1
State the two objections
Identify qiyas al-dalala (mentions the necessary concomitant of the cause) and qiyas al-'aks (establishes opposite ruling by opposite cause). Both are alleged to fall outside the definition because they lack direct equality in the cause.
These objections challenge the comprehensiveness of the definition.
2
Follow the first response: denial and metaphor
The initial response is that these forms are not true qiyas; calling them qiyas is metaphorical. Understand this as a 'block and concede' strategy.
This is a defensive move to protect the core definition.
3
Unpack the second response for qiyas al-dalala: implicit equality
The definition's 'equality' is general enough to include implicit equality. In qiyas al-dalala, the shared attribute implies the cause, even if not directly stated. Example: stolen item return implies preservation of wealth.
This broadening uses the concept of implication (tadammun).
4
Unpack the second response for qiyas al-'aks: hypothetical equality
Equality can be actual or hypothetical. In qiyas al-'aks, we assume the absence of the ruling in one case to establish the opposite. This is reasoning by entailment, but the equality is hypothetical on the condition of absence.
The Shafi'i marriage example illustrates this.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
