(تحقيقاً أو تقريراً) وقياس العكس راجع إلى الاستدلال بالملازمة والقياس لإثباتها، ففي المثال المذكور لو لم يجب الصوم شرطاً في الاعتكاف لم يجب بالنذر كالصلاة، فإنها لما لم تجب شرطاً فيه لم تجب بالنذر، مع The 'illa (cause) of the branch is for a single cause not grasped by mere language, and it is for Sadr al-Shari'ah. (And) it was said: (establishing) the ruling of the original for the branch with associating to other than that, as may be said: equalizing the branch with the original in the cause and ruling. (And it) i.e., applying qiyas to the act, is a concession, because qiyas is a divine proof placed by the Lawgiver to know His rulings, and it is not an act of anyone, but since its knowledge is by the act of the mujtahid, it may be applied metaphorically. Then in some definitions there are investigations and answers to be sought from the lengthy works. (And it was objected) to the reverse definition of qiyas al-dalala, which is what mentions the necessary of the cause without it because it is not equality in the cause, and qiyas al-'aks, which is what establishes the opposite of the ruling by the opposite of the cause, such as our saying: when fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf by vow, it is obligatory without it, like prayer, which when not obligatory with it by vow is not obligatory without it. (And the answer first) to both is preventing them from being within the defined, and we do not call them qiyas except metaphorically. And secondly regarding the first: the equality mentioned in the definition is more general than being explicit or implicit, and implicit equality is attained. For example: when it is said regarding the stolen item: it must be returned intact, so compensation is due if it is destroyed, like the usurped item; the existence of the shared term 'return' in them even if it is not the cause, but it includes the intention of preserving wealth, or if you wish you may say: transgression which is the reality. (And what is in al-Tahrir: qiyas then is not the mentioned one) rather it is what mentions the implied cause, because it is equality in the cause truly. So I say in it: metaphorical use in the limit does not necessitate metaphorical use in the limited. And since equality is intended to include implicit, even if metaphorical, then qiyas is real, and it is apparent, except that the author of al-Tahrir did not transmit the answer by metaphor, but rather transmitted the answer that it is reducible to qiyas al-'illa for including the cause of the ruling, so it was criticized that then qiyas is not the mentioned one. As for the answer by assuming metaphor, even if this is not objected to, then qiyas al-dalala becomes two qiyases, and no one has said that, so reflect. (And) regarding the second: just as equality is intended to be more general than implicit, so too equality is intended to be more general than being actual or hypothetical. And qiyas al-'aks returns to inference by entailment and qiyas to establish it. In the mentioned example, if fasting were not required as a condition in i'tikaf, it would not be required by vow like prayer, for when it is not required as a condition in it, it is not required by vow, while it is required by vow, so it must be a condition in it. So equality here is hypothetical on the hypothesis of its non-requirement as a condition. And the author gave another example and said: (for example: if it is said) as the Shafi'is say: objection is established against her when she marries without the guardian's permission, so the marriage from her is invalid, like the man, since objection is not established against him when he marries himself, his marriage is valid. So its conclusion: if the marriage from her were valid, she would become like a man, so objection would not be established against her, while it has been established. And he chose this example only to indicate that the answer that the intended is to measure the non-vowed fast of i'tikaf against a vowed one by tanqih al-manat and canceling the specificity of the vow, because if it had an effect, prayer would also be obligatory by vow, so mentioning prayer to cancel the specificity is insufficient due to its non-application in this example. Similarly, the answer that the intended ruling there is to equalize the state of vow and its absence in the fast of i'tikaf like prayer, so understand.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a definition of qiyas (analogical deduction) as understood in Hanafi usul, presented as a commentary on a previous definition. It begins by stating that the 'illa (effective cause) of the branch case is a single cause not known merely by language, which is the view of Sadr al-Shari'ah. The definition given is: establishing the ruling of the original case for the branch case by associating them in the cause and ruling, i.e., equating the branch with the original in both cause and ruling. The author notes that calling the act of a mujtahid 'qiyas' is a concession (musamaha) because qiyas is actually a divine proof, not a human action; however, since understanding it involves the mujtahid's effort, the term may be applied metaphorically.

The text then addresses objections to the definition. The first objection concerns 'qiyas al-dalala' (indicative analogy), which mentions the necessary concomitant of the cause (lazum al-'illa) rather than the cause itself, so it does not involve equality in the cause. The second objection concerns 'qiyas al-'aks' (inverse analogy), which establishes the opposite ruling by the opposite cause, such as: fasting is obligatory in i'tikaf if vowed, but not without a vow; similarly, prayer is not required even with a vow because it is not a condition in i'tikaf, so fasting must be a condition. The responses are given in detail. For both objections, the first response is a categorical denial: these are not considered qiyas in the real sense, only metaphorically. For qiyas al-dalala, a second response is that the equality in the definition includes implicit equality, i.e., even if the shared attribute is not the direct cause, it implies the cause. For example, in the stolen item case, both the returned and destroyed items share the attribute 'return', which implies preservation of wealth, which is the real cause. The text interacts with al-Tahrir's position, noting that if we allow metaphorical extension, qiyas al-dalala becomes two types of qiyas, which no one holds. For qiyas al-'aks, the response is that equality can be actual or hypothetical (taqdiriyya); the inverse reasoning relies on an assumed equality if the original ruling were absent. The author illustrates with a Shafi'i example concerning marriage without guardian consent, emphasizing that the correct answer involves tanqih al-manat (refinement of the ratio legis) and canceling the specificity of the vow in the earlier example. The passage concludes with urging understanding (fafham).

Key Terms
قياس الدلالة (qiyās al-dalāla): A type of analogy that mentions the necessary concomitant (lazim) of the cause rather than the cause itself.
قياس العكس (qiyās al-ʿaks): An inverse analogy that establishes the opposite ruling by the opposite cause.
مساواة ضمنية (musāwāt ḍimniyya): Implicit equality: the shared attribute implies the cause even if not directly stated.
مساواة تقديرية (musāwāt taqdīriyya): Hypothetical equality: equality assumed on a hypothetical condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is not qiyas at all, only metaphorical.
B) Equality includes implicit equality, and qiyas al-dalala involves such.
C) The objector is mistaken about the definition.
D) It is reduced to qiyas al-'illa as per al-Tahrir.

Key Takeaway
Implicit and hypothetical equality extend the definition of qiyas to include qiyas al-dalala and qiyas al-'aks.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Four Pillars of Qiyas (Arkan al-Qiyas)
Listing and explaining the four essential components of analogical deduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four pillars of qiyas, analyze the different definitions of the asl, and apply the two-premise logical structure.

Core Idea
Qiyas has four pillars, but the true pillar is the common attribute that unites original and branch.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas (analogical deduction) is a fundamental proof for deriving rulings. To perform a valid qiyas, one must understand its essential components—the four pillars (arkan). This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut lists these pillars and clarifies a key difference of opinion about what constitutes the original case (asl). It also emphasizes that the common attribute (wasf jami') is not a standalone pillar but the element that establishes equality between the original and branch. Let's break down the text step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
Read the first line: 'ثم أركانه أربعة'. The text then lists one: الأصل, two: حكمه, three: الفرع, four: الوصف الجامع. Note that 'حكمه' refers to the ruling of the original, and 'الفرع' is the branch case.
The asl is the original case (e.g., wine).
2
Analyze the dispute on the asl
The text says 'وقيل' three times: some say asl is the proof (dalil), some say it is the ruling (hukm). Understand that the conventional view among jurists is that asl is the case itself, but each interpretation has a valid perspective.
This intra-Hanafi difference shows the flexibility in defining the asl.
3
Recognize the role of the unifying attribute
The fourth pillar is the wasf jami'. The text explains that it is 'أصل لحكم الفرع' (a root for the branch's ruling) and 'فرع لحكم الأصل' (a branch from the original's ruling). It cautions that most Hanafis consider it the pillar, but they mean it realizes equality externally, not alone.
The attribute is the effective cause ('illa).
4
Structure qiyas as two premises
The text gives the example: 'النبيذ مسكر كالخمر والخمر حرام للإسكار فالنبيذ حرام'. This is two premises (branch shares attribute, original has ruling due to attribute) leading to the conclusion. So the qiyas argument has these four components as its building blocks.
The two premises are the primary pillars; the four are secondary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أركانه أربعة أحدها الأصل المحل المشبه به وهو المتعارف) بين الفقهاء (كالخمر، بل شربه في قياس النبيذ عليه بجامع الشدة المطربة (وقيل) الأصل (دليله) دليل المشبه به فهو في المثال المذكور قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَمُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ ﴾ [المائدة: ۹۰] (وقيل: حكمه فهو حرمة الخمر ولكل وجه ( و ) الثاني (حكمه ) كالحرمة في المثال المذكور (و) الثالث (الفرع المحل المشبه كالنبيذ وذلك باعتبار الحكم) فإن حكمه فرع لحكمه (و) الرابع (الوصف الجامع) كالشدّة المطربة (وهو) أصل لحكم الفرع) فإنه يثبت به في نظر المجتهد (وفرع لحكم الأصل (غالباً وقد لا يكون فرعاً كما إذا كانت منصوصة والتحقيق أن القياس (حجة كسائر الحجج (فركنها المقدمتان) أولاً (فما يتحصلان به) أركان ثانياً فإنها أركان الأركان وهي الأمور الأربعة كما) في قولك : النبيذ مسكر كالخمر والخمر حرام للإسكار) فالنبيذ حرام (وأما قول أكثر الحنفية أن ركنها هو العلة المشتركة فأرادوا به ما يحقق المساواة في الخارج بالفعل لا أنها ركن وحدها دون الأصل والفرع فتدبر
Then its pillars are four. First: the original (asl) which is the thing compared to, and it is what is conventionally known among jurists (like wine, or rather its drinking in measuring date-wine (nabeedh) by it due to the common trait of intoxication-producing strength). (And it was said) that the original is its proof, i.e., the proof of the thing compared to, so in the example it is the verse: 'Indeed wine, gambling, idols, and divining arrows are abomination from the work of Satan, so avoid it' [Quran 5:90]. (And it was said) that the original is its ruling, i.e., the prohibition of wine. And each has a face. (And) the second (pillar) is its ruling (al-hukm), like prohibition in the mentioned example. (And) the third (pillar) is the branch (far'), the thing compared, like nabeedh (date-wine), and that is with respect to the ruling, for its ruling follows from its ruling. (And) the fourth (pillar) is the unifying attribute (al-wasf al-jami'), like strength causing intoxication. It is a root for the ruling of the branch, for it is established by it in the view of the mujtahid, and it is a branch from the ruling of the original usually, and may not be a branch when it is textual. And the investigation is that qiyas is a proof like other proofs. Its pillar (in one sense) is the two premises first. Then what results from them are pillars secondarily, for they are the pillars of the pillars, and they are the four things as in your saying: Nabeedh is intoxicating like wine, and wine is prohibited due to intoxication, so nabeedh is prohibited. As for the statement of most Hanafis that its pillar is the common attribute, they meant by it what realizes equality externally actually, not that it is a pillar alone without the original and the branch, so reflect.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage enumerates the four arkan (pillars) of qiyas, which are essential components for a valid analogy. The first pillar is the asl (original case), the subject of comparison. Conventionally among jurists, the asl is exemplified by khamr (wine) or its drinking, which serves as the basis for measuring nabeedh (date-wine) due to the shared attribute of intoxication. There is a difference of opinion on what constitutes the asl: some say it is the proof (dalil) of the original—for wine, the Quranic verse prohibiting it (5:90); others say it is the ruling itself (prohibition). Both views are valid. The second pillar is the hukm (ruling) of the original, such as the prohibition of wine. The third pillar is the far' (branch), the new case being compared, like nabeedh. The fourth pillar is the wasf al-jami' (unifying attribute), which is the common cause linking the branch to the original, like the intoxicating strength (shidda mutriba). The description of this attribute is that it serves as the basis (asl) for the branch's ruling in the mujtahid's view, and it is usually derived from the original's ruling, unless the attribute itself is textually indicated (manususa). The passage then clarifies the logical structure: qiyas is a proof composed of two premises (e.g., 'nabeedh is intoxicating like wine' and 'wine is prohibited for intoxication'), which yield the conclusion. The four components are secondary pillars (arkan al-arkan). Most Hanafis consider the common attribute as the primary pillar, but they mean that it is the operative element that realizes equality externally, not that it stands alone without the original and branch. The instruction 'fata'ammal' (reflect) invites careful consideration.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-aṣl): The original case from which the ruling is derived; the thing compared to in analogy.
الوصف الجامع (al-waṣf al-jāmiʿ): The common attribute between the original and branch cases that is the effective cause ('illa) for the ruling.
الفرع (al-farʿ): The new case being compared to the original in analogy.
الحكم (al-ḥukm): The ruling of the original case, which is to be transferred to the branch case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view mentioned in the text, what do most Hanafis mean when they say the pillar of qiyas is the common attribute?
A) The common attribute is sufficient without considering the original and branch
B) The common attribute is the element that realizes equality externally, not a stand-alone pillar
C) The common attribute is identical to the ruling
D) The common attribute must be textually indicated

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of qiyas are the original case, its ruling, the branch case, and the common attribute; the common attribute is the operative cause but requires the other pillars to complete the analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Four Pillars of Qiyas
Defining the pillars of qiyas and its evidentiary value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four pillars of qiyas (asl, hukm, far', 'illah) and explain the Hanafi view that the 'illah is the central pillar that transmits the ruling.

Core Idea
Qiyas has four pillars; the 'illah is the effective cause that carries the ruling from original to branch.

This passage defines the four essential components of qiyas using the Quranic example of wine prohibition extended to nabidh. You will learn each pillar and the critical role of the common cause ('illah) in the Hanafi framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verse and the four pillars
Locate the verse (al-Ma'idah 5:90) and note how the author extracts asl (wine), hukm (prohibition), far' (nabidh), and wasf jami' (intoxication).
The verse is used as an illustration, not as the proof for the legality of qiyas itself.
2
Define each pillar
For each pillar, state its definition and role: asl is the original case with a known ruling; hukm is that ruling; far' is the new case; 'illah is the common attribute that justifies extending the ruling.
The 'illah is the key that makes the analogy valid.
3
Understand the Hanafi emphasis on the 'illah as the rukn
The text notes that most Hanafis consider the 'illah alone the pillar of qiyas, but clarifies that the original and branch are still necessary as the loci of the 'illah.
This highlights the centrality of causation in Hanafi legal reasoning.
4
Differentiate between the four pillars and the two premises
The qiyas syllogism consists of two premises (e.g., 'Nabidh is intoxicating like wine' and 'Wine is prohibited due to intoxication') which yield the conclusion. The four pillars are the components of the analogy, not the syllogistic form.
This distinction helps avoid confusion with logical qiyas.
5
Recognize the dual nature of the 'illah
The 'illah is described as an origin (asl) for the ruling of the branch and a branch (far') of the ruling of the original, except when textually stated. This indicates its relational role.
Understanding this prepares you for the epistemological discussion in Lesson 2.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع/ القياس الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ ﴾ [المائدة: ۹۰] (وقيل: حكمه فهو حرمة الخمر ولكل وجه ( و ) الثاني (حكمه ) كالحرمة في المثال المذكور (و) الثالث (الفرع المحل المشبه كالنبيذ وذلك باعتبار الحكم) فإن حكمه فرع لحكمه (و) الرابع (الوصف الجامع) كالشدّة المطربة (وهو) أصل لحكم الفرع) فإنه يثبت به في نظر المجتهد (وفرع لحكم الأصل (غالباً وقد لا يكون فرعاً كما إذا كانت منصوصة والتحقيق أن القياس (حجة كسائر الحجج (فركنها المقدمتان) أولاً (فما يتحصلان به) أركان ثانياً فإنها أركان الأركان وهي الأمور الأربعة كما) في قولك : النبيذ مسكر كالخمر والخمر حرام للإسكار) فالنبيذ حرام (وأما قول أكثر الحنفية أن ركنها هو العلة المشتركة فأرادوا به ما يحقق المساواة في الخارج بالفعل لا أنها ركن وحدها دون الأصل والفرع فتدبر وحكمه أي حكم القياس ثبوت حكم الأصل في الفرع والظن به بعد النظر لا القطع) به (وإن قطع بمقدماته ومواده) وهذا بخلاف سائر الحجج فإنه يحصل القطع بعد القطع بمقدماتها (وذلك لأن طريق الإيصال فيه (ظني) فلا يحصل به القطع فإنه لا يرفع احتمال كون الأصل شرطاً) في حكمه وتأثير علته أو الفرع مانعاً عن الحكم فلا يصل إليه الحكم، ولما كان يرد عليه أن القياس إنما ينتج بملاحظة أن كلما توجد العلة يوجد المعلول وهذه مقدمة قطعية توجب القطع إن كانت العلة قطعية، وإذا جوز كون الأصل شرطاً والفرع مانعاً فقد منع عليه العلة وكان الكلام عند قطعية المقدمات قال (ولو) قطع بكون العلة علة تامة وبنى الإنتاج على تلك المقدمة (رجع إلى القياس المنطقي ولم يبق قياساً فقهياً (فتفكر) وهذا ليس بشيء فإن رجوعه إلى القياس المنطقي لا شناعة فيه، بل هو الأحق بالقبول فإن حاصله إلى أن يرجع النبيذ توجد فيه الشدة المطربة التي هي علة الحرمة، وكل ما يوجد فيه علة الحرمة فهو حرام فطريق الإيصال فيه شكل أول قطعي الإنتاج، وإنما يجيء الظن من المادة من مظنونية العلة، فإذا قطع بالعلية وجب القطع البتة واعتبر بدلالة النص، فإنها إنما توجب القطع لكون العلة هناك مقطوعة، فإن حصل القطع بالعلة اجتهاداً لا من اللغة يحصل القطع أيضاً، فالأولى أن يبنى الحكم على الاستقراء، فإنا تتبعنا القياسات المخرجة بالاجتهاد وجدنا عللها مظنونة، فلذا حكم بأنه لا يفيد القطع فتأمل ثم التحقيق أن الموجود في الفرع عين العلة التي للأصل وعين الحكم الموجود في الأصل (لأنهما محمولان على الأصل (وهو) أي المحمول (لا بشرط شيء) فحكم الأصل وعلته لا بشرط شيء وهو بعينه موجود في الفرع (ولأن المشتمل على المصلحة والمفسدة إنما هو الطبيعة المطلقة لا الخصوصيات والعلة الأمر المشتمل على المصلحة أو المفسدة لكن شارح المختصر ذهب إلى المثلية أي إلى أن التحقيق في الفرع مثل حكم الأصل وعلته كما يشير إليه تعريف الإمام علم الهدى قدس سره (معللاً بأن المعنى الشخصي لا يقوم بمحلين فلا يقوم ما قام بالأصل بالفرع بل مثله (وذلك) إنما قال نظراً إلى الحصص والحصة الموجودة في الأصل من العلة والحكم لا توجد في الفرع أصلاً (أو) نظراً (إلى نفي وجود الطبيعة المطلقة (كما هو رأي ابن الحاجب) فليس هناك لا بشرط شيء يوجد في الأصل وفي الفرع (فتأمل) وهذا فيه خفاء، فإن الطبيعة وإن لم تكن موجودة في الخارج لكن صدقها على الموجودات غير منكر، ومن البين أنها صادقة على الأصل والفرع، وهذا هو المعنى باشتراك العلة وهو متحقق وليس المراد من الاشتراك في العلة تحققها فيهما بنفسها، فإن العلة ربما تكون معنى انتزاعياً لا يمكن أن يوجد في الخارج، وقد جوز المصنف عليه العدميات فافهم.
The fourth principle/ Qiyas: 'Wine, gambling, idols, and arrows are an abomination of Satan's handiwork, so avoid it' [Al-Ma'idah: 90]. (And it is said: its ruling is the prohibition of wine, and each has an aspect). (And) the second (its ruling) like prohibition in the mentioned example. (And) the third (the branch, the assimilated case, like nabidh, and that by consideration of the ruling) for its ruling is a branch of his ruling. (And) the fourth (the comprehensive attribute) like the intoxicating potency. (It is) an origin for the ruling of the branch) for it is established by it in the view of the mujtahid, (and a branch of the ruling of the original) usually, and sometimes it is not a branch, as when it is textually stated. And the investigation is that qiyas (is a proof like other proofs. Its pillar is the two premises) first. (Then what is obtained from them are the pillars) secondarily, for they are the pillars of the pillars, which are the four matters, as in your saying: Nabidh is intoxicating like wine, and wine is prohibited due to intoxication, so nabidh is prohibited. (As for the statement of most Hanafis that its pillar is the common cause, they meant by that what actualizes equality in external existence in actuality, not that it is a pillar by itself without the original and the branch, so ponder. And its ruling, i.e., the ruling of qiyas, is the establishment of the ruling of the original in the branch, and probability therein after reflection, not certainty) (even if its premises and materials are certain). And this is contrary to other proofs, for certainty is obtained after certainty of their premises. (And that is because the method of transmission therein is probable, so certainty is not obtained by it, for it does not remove the possibility that the original is a condition) in its ruling and the effect of its cause, or that the branch is a preventer of the ruling, so the ruling does not reach it. Since it may be objected that qiyas only results by observing that whenever the cause exists, the effect exists, and this is a certain premise that necessitates certainty if the cause is certain; and if one allows the original to be a condition and the branch a preventer, then the cause is prevented, and the discussion was when the premises were certain. He said: (If) one is certain that the cause is a complete cause and bases the result on that premise, (it reverts to logical qiyas and is no longer legal qiyas, so reflect). But this is nothing, for its reversion to logical qiyas has no disgrace; rather, it is more deserving of acceptance, for its summary is that nabidh contains the intoxicating potency which is the cause of prohibition, and everything that contains the cause of prohibition is prohibited. So the method of transmission is a first figure that is certain in result. Probability only arises from the material, from the probability of the cause. So if one is certain of the causality, certainty is necessarily required, and it is considered like textual indication, for it requires certainty because the cause there is certain. So if certainty of the cause is obtained through ijtihad, not from language, certainty is also obtained. So it is better to base the ruling on induction, for we have traced the qiyas derived through ijtihad and found their causes probable; therefore it is ruled that it does not yield certainty. Then ponder. Then the investigation is that what exists in the branch is the very cause of the original and the very ruling existing in the original (because they are predicated on the original. (It) i.e., that which is predicated, is unconditioned. So the ruling of the original and its cause are unconditioned, and it is exactly what exists in the branch. (And because that which contains benefit or harm is only the absolute nature, not particularities, and the cause is that which contains the benefit or harm. But the commentator of al-Mukhtar opted for similarity, i.e., that the reality in the branch is like the ruling of the original and its cause, as indicated by the definition of Imam 'Alam al-Huda, may his secret be sanctified, (arguing that the individual meaning does not subsist in two loci, so what subsists in the original does not subsist in the branch except its like. (And that) he said only considering the portions, and the portion of the cause and ruling existing in the original does not exist in the branch at all. (Or) considering (the denial of the existence of the absolute nature (as is the view of Ibn al-Hajib), so there is no unconditioned thing that exists in the original and the branch. (Ponder) And this is obscure, for although nature does not exist externally, its truthfulness to existents is undeniable, and it is clear that it is true of the original and the branch, and this is the meaning of the commonality of the cause, and it is realized. The intended meaning of commonality in the cause is not its actual existence in both, for the cause may be an abstract meaning that cannot exist externally, and the author allowed non-existential causes, so understand.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analysis of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by illustrating the four pillars (arkan) of qiyas using the Quranic verse on prohibition of wine: the original (asl) is wine, the ruling (hukm) is prohibition, the branch (far') is nabidh (date wine), and the common attribute (wasf jami') is intoxication. The text then clarifies that the essential pillar according to most Hanafis is the common cause ('illah), but this does not mean the original and branch are ignored; the cause is the means of equalization. The key point is epistemological: qiyas yields zann (probability), not qat' (certainty), even if its premises are certain, because the method of transmission (the link via 'illah) is inherently zanni. It addresses an objection: if the cause is certain, the result should be certain, as in logical syllogism. The author responds by noting that legal qiyas differs because the 'illah is often probable (maznuna), derived via ijtihad, not from textual certainty. The text then discusses whether the existence of the 'illah in the branch is identical or similar, siding with the view that the absolute nature (tabi'ah mutlaqah) applies to both, allowing commonality. The overall aim is to define qiyas precisely within Hanafi methodology, distinguishing it from logical qiyas and establishing its probative value as zanni.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a branch case due to a shared effective cause.
العلة (al-'illah): The effective cause or common attribute that justifies analogy.
الأصل (al-asl): The original case with an established ruling from the primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the fourth pillar (al-wasf al-jami') in the qiyas of wine to nabidh?
A) Wine
B) Prohibition
C) Nabidh
D) Intoxicating potency (shiddah mutribah)

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of qiyas are asl, hukm, far', and 'illah, with the 'illah being the crucial effective cause that transfers the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Why Qiyas Yields Probability
Defining the pillars of qiyas and its evidentiary value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qiyas yields probability (zann) rather than certainty, and evaluate the objection that it should produce certainty when the cause is certain.

Core Idea
Legal qiyas is inherently probable because the cause is often uncertain, though logical qiyas can be certain.

The passage now addresses a critical epistemological question: why does qiyas not produce certainty even when its premises are certain? You will follow the author's reasoning, from the nature of the cause to the objection about logical qiyas and the final conclusion based on induction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim about qiyas
The text states that the ruling of qiyas is the establishment of the original's ruling in the branch with probability (zann), not certainty, even if premises are certain.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
2
Understand the reason for probability
The method of transmission (tariq al-iyqal) is probable (zanni) because it does not eliminate the possibility that the original is a condition or the branch a preventer.
The 'illah may not be fully effective due to potential contexts.
3
Analyze the objection from logical qiyas
An objector argues: if the cause is certain, the conclusion should be certain. The author presents the response: if the cause is certain, it becomes logical qiyas (first figure syllogism), which is certain but distinct from legal qiyas.
The author accepts logical qiyas as valid but notes that legal qiyas typically deals with probable causes.
4
Follow the induction-based resolution
The author prefers to base the ruling on induction: ijtihadi qiyas are examined and their causes are found to be probable, so qiyas generally yields zann.
Even if one certain cause is found, the method remains zanni due to the inductive evidence.
5
Examine the identity vs. similarity debate
The text discusses whether the 'illah in the branch is identical or similar to that in the original. The preferred view is that the absolute nature (tabi'ah mutlaqah) applies to both, allowing commonality.
This supports the notion that the 'illah is the same in essence, not just similar.

وعلته كما يشير إليه تعريف الإمام علم الهدى قدس سره (معللاً بأن المعنى الشخصي لا يقوم بمحلين فلا يقوم ما قام بالأصل بالفرع بل مثله (وذلك) إنما قال نظراً إلى الحصص والحصة الموجودة في الأصل من العلة والحكم لا توجد في الفرع أصلاً (أو) نظراً (إلى نفي وجود الطبيعة المطلقة (كما هو رأي ابن الحاجب) فليس هناك لا بشرط شيء يوجد في الأصل وفي الفرع (فتأمل) وهذا فيه خفاء، فإن الطبيعة وإن لم تكن موجودة في انتزاعياً لا يمكن أن يوجد في الخارج، وقد جوز المصنف عليه العدميات فافهم.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analysis of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by illustrating the four pillars (arkan) of qiyas using the Quranic verse on prohibition of wine: the original (asl) is wine, the ruling (hukm) is prohibition, the branch (far') is nabidh (date wine), and the common attribute (wasf jami') is intoxication. The text then clarifies that the essential pillar according to most Hanafis is the common cause ('illah), but this does not mean the original and branch are ignored; the cause is the means of equalization. The key point is epistemological: qiyas yields zann (probability), not qat' (certainty), even if its premises are certain, because the method of transmission (the link via 'illah) is inherently zanni. It addresses an objection: if the cause is certain, the result should be certain, as in logical syllogism. The author responds by noting that legal qiyas differs because the 'illah is often probable (maznuna), derived via ijtihad, not from textual certainty. The text then discusses whether the existence of the 'illah in the branch is identical or similar, siding with the view that the absolute nature (tabi'ah mutlaqah) applies to both, allowing commonality. The overall aim is to define qiyas precisely within Hanafi methodology, distinguishing it from logical qiyas and establishing its probative value as zanni.

Key Terms
الظن (al-zann): Probability; a belief that is stronger than doubt but less than certainty.
القطع (al-qat'): Certainty; a belief that admits no doubt.
طريق الإيصال (tariq al-iyqal): The method of transmission or linking the cause to the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary reason qiyas does not produce certainty?
A) The Quran explicitly states that analogy is uncertain.
B) The method of transmission (طريق الإيصال) is probable (zanni).
C) The original and branch are never truly comparable.
D) Qiyas is not a valid proof in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas yields probability (zann) because the method of transmission is zanni, and the causes are typically probable, as confirmed by induction.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Conditions of Qiyas: Ma'qul al-Ma'na and Non-Specificity
Stating conditions of qiyas with examples and a specific concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for qiyas by determining whether a given original ruling is ma'qul al-ma'na and whether it is a special concession (khususiyyah) that cannot be analogized.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires the original ruling to have a rationally understood cause and not be a special concession.

This lesson explores two foundational conditions for valid analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. First, the ruling of the original case must be "ma'qul al-ma'na" — its legal cause must be intellectually discernible, not purely devotional. Second, the ruling must not be specific to the original case, excluding special concessions that cannot be extended by analogy. We will unpack these conditions using examples from the text, including the validity of fasting after forgetful eating and the Bedouin expiation story.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Locate the first condition stated: 'minha li hukm al-asl an yakuna ma'qul al-ma'na.' Understand that this means the 'illah (cause) of the original ruling must be rationally knowable.
2
Apply the condition with examples
Examine the counter-examples: numbers of rak'at, zakat amounts, and hudud (penalties) are not ma'qul al-ma'na. Note the special cases of forgetful eating during fasting and forgetting basmalah during slaughter — the text clarifies these are not purely devotional because they involve missing conditions.
This step demonstrates the nuance: rulings that seem 'ta'abbudi' may still have a rational basis when analyzed properly.
3
Identify the second condition
Find 'wa minha an la yakhtassa bihi' — the ruling must not be specific to the original case. Recognize that if a ruling is a special concession (rukhsah) for a particular person or situation, it cannot be extended by qiyas.
4
Analyze the Bedouin example
The hadith of the Bedouin who was allowed to feed his expiation to his family is a special concession because the Prophet laughed and approved it. The text argues this is 'khususiyyah', not a generalizable qiyas precedent.
Note the debate: the majority consider this ma'qul al-'illa but specific; some consider it purely devotional. The Hanafi position is that it is rationally understandable but specific.

وكذا ليس شرط الحل التسمية مطلقاً بل حال التذكر بل التحقيق أن الصورتين مما يفقد فيهما الشرط الذي يليه ومنها أن لا يكون مختصاً به أي بالمنصوص بدليل دل عليه : فإنه إذا كان مختصاً بطل الإلحاق به قطعاً كإطعام الأعرابي كفارته لأهله عن أبي هريرة قال: جاء رجل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم فقال: هلکت یا رسول الله قال وما أهلكك؟ قال : وقعت على أهلي في رمضان فقال: «هل تجد ما تعتق رقبة؟ قال : لا قال: «فهل تستطيع أن تصوم شهرين متتابعين؟ قال: لا، قال: «فهل تجد ما تطعم ستين مسكيناً ؟ قال : لا ، قال : ثم جلس فأتى النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم بعرق فيه تمر فقال : تصدق بهذا فقال : أعلى أفقر منا فما بين لا بتيها أهل بيت أحوج إليه منا، فضحك النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم حتى بدت أنيابه ثم قال : اذهب فأطعمه أهلك ؟ رواه مسلم فهذا أي إطعام أهله طعام كفارته (على قول الجمهور) لا من قبيل أعداد الركعات فإنه معقول العلة لا كما في التحرير حيث أورده نظير الغير معقول العلة لأنه كأحد من الفقراء فسد خلته كسد خلة الفقير الآخر وهو العلة (لكن تفوت) به حكمة الزجر) على تقدير فإنه عسى أن يكون رضا الله
Chapter: On the Conditions of Qiyas. Among them for the ruling of the original is that it be ma'qul al-ma'na (rationally understandable), i.e., that its cause can be known, not like the numbers of rak'at and the quantities of zakat. According to the Hanafis, penalties (hudud) are included in this. And among them, the validity of fasting when eating forgetfully is counted, established by his saying, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions: 'Complete your fast, for Allah has fed you and given you drink, and there is no making up for you.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni. And the permissibility of the slaughtered animal when leaving the basmalah (similarly) i.e., forgetfully, established by his saying, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions: 'If one forgets to say the name when slaughtering, let him say the name and mention Allah, then eat.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi. So in al-Taysir, because the existence of something without its pillar or condition is not rationally understandable. And by eating forgetfully, the pillar of fasting is lost, because it is abstention, and it has been lost. And in leaving the basmalah forgetfully, the condition of permissibility is lost, because the basmalah is a condition by text. And in his statement 'it is counted among them' there is an indication of weakness in it, for one could say: we do not accept that the pillar of fasting is abstaining from eating absolutely, but rather abstaining from eating while remembering. Likewise, the condition of permissibility is not the basmalah absolutely, but rather when remembering. Rather, the investigation is that both cases involve the loss of the relevant condition. And among them is that it not be specific to it, i.e., to the textually stated ruling, by evidence indicating that. For if it is specific, then analogizing to it is invalidated absolutely, like the Bedouin feeding his expiation to his family. From Abu Hurayra, he said: A man came to the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, and said: I have perished, O Messenger of Allah. He said: What has caused you to perish? He said: I had intercourse with my wife in Ramadan. He said: Do you have a slave to free? He said: No. He said: Can you fast two consecutive months? He said: No. He said: Can you feed sixty poor people? He said: No. He said: Then he sat and brought a basket of dates to the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, and said: Give this in charity. He said: To one poorer than us? There is no household between the two lava plains more in need of it than us. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, laughed until his molars appeared, then said: Go and feed it to your family. Narrated by Muslim. So this, i.e., feeding his family with his expiation (according to the majority) is not of the type of numbers of rak'at, for it is ma'qul al-'illa, not as in al-Tahrir where he presented it as an example of what is not ma'qul al-'illa, because he is like one of the poor, his need is satisfied just as the need of another poor person is satisfied, which is the cause. But the wisdom of deterrence is lost by it, on the assumption that feeding his family is permissible, for it was established as a special concession specific to his case, because he made the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions, laugh, so Allah pardoned him. Hence Imam Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, may Allah honor his face, said: Do not belittle a good deed, even if it be a hair, for perhaps it will bring the pleasure of Allah.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the conditions (shara'it) of qiyas. It first states that the ruling of the original case (hukm al-asl) must be ma'qul al-ma'na, meaning its underlying cause ('illah) can be rationally understood. Pure devotional rulings (ta'abbudi) where the cause is unknown, like the exact numbers of rak'at in prayer or the precise amounts of zakat, cannot serve as the basis for qiyas. The Hanafis also include hudud (penalties) in this category, as their specific measures are not subject to analogical extension. The author then addresses two examples that might seem to contradict this rule: the validity of fasting when one eats forgetfully, and the permissibility of a slaughtered animal if the butcher forgets the basmalah. In both cases, the rulings are established by specific hadiths and appear to be purely devotional. However, the author argues that these are not exceptions because the conditions (remembrance) are missing; the rulings are not irrational but rather based on the absence of a necessary condition. Thus they are still ma'qul al-ma'na in a sense. The passage then introduces another condition: the ruling must not be specific to the original case (la yakhtassu bihi). The example of the Bedouin who was allowed to feed his expiation to his family is cited: this was a special concession for that individual, so it cannot be analogized to others. The author notes that according to the majority, this concession is not like purely devotional numbers; it has a rational basis (relieving need), but it is specific to that case because of the reason for the concession. The lesson thus clarifies two key conditions for a valid qiyas: (1) the original ruling must be rationally understandable (ma'qul al-ma'na), and (2) it must not be a special concession specific to that case.

Key Terms
معقول المعنى (ma'qul al-ma'na): ما يمكن إدراك علته بالعقل، أي ليس تعبدياً محضاً
التعبدي (al-ta'abbudi): ما لا تعرف علته ويعبد الله به
الخصوصية (al-khususiyah): كون الحكم مختصاً بالمنصوص عليه بدليل، فلا يجوز القياس عليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi conditions for qiyas, which of the following rulings can serve as the original case for analogical reasoning?
A) The number of rak'at in Salat al-Fajr.
B) The permissibility of a forgetful eater in Ramadan keeping his fast.
C) The Bedouin feeding his expiation to his family (as a special concession).
D) The amount of zakat on 5 camels.

Key Takeaway
For a ruling to be valid as an original in qiyas, it must be ma'qul al-ma'na and not a special concession specific to its case.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The First Condition of Qiyas: The Ruling Must Be Ma'qul al-Ma'na
Stating the first condition of qiyas with examples from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a ruling is ma'qul al-ma'na or ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na and explain why it cannot be used as the asl for qiyas.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires the original ruling's cause to be rationally perceptible; purely devotional rulings cannot be extended.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every ruling can serve as the basis for analogical reasoning. The first condition is that the hukm of the asl must be 'ma'qul al-ma'na' — its effective cause must be intelligible. This lesson unpacks that condition with examples from hadith, highlighting rulings that are purely textual (ta'abbudi) and thus outside the scope of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition
The hukm of the asl must have an identifiable 'illa (effective cause) that can be understood rationally.
This is the first condition listed in the passage.
2
Identify counterexamples
Rulings like numbers of rak'ats, amounts of zakat, and (according to Hanafis) fixed punishments are not ma'qul al-ma'na because they are based on explicit texts without a rational cause.
The passage explicitly gives these as examples of ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na.
3
Analyse the hadith examples
The hadith on forgetful eating and forgetful tasmiya show that the ruling is given regardless of a missing pillar or condition, indicating the ruling is ta'abbudi.
The author argues that these rulings cannot be extended by qiyas.
4
Evaluate the objection
Some may argue that the pillar or condition is not absolutely missing, but the author's verification (tahqiq) confirms that the condition (remembrance) is indeed missing, reinforcing the ta'abbudi nature.
This objection is mentioned in the passage and resolved.
5
Apply the condition
Given a new ruling, determine if it has a rational cause. If not, it cannot be used as asl for qiyas.
Practice in the tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل :
في شرائط القياس
للقياس (منها لحكم الأصل أن يكون معقول المعنى) أي ما تدرك علته (لا كأعداد الركعات ومقادير الزكاة ومنه عند الحنفية الحدود وقد عد منه صحة الصوم مع الأكل ناسياً) الثابتة بقوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم : «أتم صومك ، فإن الله أطعمك وسقاك، ولا قضاء عليك» رواه الدارقطني وحل الذبيحة مع ترك التسمية (كذلك) أي ناسياً، الثابت بقوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام: «فإن نسي أن يسمي حين يذبح فليسم وليذكر الله ثم ليأكل) رواه الدارقطني والبيهقي كذا في التيسير لأن وجود الشيء بدون ركنه أو شرطه غير معقول وبالأكل ناسياً يفوت ركن الصوم، لأنه الإمساك، وقد فات، وفي ترك التسمية ناسياً فإن شرط الحل، لأن التسمية شرط بالنص وفي قوله : وقد عد منه إشارة إلى الضعف فيه، فإنه لقائل أن يقول: لا نسلم أن ركن الصوم الإمساك عن الأكل مطلقاً، بل الإمساك عن الأكل مع التذكر وكذا ليس شرط الحل التسمية مطلقاً بل حال التذكر بل التحقيق أن الصورتين مما يفقد فيهما الشرط الذي يليه
Chapter: On the conditions of analogy. For analogy, (among them is that the ruling of the original must be of intelligible meaning) i.e., whose cause can be perceived (not like numbers of rak'ats and amounts of zakat, and according to the Hanafis, punishments are from it, and it includes the validity of fasting while eating forgetfully) established by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Complete your fast, for Allah has fed you and given you drink, and there is no make-up upon you' narrated by al-Daraqutni, and the permissibility of the slaughtered animal with leaving out the tasmiya (likewise) i.e., forgetfully, established by his saying, peace be upon him: 'If he forgets to say the name when slaughtering, let him say the name and remember Allah, then eat' narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi as in al-Taysir, because the existence of a thing without its pillar or condition is unintelligible. And by eating forgetfully, the pillar of fasting is missed because it is abstention, and it has been missed. And in leaving out the tasmiya forgetfully, the condition of permissibility is missed because tasmiya is a condition by text. And in his saying: 'and it includes from it' is an indication of the weakness in it, for it is for someone to say: We do not accept that the pillar of fasting is abstention from eating absolutely, rather abstention from eating with remembrance, and similarly the condition of permissibility is not tasmiya absolutely, rather at the time of remembrance. Rather the verification is that both cases are ones in which the condition that follows is missed.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling: It states the first condition of analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The hukm of the asl (original case) must have an intelligible meaning (ma'qul al-ma'na), meaning its effective cause (illa) can be rationally perceived. Rulings that are purely devotional (ta'abbudi) or fixed by text without a perceptible cause—such as the specific numbers of rak'ats in prayer, the amounts of zakat, and, according to the Hanafis, fixed punishments (hudud)—cannot serve as asl for qiyas. The author then provides two hadith-based examples: (1) a person who eats forgetfully while fasting: the fast remains valid and no qada' is required; (2) a person who forgets to recite the tasmiya (Bismillah) while slaughtering: the slaughtered animal is halal. Both rulings are based on explicit prophetic texts, not on a rational cause. The author acknowledges a possible objection: perhaps fasting's true pillar is abstention with awareness, and tasmiya's condition is only when one remembers. The verification (tahqiq) is that in both cases, the relevant condition (remembrance) is missing, so the ruling is based on textual dispensation, not on an intelligible cause. Therefore, these rulings cannot be extended by qiyas.

Key Terms
معقول المعنى (ma'qul al-ma'na): A ruling whose effective cause (illa) can be rationally perceived and is not purely devotional.
غير معقول المعنى (ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na): A ruling whose 'illa is not perceptible; it is established solely by textual stipulation.
ركن (rukn): An essential component of an act; here, abstention (imsak) is said to be the pillar of fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first condition for the hukm of the asl in qiyas according to the passage?
A) It must be established by a mutawatir hadith.
B) It must have an intelligible meaning (ma'qul al-ma'na).
C) It must be from the Qur'an.
D) It must be a ruling from the fourth source.

Key Takeaway
The hukm of the asl in qiyas must be ma'qul al-ma'na; purely devotional rulings like numbers of rak'ats cannot be analogized.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
The Condition That the Hukm of the Asl Must Not Be Specific
Explaining the second condition of qiyas with the example of the man in Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a ruling is specific (mukhtass) and explain why such a ruling cannot serve as the basis for qiyas in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A ruling proven specific to its case by a dalil cannot be extended via qiyas—even if it has an apparent rational cause.

In qiyas, the ruling of the original case (asl) must be general in its application, not particular to that specific incident. This lesson explores the second condition: the hukm of the asl must not be mukhtass (specific). Using the famous hadith of the man who broke his fast in Ramadan, we examine how a ruling may appear general but is actually a concession (rukhsa) specific to that individual, and why Hanafi usul prevents analogizing from such a case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
State the second condition for qiyas: the hukm of the asl must not be specific (mukhtass) to its original context. If a proof indicates specificity, analogy is invalidated absolutely.
This is distinct from the condition that the hukm be based on an intelligible cause (ma'qul al-illa). Even if the cause is perceptible, specificity overrides.
2
Understand the evidence of specificity
Recognize that a dalil (here, the context of the hadith) can prove a ruling is particular. The Prophet's laughter and the man's unique situation are used as evidence that the permission to feed his family was a specific concession.
The dalil is not the text itself but the surrounding circumstances that indicate specificity.
3
Analyze the hadith example
Walk through the story: the man had intercourse in Ramadan, offered kaffara options, was unable, the Prophet gave him dates and told him to feed his own family. The majority (jumhur) see a general cause (filling need). Hanafis argue the ruling is specific due to the story's uniqueness.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim; the key phrase is 'Go and feed it to your family'.
4
Compare the two interpretations
Contrast the majority view (generalizable because the cause is filling need) with the Hanafi view (specific concession because feeding oneself is not obedience and the context indicates a pardon).
The author sides with the Hanafi view, citing Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if generalizable, a poor person could feed his own family as kaffara; according to Hanafis, he cannot because the ruling was a one-time concession.
This illustrates how ikhtilaf in usul affects fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن لا يكون مختصاً به أي بالمنصوص بدليل دل عليه : فإنه إذا كان مختصاً بطل الإلحاق به قطعاً كإطعام الأعرابي كفارته لأهله عن أبي هريرة قال: جاء رجل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم فقال: هلکت یا رسول الله قال وما أهلكك؟ قال : وقعت على أهلي في رمضان فقال: «هل تجد ما تعتق رقبة؟ قال : لا قال: «فهل تستطيع أن تصوم شهرين متتابعين؟ قال: لا، قال: «فهل تجد ما تطعم ستين مسكيناً ؟ قال : لا ، قال : ثم جلس فأتى النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم بعرق فيه تمر فقال : تصدق بهذا فقال : أعلى أفقر منا فما بين لا بتيها أهل بيت أحوج إليه منا، فضحك النبي صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم حتى بدت أنيابه ثم قال : اذهب فأطعمه أهلك ؟ رواه مسلم فهذا أي إطعام أهله طعام كفارته (على قول الجمهور) لا من قبيل أعداد الركعات فإنه معقول العلة لا كما في التحرير حيث أورده نظير الغير معقول العلة لأنه كأحد من الفقراء فسد خلته كسد خلة الفقير الآخر وهو العلة (لكن تفوت) به حكمة الزجر) على تقدير جواز إطعام الأهل فإنما ثبت رخصة خاصة به مختصة بقصته) فإنه أضحك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم فعفا الله عنه، ولذا قال الإمام جعفر ابن محمد الصادق كرم الله وجهه : لا تحقر الحسنة ولو شعرة فإنه عسى أن يكون رضا الله عنك فيه فلا يعمم) بالتعليل، ولا يبعد أن يقال ليس شرع الكفارة لسد خلة أي فقير كان، بل هو لستر ذنب بطاعة ولا طاعة في أكل نفسه، فإطعام نفسه وأهله في الكفارة غير معقول العلة فثبت ما في «التحرير» ولا ينافيه تمثيل الجمهور للاختصاص به فإن جزئياً واحداً يقع مثالاً لقواعد كثيرة فافهم
And among them is that it (the ruling of the asl) should not be specific to it, i.e., to the textually stipulated ruling, by a proof indicating that: for if it is specific, analogizing to it is invalidated absolutely, like feeding the Bedouin his own expiation to his family. From Abu Hurayra, he said: A man came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: I am ruined, O Messenger of Allah. He said: What has ruined you? He said: I had intercourse with my wife in Ramadan. He said: Do you find a slave to free? He said: No. He said: Can you fast two consecutive months? He said: No. He said: Can you find to feed sixty poor people? He said: No. He said: Then he sat, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, came with a basket containing dates and said: Give charity with this. He said: To one poorer than us? There is no household between the two lava fields more needy than us. The Prophet, peace be upon him, laughed until his molars appeared, then said: Go and feed it to your family. Reported by Muslim. So this, i.e., feeding his family his expiation food (according to the majority), is not from the category of numbers of rak'ats, for it has an intelligible cause, not as in al-Tahrir where he presented it as an analogue of that which has no intelligible cause, because like one of the poor, his need is filled like the filling of the need of the other poor, which is the cause. (But it misses) the wisdom of deterrence. On the assumption of the permissibility of feeding the family, it is only established as a specific concession specific to his story, for he made the Messenger of Allah laugh, and Allah pardoned him. Therefore Imam Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, may Allah honor his face, said: Do not belittle a good deed even if it is a hair, for perhaps it is Allah's pleasure with you. So it is not generalized by legal reasoning. And it is not far to say: The legislation of expiation is not to fill the need of any poor person, but rather to cover a sin by an act of obedience, and there is no obedience in feeding oneself. So feeding himself and his family in expiation is not of intelligible cause. Thus that which is in al-Tahrir is established, and the example of the majority for specificity does not contradict it, for a single particular serves as an example for many rules, so understand.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling: It explains the second condition for the hukm of the asl in qiyas: the ruling must not be specific (mukhtass) to the original case. If it is proven to be specific by a dalil, then analogy is invalid. The author provides the famous hadith of the man who had intercourse in Ramadan (from Sahih Muslim). After offering the various kaffara options, the man was too poor to do any, so the Prophet gave him a basket of dates and ordered him to feed his own family. The majority view is that this feeding of family is not like the numbers of rak'ats (which are non-intelligible), for it does have an intelligible cause (filling need). However, the author counters that this ruling is a specific concession (rukhsa) for that particular man because he made the Prophet laugh, and it was a pardon. Thus it cannot be analogized to other cases. The author supports this with the saying of Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq and concludes that feeding oneself in expiation is not an act of obedience, so the cause is not rational. The text in al-Tahrir is correct in treating it as specific, and the fact that the majority used it as an example for specificity does not contradict, because one particular can illustrate many rules.

Key Terms
مختص (mukhtass): A ruling that is particular to a specific person or situation, not intended for general application in qiyas.
رخصة (rukhsa): A concession granted due to a special circumstance, not a general rule.
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for breaking a fast by intercourse; here it is food for sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the ruling in the hadith of the man in Ramadan not suitable for qiyas according to the Hanafi position in this passage?
A) Because it has no rational cause.
B) Because it is specific to that man and his story.
C) Because it contradicts the Qur'an.
D) Because it is from an unreliable narrator.

Key Takeaway
The hukm of the asl must not be specific; if proven specific by a dalil, qiyas is invalid — even if the ruling has an apparent cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Specific Rulings Cannot Be Extended by Qiyas – Examples of Khuzayma and the Traveler
Illustration of mukhtass rulings with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ruling as specific (mukhtass) and explain why it cannot serve as an asl for qiyas.

Core Idea
A ruling with an intelligible cause is not always extensible — contextual specificity can block qiyas.

In usul al-fiqh, a ruling established for a specific person or situation cannot be analogized to others, even if the cause appears similar. This lesson examines two classic Hanafi examples: the testimony of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, whose single testimony was accepted by the Prophet ﷺ, and the travel concessions. Both are specific to their contexts and cannot be extended via qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its specificity
Find the exact hukm (ruling) and note the person or situation it applies to exclusively.
Khuzayma's single testimony suffices; traveler may shorten prayers.
2
Examine the apparent cause
What seems to be the illa (cause)? For Khuzayma, it is his perfect religiosity and memory; for travel, hardship.
Both causes are 'ma'qul' (intelligible).
3
Evaluate why qiyas is blocked
The Shari'ah explicitly limited the ruling to that specific case, often through contextual evidence (qarina) or explicit statement.
The Prophet said 'من شهد له خزيمة' (for whom Khuzayma witnesses), not 'every just person'.
4
Compare with similar but distinct cases
Why does the same cause not apply to others? For travel, heavy labor is more arduous but not granted concession because the ruling is specific to travel.
The specificity prevents qiyas even though the cause exists elsewhere.

And from it is the testimony of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, for he is like the testimony of two by text, and thus he was nicknamed among the Companions as 'the one with two testimonies'. He was a noble Companion martyred at Siffin with the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali after the martyrdom of 'Ammar. When 'Ammar was martyred, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'The rebellious group will kill you.' So he took his sword and fought until he was killed. As in al-Isti'ab. And his story, as in the books of usul, is that the Messenger of Allah bought a she-camel from a Bedouin and paid him its price. Then the Bedouin denied receiving it and kept saying: Bring a witness. So he, peace be upon him, said: 'Who will witness for me?' Khuzayma ibn Thabit said: I bear witness for you, O Messenger of Allah, that you paid the Bedouin the price of the she-camel. He said: 'How do you witness for me when you were not present?' He said: O Messenger of Allah, I believe you concerning what you bring from heaven; should I not believe you concerning what you say about paying the price of the she-camel? So the Messenger of Allah said: 'For whomsoever Khuzayma bears witness, it is sufficient.' A karamah was established specific to him, due to his understanding of the validity of testimony for him about his reports. No one else understood this, so no one like him or above him, such as the Rightly Guided Caliphs, may Allah be pleased with them, can be analogized to him. This is what Imam Fakhr al-Islam intended by his saying, but it is established as a karamah for him, so its invalidation is not correct. And he did not intend that the karamah does not extend to others, else it would be objected that it is contrary to reality, for two persons may share a single karamah. Then it may be discussed that specificity is not proven from his saying 'For whomsoever Khuzayma bears witness...' It would only follow if there were a concept of the title, and the reasoning by understanding the validity of testimony does not indicate specificity; rather it is permissible for every Muslim to understand it. The truth is that this is argumentation; the context indicates specificity. And the validity of testimony in worldly matters by his report does not depend on faith; rather it appears that with them testimony was by actual observation, so understand. And the well-known view is that it is taken out from the general rule, so it is like an exception from it, and analogizing others to him is not permissible. It was objected that reasoning for specification is permissible, so just as his specification is permissible, specification of one of his level or above is permissible by reasoning. The truth is that this is not specification due to lack of contiguity, but rather an abrogation of a general rule, and the abrogator cannot be diminished. And if it is accepted that it is specification, then its generalization to other than this specific matter was limited to the Companions until now, so understand. And you know that relying on him is intelligible in testimony (due to perfection of religiosity) and memory, and similarly taking him out from the general rule of absolutely requiring the number in testimonies (due to his specific understanding) of matters as they are, just as the testimony of the midwife is accepted to avert hardship, for men do not witness childbirth, and non-midwife women rarely witness. So acceptance of his testimony is not unintelligible, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, so reflect. And from it is the concession for the traveler, for the conceding cause is hardship, but it is not considered in others even if they have hardship greater, like heavy labor. So when it is not considered in others, the ruling is specific to him. And from it is...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling: It provides two additional examples of rulings that are specific (mukhtass) and therefore not valid as asl for qiyas. The first is the testimony of the Companion Khuzayma ibn Thabit (nicknamed 'Dhu al-Shahadatayn'), whose single testimony was considered equivalent to two witnesses by a specific hadith. This was a karamah (divine honor) for him due to his deep faith and understanding. The author discusses various points: whether this specificity can be extended to others like the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The well-known view is that it is an exception from the general rule of requiring two witnesses, and thus cannot be analogized. The author refutes objections: the specificity is proven by context, and it is not a mere specification (takhsis) but a kind of abrogation (naskh) of the general rule, or at least a specific dispensation. The reason for accepting his single testimony is regarded as 'ma'qul' (intelligible) because of his religiosity and memory, similar to accepting the testimony of a midwife to avoid hardship. The second example is the concession (rukhsa) for a traveler, which is based on hardship (mashaqqa). However, this same hardship is not considered for heavy laborers, so the ruling is specific to travel. This shows that even when a cause appears common, if the Shari'ah restricts it to a specific case, it cannot be analogized to other cases with similar causes.

Key Terms
كرامة (karamah): A divine honor or miracle granted to a saintly person; here used for Khuzayma's testimony being accepted as sufficient.
شهادة القابلة (shahadat al-qabila): The testimony of a midwife regarding childbirth, accepted by some to avoid hardship.
ترخص المسافر (tarakhkhus al-musafir): The concession (rukhsa) granted to a traveler, such as shortening prayers or breaking fast, due to hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because heavy laborers are not mentioned in the Qur'an.
D) Because hardship is not the actual cause.

Key Takeaway
A ruling that is contextually specific to a person or situation cannot be used as an asl for qiyas, even if the cause appears similar.

Conditions of the Original in Qiyas: Non-Abrogated and Shari
Stating two conditions for the original (asl) in qiyas: it must not be abrogated and must be a shari ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the original (asl) in qiyas and explain why original negation cannot serve as an original.

Core Idea
The original in qiyas must be a non-abrogated shari ruling; original negation is invalid because it is not shari.

Qiyas extends a ruling from an original to a branch. But not every ruling can be an original. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut establishes two conditions: the original's ruling must be shari and not abrogated. Understanding these conditions prevents flawed analogies, such as comparing a supervening absence of a ruling to an original absence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and list the two explicit conditions for the original in qiyas: (1) the original must not be abrogated, and (2) the ruling must be shari.
2
Understand the rationale for non-abrogation
The passage states that the ruling exists to achieve wisdom (hikma); abrogation means that wisdom is no longer considered, so the causal entailment between the 'illa and the ruling disappears.
Link to naskh: abrogation nullifies the original's validity for qiyas.
3
Understand why the original must be shari
Qiyas in usul al-fiqh aims to prove shari rulings. Therefore, the original must itself be a shari ruling. The passage notes that this condition is not automatic but accepted in the context of shari qiyas.
This excludes rational or linguistic analogies from the scope.
4
Apply to original negation
The passage gives the example of original negation (al-nafi al-asli) – the state of no ruling before revelation. This is not a shari ruling, so it cannot be an original. Additionally, there is another obstacle: lack of unity of the ratio legis (ittihad al-manat) between original and branch.
Even if it were shari, the manat would not be unified.
5
Synthesize the conditions
Combine the two conditions to evaluate any proposed original. Check: (1) Is the ruling still in effect? (2) Is it a shari ruling? If either fails, qiyas is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومنها) أي من شروط الأصل أن لا يكون منسوخاً، لأن الحكم لتحصيل الحكمة وقد زال اعتبارها بانتساخ الحكم فلم يبق الاستلزام) أي استلزام العلة للحكم (وقد تقدم في باب النسخ ومنها أن يكون حكم الأصل حكماً شرعياً ، لأن المطلوب) في القياس إثبات حكم الشرع هذه الحجة إنما تدل على أن القياس المبحوث ههنا هو الذي في الشرعيات، ولا يلزم منه اشتراط كون الأصل حكماً شرعياً إلا إذا ادعى أن المطلوب في جميع الأقيسة هو الحكم الشرعي، وهذه الدعوى كما ترى غير مبنية ببيان أصلا (ومن ههنا قالوا : النفي الأصلي لا يقاس عليه النفي الطارىء) لأن النفي الأصلي ليس حكماً شرعياً، ثم إن امتناع القياس على النفي الأصلي غير متوقف على هذا بل فيه مانع آخر وهو عدم اتحاد المناط
(Among them) i.e., among the conditions of the original: that it not be abrogated, because the ruling is for the achievement of wisdom, and its consideration has ceased with the abrogation of the ruling, so the entailment remains no more—i.e., the entailment of the cause for the ruling (and it has preceded in the chapter on abrogation). And among them: that the ruling of the original be a shari ruling, because what is sought in qiyas is establishing a ruling of the sharia. This proof only indicates that the qiyas under discussion here is that which is in shar'i matters, and it does not necessitate the condition that the original be a shari ruling unless one claims that what is sought in all analogies is the shari ruling, and this claim, as you see, is not based on any explanation at all. (And from here they said: original negation cannot be analogically extended to supervening negation) because original negation is not a shari ruling. Then, the impossibility of qiyas on original negation is not dependent on this, but rather there is another obstacle: lack of unity of the ratio legis.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage explains two conditions for the original (asl) in qiyas. First, the ruling of the original must not be abrogated (mansukh), because the reason for the ruling was to achieve a certain wisdom (hikma); once the ruling is abrogated, that wisdom is no longer considered, so the causal entailment between the 'illa and the ruling disappears. Second, the ruling of the original must be a shari' (legal) ruling, because qiyas in this usul discussion pertains to deriving Islamic legal rulings. The author notes that this condition is not automatically required unless we limit qiyas to the sharia; but in practice, qiyas in non-shar'i matters (like rational) is debated elsewhere. A corollary is that original negation (al-nafi al-asli, e.g., the original absence of a ruling) cannot serve as an original in qiyas for a supervening negation (al-nafi al-tari'), because original negation is not a shari ruling. Moreover, even if it were, there is another obstacle: the ratio legis (manat) cannot be unified between the original and the branch in such a case.

Key Terms
النفي الأصلي (al-nafi al-asli): An original absence or negation of a ruling that has never been legislatively established (e.g., no ruling on an issue before revelation).
اتحاد المناط (ittihad al-manat): Unity of the ratio legis (manat) between original and branch, a condition for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why can't original negation (al-nafi al-asli) be used as the original in qiyas?
A) Because it is abrogated.
B) Because it is not a shar'i ruling.
C) Because it lacks a cause ('illa).
D) Because it is unknown.

Key Takeaway
The original in qiyas must be a non-abrogated shari ruling; original negation is invalid because it is not shari and lacks union of manat.
